The Four Gods Of Hali

    Chapter One

	Halimah Samra fiddled with her braid as she sat in class. She stifled a yawn. It was another hot afternoon, and she found her attention straying from the day's lecture. The soft glow of magic floated around the classroom as her classmates attempted to mimic their professor's spell.
	Halimah really did yawn this time, and during the brief moment when her eyes closed, something hit her on the back of the head. Halimah's eyes snapped open as she whirled around to look behind her. A boy with green hair was watching her from a few rows down. He looked at Halimah expectantly as he motioned to the ball of paper that had fallen beneath Halimah's seat.
	Halimah just gave him an exasperated look as she quickly leaned over to snatch up the paper. After making sure the professor's eyes weren't on her, Halimah unfolded it. Bang! There was an explosion as the paper in her hands was shredded into pieces by a mini cyclone. Halimah threw her arms in front of her face as bits of paper shot in every direction.
	Halimah swiveled around to glare at the green-haired boy. He just smirked back.
	"Halimah Samra." A voice sounded from the front of the classroom. "What do you have to say for yourself?"
      Halimah slowly turned back around to face her stone-faced professor and winced as she rose to her feet. "I messed up, sir," she said as she lowered her gaze to her desk. "My focus wasn't on your lesson. Ewen distracted me, sir."
	"Ewen? What does Mr. Hanif have to do with your incompetence?"
	"I didn't mean to disrupt the class, sir," Halimah continued. "I just noticed that Ewen had a number of enchanted papers and I was worried he would try and do something foolish with them."
	The professor turned to address the green-haired boy. "Mr. Hanif, is this true?"
	"Sir," Ewen said. There was a shuffling as he quickly stood up as well. "Halimah is trying to move the blame onto me. I don't have any enchanted papers."
	But as he was speaking, Halimah absently waved a hand behind her back. A moment later, there was a loud bang as paper exploded from the rows behind her.
	"Mr. Hanif," the professor said angrily, "you just lied to your professor! You said you didn't have any enchanted papers. You've earned yourself detention! I'll be seeing you after class."
	Halimah smiled to herself as she sat back down and folded her hands on her lap. This wasn't the first time Ewen had tried to get her in trouble; the two of them were constantly at each other's throats as they fought for the position of top of the class.
	The first time Ewen tried to sabotage her this week had been a couple of days ago during their history class. Halimah had been landed an entire week of after-school detention because of it. She had let it slide that time, but she wouldn't let Ewen get his way twice in one week.
	When the chiming bells signaled the end of class, Halimah packed away her books and marched out the door. She was positive Ewen was scowling at her retreating figure, but she didn't look back.
	Halimah's classmates waved to her as she walked through the gradually emptying hallways of the academy, and she greeted them back. All of them knew her name and associated it with the girl who was always in detention. But even though she was constantly in detention, they still held to some degree of respect. It was a fact that Halimah had made it onto the academy's list of top twenty mages. So had Ewen, though, much to Halimah's annoyance.
	Halimah flipped her braid over her shoulder as she made her way outside. As she passed through the courtyard, Halimah squinted through the brilliance of the sun. No matter how bright the sun was, she could always see the two moons in the sky.
	When Halimah reached the opposite side of the courtyard, the school grounds had considerably cleared out. Everyone had either gone home or to their dormitories. But not Halimah-she still had detention to serve. Halimah lingered outside the door to her history classroom for a moment. Just as she reached out to turn the handle, the door swung open of its own accord. "Miss Samra," a voice greeted her.
	Halimah let out a sigh as she stepped inside. "Professor Lethco." The rows of desks in the classroom were empty, and Halimah made her way over to one of them before setting her book bag down on the bench next to her.
	There was a flash of movement as a gray cat gracefully leaped onto the table in front of her. "This is your third day here," the cat said crossly. "I'm sure I don't need to tell you what you need to be doing."
	"No, sir." Halimah made her way over to the corner of the classroom and picked up the wooden bucket waiting for her. This she carried out of the classroom and down the hall. After she filled it up with soapy water, Halimah returned to Professor Lethco's classroom. And as she got to work wiping down the tables, Professor Lethco began talking to her.
	"While I was looking through books about the great war to create my lesson plan," the cat said, "I was suddenly reminded of something."
	"What were you reminded about?" Halimah asked when it became obvious that her professor wanted her to converse.
	"The winged folk," Professor Lethco said simply.
	Halimah's hand stilled for a moment from where she was cleaning the tables. "The winged folk," she echoed as she swiftly resumed her task. "Let me guess-were you reminded of the time the king of the day angels declared war on the night angels and all of Hali? Even though I was just a baby during the war, you and the other professors all lived through those times. Or were you thinking about how the gods were reduced to mortals when they gave up their immortality to stop him?"
	"Neither, actually. I suddenly remembered how during the war, a rumor was spread that the wing-folk could link their consciousness with a human of Hali and communicate with them during their unconscious state."
	Halimah's hand stilled again. But just as her head snapped up to look at the cat, the door to the classroom was thrown open. "Ewen!" Halimah exclaimed angrily as her gaze flew to the door.
	"Professor Badat sent me here to pick up papers," Ewen said sourly.
	"Papers?" Professor Lethco asked mildly. "Oh, yes. That's right." There was a flash of plum-colored smoke, and Ewen had to hastily throw out his arms to catch the stack of papers that suddenly materialized. With a glare over his shoulder at Halimah, Ewen turned and marched out of the room.
	Once Ewen was gone, Halimah waited for Professor Lethco to resume his conversation. But much to her dismay, he began rambling about his other classes and lesson plans. "Sir," Halimah finally said when her curiosity got the better of her, "about the winged folk-"
	"Will you look at the time!" The cat cut her off. "You should run along now, Miss Samra."
	Halimah exhaled through her nose as she dropped her rag back into the bucket. "Yessir."
	That night, Halimah lay awake in her dormitory room. She silently cursed Ewen as she stared up at the ceiling. Her history professor had been about to tell her something important. She hadn't known the winged folk could communicate with humans. When she had first seen the woman with the violet wings in her dreams, she thought she was going crazy.
	Halimah tried her best to clear her mind as she squeezed her eyes shut. She'd see Professor Lethco again tomorrow during her detention.
	In her dreams, Halimah was floating in a void. Everything was pitch black. But as she looked on, a single star flickered to life. And then another, and another, and another. The entire void slowly filled with an array of twinkling lights, and standing with her back to her as a woman with violet feathered wings.
	Before Halimah could call out to her, the winged woman turned her head to look back at Halimah. Halimah's words seemed to escape her, but before she could find her voice again, she had awakened to the sun spilling in through the window of her room.
      
~

	"Professor Lethco?" Halimah called as she knocked on the door to her history professor's classroom. She had tried the handle a moment ago but found that the door was locked.
	"Haven't you heard?" an unpleasant voice sounded from behind her. "Professor Lethco left right when the final bell chimed."
	Halimah didn't even need to turn around to know Ewen was standing behind her. She frowned as she turned around to face him. "What do you want this time? Are you following me?"
	Ewen gave Halimah a look. "If I could have it my way, I'd stay as far away from you as possible. I'm only here to collect you because Professor Lethco left. You're going to be serving detention in Professor Badat's classroom with me."
	"Detention? With you?"
	"You landed me a week in detention, don't you remember?"
	"Oh, that's right. I nearly forgot."
	Halimah spent the entire hour of detention ignoring Ewen, and Ewen spent the entire hour ignoring her. When she could finally head back to her dormitory, Halimah walked as quickly as she could. It was the weekend now and she'd have to wait until next week to find Professor Lethco.
	When Halimah finally fell asleep after a long night of studying in the shared common room, she opened her eyes to find that she was floating.
      Back in the void of stars, Halimah anticipated the winged woman's arrival. This time as she waited, Halimah examined her surroundings. Her thick hair billowed around her as she turned her head. She could see the galaxy. And the moon. And the second one.
      "Hello," a feminine voice purred. Halimah twisted around to find the woman with the long flaming hair and violet wings floating a good distance away.
      "Hello," Halimah breathed.
      
~

	"Professor Lethco!" Halimah called as she skidded into the classroom. The moment the bell chimed, signifying the start of their passing period, Halimah sprinted through the grassy courtyard to reach her history class. She looked around the classroom. She had made it before most of the other students. "Professor Lethco?" Halimah said again as she scanned the room for the cat.
	"Miss Samra." Halimah looked down to see the gray cat seated calmly on the floor. "It's the start of a new week. Don't tell me that I need to give you detention for yelling in the classroom and running in the halls."
	Halimah blinked at the cat. "Professor, I want to ask you something."
	"I'm about to start class," Professor Lethco said distractedly. "Can it wait for later?"
	Halimah reluctantly nodded her head. But even as her professor started the class, she got the feeling that once the bell chimed, the cat would dismiss her again. Making up her mind, Halimah shot to her feet.
	"Miss Samra?" Professor Lethco looked at her in surprise from the front of the classroom. Halimah could feel the eyes of her classmates on the back of her head.
	"Professor!" Halimah said loudly, "I have a confession to make!" Professor Lethco stared at her, stunned as Halimah continued, "I was the one who enchanted Ewen's papers. I was the one who put him in detention."
	"Do you take my class as a joke?" the cat asked irritatedly. "Detention, Miss Samra. I'll be seeing you here after school."
	Halimah did her best to hide her smile as she sat back down.
	After school, Halimah returned to her history classroom. "Professor Lethco," Halimah said as she hurried over to the cat, "please, what do you know about the winged folk and how they communicate?"
	Professor Lethco turned to face Halimah from where he was magically cleaning the blackboard with flashes of purple smoke. "Miss Samra, tell me, why are you suddenly so interested in the winged folk? Even primary school students know that they haven't come down to Hali since the gods put a stop to the war."
	"I think I've been seeing one of them in my dreams," Halimah said quietly. "And I'm not a person who dreams often. It must be a dream-but each time just seems so real."
	Professor Lethco just looked at Halimah for a long moment. "Are you sure you're contacting one of the winged folk in your unconscious state? Are they a night angel or day angel?"
	"A night angel."
	Professor Lethco fell silent at that. Finally, he closed his eyes for a brief moment as he seemed to gather his thoughts. "Miss Samra, if you wish to find the answers you seek, I recommend you take a walk down to the Temple of Life."
	"The Temple of Life? But even since the goddess herself passed away, her temple has been abandoned."
	"I never said you had to enter the temple. I only said that you should take a walk to it. But I'll have to warn you, if you really are communicating with a night angel, you could end up in danger."
	"Danger?" Halimah's voice wavered. "Is it really that serious? I-maybe it was nothing more than a dream after all."
	"I'll warn you to think carefully about your next move," Professor Lethco said seriously. "Only a wielder of soul magic can be contacted by a night angel."
	"A wielder of soul . . . But a wielder of soul can only appear if a god has a child with a mortal! No." Halimah shook her head as she took a step back from the cat. "My parents both passed away when I was younger, but they were ordinary people! They never went to the academy-they only knew basic magic! I knew my mother. I won't believe she was the goddess of life. Besides, I can't be a wielder of soul-I practice air magic! See?" Halimah desperately held out a hand, and rosy pink light flickered to life in the air around her. "My magic is pink, not silver-white."
	"If you want the answers you seek," Professor Lethco repeated, "take a walk down to the Temple of Life. If you truly are a wielder of soul magic, it's my responsibility to take you to one of the former gods. They will teach you how to control your magic."
	"And what if I'm not?"
	"Then you return to the academy after your little walk and continue your schooling. At least then you can rest assured that it was only a dream and that you're the daughter of an ordinary couple after all."
	Halimah spent the rest of her detention cleaning the tables in silence. The Temple of Life was located on the beach not more than an hour's walk from the academy. Halimah let her gaze linger on the tall grassy fields waving in the wind outside. She couldn't see the beach from here, but she knew it was out there. Could it be calling to her?

~
      
      Halimah was floating in the void.
      "Hello," a voice purred.
      Halimah twisted around in the air to find the female night angel drifting along beside her. "Are you real?" Halimah asked desperately. "Or are you a dream?"
      "Am I real?" The woman's lips flicked into an amused smile. "Do you want me to be?"
      Halimah opened her mouth, but then closed it again when no sound came out.
      The woman just gave her a knowing smirk.
      
~

	In the morning, Halimah had made up her mind. After tying back her thick hair and marching downstairs to the students' shared cafeteria, Halimah finished her breakfast as quickly as she could. If she wanted to go to the beach, she needed to be long on her way by the time class started in case any of the school staff went looking for her. Halimah was so preoccupied that she didn't even bother replying to the sarcastic comments Ewen shot in her direction when he passed by.
	Before long, Halimah was off on her way. She left the cafeteria early enough that there weren't any other students around to witness her stray from the path to the academic buildings. She quickened her pace as she hurried through the tall grass. Halimah was still in denial. Soul magic was one of the strongest types of magic; it was something so pure that it could extinguish any evil. Her magic wasn't like that at all.
	Halimah wasn't a horrible magic wielder-she had made it onto the list of top twenty students for a reason. A smug smile flickered across her face. She had placed seventeenth according to the results of last year's end-of-year test. Ewen had come in one place behind her at eighteen. But the two of them were always neck in neck, and in previous years, Ewen had always placed above her on the exam. There was still one year left until they both graduated, though, and Halimah was determined to get the last laugh.
	As the tall grass finally gave way to the powdery beach, Halimah hesitated as the ocean glittered in front of her. The beach was calm, and the water was clear and sparkling. What was she doing skipping class? This wasn't like her at all. But the night angel in her dreams . . . It had started nearly three months ago, and she couldn't go on this way anymore.
	Halimah determinedly made her way down the long stretch of beach. She could see the Temple of Life in the distance, and it grew steadily closer with each step. But then all of a sudden, Halimah pivoted. It was like her feet were moving on their own as she began to walk toward the water. Halimah's panic began to overtake her as she tried to regain control of her legs.
	Halimah fought with all her strength against the force pulling her toward the ocean. But even as her magic sparked in a rosy-pink glow around her, she couldn't break free. Halimah's heart began to beat faster as her shoe touched the lazy water lapping up against the sand. Before she could blink, she was up to her knees in the cool water. Her school uniform felt heavy as it became waterlogged.
	Halimah tried to scream-to call out for help-but her mouth wasn't working either. All she could do was continue to descend into the water. Halimah's heart sank as she found herself up to her neck. There hadn't been anyone on the beach or in the fields when she had come here. Halimah squeezed her eyes shut as her head went under.
	Even as the water began to flood her lungs, Halimah's feet continued to lead her deeper into the ocean. Halimah could feel her mind straining as she tried to gather her magic. Rosy-pink light flared through the water. Halimah screamed, and the trail of bubbles that spewed from her mouth nearly shocked her into silence. She could move her mouth again. There was no point in it now, though. She felt lightheaded.
      Just as Halimah's eyes fluttered close, silver light erupted around her. Her eyes snapped open. After getting over her momentary shock, she frantically squinted through the brightness for its caster. Had someone come to save her? No, Halimah realized with a jolt. The silver light was coming from her.
      The feeling had returned to her limbs, and Halimah shot to the surface of the water. Her dark hair was plastered to the sides of her face as she gasped for breath. But she was breathing too quickly. All Halimah could do was look hopelessly up at the clear sky as her heavy clothes pulled her back under the surface.

~

	Everything felt foggy. As Halimah drifted in and out of consciousness, she felt the warmth of the sun beating down on her from above. She could feel the sand of the beach at her fingertips. Halimah's eyes felt heavy, but even as she lay there, she could feel a pressure on her chest. A moment later someone pinched her nose, and then there was light pressure on her mouth.
	Halimah fought through the fog as she forced herself to open her eyes. Green filled her vision, and she had to blink a couple of times to make sure she was awake. "Ewen?" Halimah choked out.
	"You're awake!" Ewen exclaimed breathlessly as he sat back on his heels.
	Halimah just stared up at him.
	"What?" Ewen's expression changed from relief to annoyance in a matter of seconds. "If I didn't give you air, you wouldn't have woken up at all."
	Halimah shook her head as she slowly sat up. "What happened? Why are you here?"
	"I followed you," Ewen admitted unapologetically as he rose to his feet. He made no move to help Halimah to hers, and Halimah remained sitting on the sand. "You were too suspicious this morning. I thought I might be able to catch you trying to find some illegal method to help you cheat on the final exam. What were you doing in the ocean? Even if you're my rival, you're also my classmate. I can't just let you throw away your life like that."
	"I-" Halimah said, at a loss for words, "thank you."
	"You should use your magic to dry your clothes. If you show up to class the way you are now, you'll be stuck in detention for an entire month. Nothing I do will be able to get you into more trouble then."
	Halimah just sighed as she climbed to her feet. She summoned her magic, but instead of the rosy-pink color she expected, the light that surrounded her was silver.
	Ewen whirled around from where he had started back up the sandy beach to stare at her in disbelief. "Halimah, is that . . . soul magic?"

    Chapter Two

	Halimah stared in shock at the silver light radiating from her. "I-but I'm not a wielder of soul!"
	"It looks like you are now," Ewen said weakly. "Halimah, are you the daughter of one of the gods?"
	Halimah rapidly shook her head, and the silver light faded. Her clothes were still soaked through and she began to panic. Her magic wasn't working. "I need to go find Professor Lethco!" With that said, she took off at a sprint down the beach. Sand flew in her wake as she reached the fields of golden grass.
	"Wait!" Ewen called after her. "Class is in session! You can't just bust into his classroom."
	"We're both in trouble now for ditching. We're going to end up in detention either way!"
	"I just saved your life! And this is how you thank me? With detention?"
	Halimah slowed her pace. Even if she did burst into Professor Lethco's classroom, he wouldn't talk to her until school was out for the day. "I'm going back to my other class," she said shortly. "You should go to your classes as well."
	Ewen nodded curtly as he fell into pace with her. There was a flash of green light, and then Halimah's clothes were dry again.
	"Thank you," Halimah said softly. Ewen just nodded again, and the two of them walked the rest of the way through the tall grass in silence.
	Halimah was especially absentminded during her lessons for the remainder of the day. And now that her magic had changed . . . She couldn't just use it in front of her classmates.
	"Halimah Samra!" Her professor slammed her fist down on her desk. Halimah blinked back to reality at the sound. "If you think you can daydream through my lessons, how about we have you demonstrate how to use air magic to grow and shape fires."
	Halimah just stared at the candle that had appeared on the table in front of her in a puff of smoke.
	"Please, go ahead," her professor said silkily.
	"I-"
	"Halimah isn't feeling well," Ewen interrupted as he stood up from his seat on the far side of the classroom. "I spent the morning trying to convince her to go see the nurse, but she was stubborn and ended up coming to school anyway. Please let her go to the infirmary."
	Halimah stared at Ewen as she tried not to let her surprise show on her face. Ewen just gave her a look that read, Are you going to take my help or not?
	"Is it true, Miss Samra?" Halimah's professor asked.
	Halimah dipped her head in a nod. "Yes, it's true that I haven't been feeling well today."
	"If it's really that serious, I shouldn't keep you from seeing the nurse. Off you go."
	Halimah quickly shoved her books into her bag before scurrying out of the classroom. But instead of heading in the direction of the infirmary, Halimah walked toward Professor Lethco's classroom. Even though she had been practicing magic for years, the new magic now flowing through her veins felt so foreign. She had no idea how to control it-no idea how to wield it. She was in some of the highest magic classes at the school. Shaping magic was difficult enough as it was, but now that Halimah was completely out of touch with her magic, there was no way she'd be able to continue the year like this. Professor Lethco said that if Halimah really was a wielder of soul, he would take her to the former gods. Only they would know how to help her train and wield her new power.
	When Halimah reached the door to Professor Lethco's classroom, she hesitated for a moment before pushing it open. She could feel the eyes of the students in the classroom fall on her as she searched for her history professor.
	"Miss Samra?" Professor Lethco asked from the front of the classroom.
	"Professor Lethco," Halimah said quietly, "may I have a word? It's urgent."
	Professor Lethco let out a sigh as he turned back to address his students. "Continue reading pages eighty through ninety. I'll be back after I speak with Miss Samra."
	The door swung shut behind Professor Lethco as the cat joined Halimah in the walkway. Halimah glanced at the empty courtyard through the large stone arches that made up the walkway, before finally turning to face the cat. "I walked down to the Temple of Life. I-my magic is silver now."
	Professor Lethco inhaled sharply. "Does anyone else know about your magic?"
	"Only Ewen," Halimah said quickly. "No one else knows."
	"You know where my office is, correct?"
	"Yes, sir."
	"Wait for me in my office. I need to collect Mr. Hanif."
	Before Halimah could ask any more questions, the cat hurried off down the sunny walkway. Halimah just blinked after him for a long moment before turning and making her way to the professor's office.
	As Halimah waited around inside, time seemed to drag by. She paced back and forth, pausing every once in a while to glance out the window at the swaying fields beyond. After what felt like an eternity, there was the sound of footsteps, and Halimah turned to watch as Ewen entered the room.
	When Ewen saw her, he just folded his arms over his chest and looked in the opposite direction.
	Halimah let out a sigh. "Ewen . . . Thank you for earlier."
	"Which part? The one where I saved your life? Or the one where I kept your new magic from being revealed to everyone?"
	"Both. I know the two of us haven't exactly gotten along very well all these years, but I have the feeling that I'll be leaving the academy very soon."
	"You're leaving?" Ewen asked almost eagerly as he turned to look at Halimah.
	Halimah frowned as she nodded her head. "Did Professor Lethco tell you anything?"
	"He told me to wait here in his office. When he finishes teaching his class, he'll come and talk to us."
	Halimah walked over to stand in front of the window. After another long stretch of time, the door creaked open and Professor Lethco entered the office. "Miss Samra, Mr. Hanif, I'll ask the two of you to follow me."
	Halimah exchanged a glance with Ewen as their professor turned and left the room. Halimah briskly exited the classroom and followed the cat down the open walkways. She could see Ewen out of the corner of her eye as he trailed after them. Halimah began to feel more confused as Professor Lethco led them off the school grounds and into the grassy fields surrounding it.
	"Professor-" Halimah started, but Professor Lethco cut her off.
	"Patience, Miss Samra. You don't know who could be listening in on our conversation."
	Halimah fell silent.
      Eventually, the three of them arrived at a small town. They came to a stop in front of one of the houses, and the door swung open for them on its own accord. Once they all entered, the door closed with a click.
	"Professor," Ewen started as he looked around the living room they were now standing in, "is this your house?"
	"That is correct, Mr. Hanif. The two of you will rest here tonight and prepare for our journey to see the former gods."
	"See the former gods?" Halimah asked in disbelief. "You're taking me to them after all?"
	"You are a wielder of soul, Miss Samra," Professor Lethco said heavily. "I'm sure you understand what it means to possess soul magic: you can have the potential to become a protector of our great Hali. Now that the gods have been reduced to mortals, they've all been looking for young talents to take over as protectors of Hali."
	"Professor," Ewen cut in, "why do I have to go? I won't be any use to the former gods. I still have to complete my last year at the academy."
	Professor Lethco let out a sigh. "Mr. Hanif, I'm afraid you can't go back now either. After all, you know about Miss Samra's new powers."
	"I swear I won't tell anyone-"
	"What if someone comes to the academy demanding the whereabouts of the wielder of soul?" Professor Lethco looked at Ewen seriously. "If they threaten you, I'm sure you will talk."
	"Is it likely that someone will come to the academy?" Halimah asked weakly.
	"Follow me," Professor Lethco said instead. He lead Halimah and Ewen over to the dining room table. After they had both taken a seat, the professor continued, "Not many people know this, but about three months ago, the former god of fire, Thuc, vanished."
      Three months ago . . . "But that's when the night angel first appeared in my dreams!" Halimah said quickly.
      "According to the letter I received from Gwenevieve, someone snuck into the Temple of Fire in the middle of the night. Nearby townsfolk reported that there seemed to be the sounds of fighting. A few people went to investigate after the sounds stopped, but when they entered the temple, there was no one there. Thuc and his partner had vanished. We fear they might have been abducted."
      "Gwenevieve?" Halimah just stared at her professor. "As in the former goddess of the sea, Gwenevieve?"
      Professor Lethco just nodded distractedly.
      "How do you know the former goddess of the sea?" Ewen asked the cat in equal shock. "And how did we not know that Thuc and his partner vanished? This isn't a small matter."
      "We've been trying to keep it quiet," Professor Lethco explained heavily, "but the news is slowly beginning to spread. It will only be a matter of weeks before all of Hali knows."
      "Doesn't Thuc have a son?" Halimah suddenly remembered. "What happened to his son?"
      "His son?" Professor Lethco said in surprise. "No, there was nothing about his son. But then again, Saedyn hadn't been seen in quite a while. If I remember correctly, he should be around the same age as the two of you. I don't even know if he even lives at the Temple of Fire anymore."
      "Could someone have been targeting them?" Ewen asked, troubled.
      "The former gods are still far more powerful than any ordinary human," Halimah said as she shook her head. "Who would have the power to abduct them in their own temple?"
      "The day and night angels, I fear," Professor Lethco said simply. "I just hope my suspicions can be proven wrong. We'll need to make haste tomorrow morning; if the former gods really are being targeted, either Gwenevieve or Favian could be targeted next."
      "Who are we going to go to?" Halimah asked quickly.
      "Favian," Professor Lethco said as he waved a paw. "The former god of the sky is closer than Gwenevieve." Halimah watched as a bag flew down the stairs from the upper level of the house. The professor snatched it up and began summoning various objects from all over the room. All of them zoomed neatly into the bag. "I've packed everything we need. I'll have to trouble the two of you to sleep on the living room floor tonight. We depart in the morning."

~
      
      When night fell, Halimah fell asleep almost instantly. Her brain was exhausted.
      She waved her arms and propelled herself through the starry void. Without warning, she collided with something quite solid, and she bounced backward.
      The woman with the violet hair and violet wings was back with a smile on her face. "Consider this me protecting you from drifting too far."
      Halimah pushed with her hands, but there was some kind of invisible barrier keeping her from moving forward.
      "Your true magic has been awakened," the night angel said softly. "I helped awaken it for you when I sensed you were near a temple. I wasn't trying to hurt you when I had you walk into the water, but when your magic was awakened, I had to make sure no one else would be alerted of the emergence of a wielder of soul. We need your magic. We need you."
      
~

      Halimah watched the professor's house until it melted into the horizon. The three of them were riding in a small wooden wagon as it magically zoomed down the path cut between the tall grass. This would be Halimah's first time leaving the Firefly District. When she had mentioned this to her professor, he had seemed very eager to help list out all the historical sites they would pass on their way to the Temple of the Sky.
      The speed they were traveling was almost dizzying as the land blurred by, and it wasn't long until the golden fields had disappeared from view.
      "We've just entered the Fisher's Cove District," Professor Lethco informed Halimah loudly over the roar of the wind. The three of them had been traveling for a few hours already, and Halimah's limbs were starting to go stiff. "A few more hours and we'll have crossed the border to the Sand Dance District."
      When they finally crossed into the Sand Dance District, even though the sun was beginning to sink beneath the horizon, the temperatures had risen drastically-all the greenery had been replaced with dirt and vibrant red-orange sand. It was late afternoon by the time the Temple of the Sky finally came into view.
      "Ah-ha," Professor Lethco said triumphantly. "There it is."
      But as they continued to near it, a blast of pale blue light exploded out of the top of the temple, shooting into the sky like a beacon.
      "Stop the cart!" Ewen shouted in a panic.
      The professor waved a paw and the cart skidded to a halt. The three of them watched in shock as a figure shot out of the top of the temple. He had dark skin, long hair, and a robe that seemed to shimmer with all the colors of the sky.
      "That's Favian," Professor Lethco said in disbelief. "What happened?"
      But his question was answered a moment later as two winged figures rocketed into the air after the former sky god. Both of them had flaming violet hair and violet wings.
      "Night angels," Halimah breathed. She looked on in astonishment as the night angels chased Favian through the air.
      "What are night angels doing here?" Ewen's mouth had fallen open in shock. Unlike Halimah, this was his first time laying eyes on the winged folk. "We have to help Favian!"
      Just as Ewen lifted a glowing hand, Professor Lethco vigorously shook his head. "Mr. Hanif, if you value your life, you do not want to catch the attention of the night angels."
      Ewen looked torn, but he reluctantly lowered his arm.
      From the sky above them, the former god of the sky pointed a hand at the night angels, and a blast of pale blue light flashed toward them. The night angels just flapped their large wings and easily dogged the light. Halimah blinked as she tried to keep up with the action. The night angels moved so fast that they were nothing but blurs of violet against the fading sky.
      One of the night angels waved something that looked like a net of living flame in the air. All Halimah could do was watch in horror as the night angels scooped Favian up into the net and vanished into the sky with another flap of their wings.
      "What?" Ewen exclaimed in shock.
      The professor just shook his head as if he too couldn't believe what they had just witnessed.
      The three of them stared at the spot where the former sky god had vanished before Halimah found her voice. "What happens now?"
      "We just saw the former sky god get kidnapped," Ewen said in disbelief.
      Professor Letcho finally recovered from his shock. "Did they take Favian away because they knew I was bringing the wielder of soul here? We need to go see Gwenevieve before it's too late."
      "How about we go into the temple?" Halimah suggested, shaken. "Maybe Favian left something behind as a warning." The professor nodded in agreement, and the three of them clambered out of the cart and hurried to the temple's entrance.
      The Temple of the Sky was made from pale sunbaked clay that contrasted with the deep red sands surrounding it. Half of the temple sat on land, while the other was suspended over the ocean behind it, the same design as the Temple of Life. The inside of the temple was cool, and tall glass windows lined the main hall of the temple, giving them a spectacular view of the sparkling blue ocean outside.
      Halimah stifled her gasp as they pushed open the double doors to the next room. The room was completely trashed. A fight had gone down here: the ceiling of the room had been blasted apart, and dust was still floating to the ground.
      "This was the dining hall," Ewen remarked as he glanced at the shattered plates and goblets littering the floor. Halimah watched as the green-haired boy suddenly closed his eyes in concentration. Green light radiated from Ewen and enveloped the entire room. All the broken tables and silverware drifted off the ground before pieceing themselves back together. Even the chunks of broken ceiling flew back up and mended themselves. Within moments, the room looked as if a struggle had never taken place.
      Halimah folded her arms over her chest as a shadowy figure fell through the roof. Ewen was rewinding the scene. All of the shadows were nothing but memories. Just a couple of days ago, Halimah herself would have been able to cast this spell. During the journey to the Sand Dance District, she tried to use her magic for little things, but found to her dismay that her new magic just wouldn't cooperate.
      Halimah looked closer at the shadowy figure again. It was Favian. Two more shadows fell through the roof. These ones had wings: night angels. Halimah watched as the shadows of the night angels disintegrated into nothing.
      "I got it!" Ewen said in triumph, and the green light faded a moment later. "Look"-the green-haired boy gestured toward the table at the front of the hall. The shadow of Favian was sitting at the table as he examined some kind of map spread out in front of him. Then the former sky god looked up as if someone had knocked on the door. Shadow Favian smiled, and his lips moved as if he were talking. A second shadowy figure walked through the doors to the dining hall.
      Professor Lethco sucked in a breath. Halimah and Ewen both sent quizzical looks in his direction, but the professor responded with a quick, "I'll tell you later."
      The new shadow figure walked over to Favian and they exchanged some words. Shadow Favian looked relieved to see the new person and gestured for them to have a seat. The newcomer sat down, and Halimah finally got a good look at him. He couldn't have been much older than herself. From his appearance alone, he must have been mixed with blood from the Crystal District, the same way over half of everyone in Hali was mixed in some way or another. The boy had pale skin, striking amber eyes, and black shoulder-length hair that was tied away from his face. When Halimah looked closer, she realized that his hair was streaked with silver.
      The two of them seem to be having some sort of important conversation. Shadow Favian then handed the new figure a goblet and the two of them clinked their glasses together. They drank deeply. The new person stood up, and after bidding the sky god farewell, left the hall. His shadow vanished when it reached the doors to the hall.
      Favian drank the rest of the liquid in the goblet before returning to his map. A few minutes later, the two night angels burst into the room, shattering the large glass windows as they swept in from over the water. The fighting started, and then all the shadows disappeared from view as they shot upward.
      "Well," Professor Lethco said at last. "There you have it."
      Ewen was frowning. "It's too bad that the rewind doesn't work with sound. I can't read lips very well either."
      "Who was that other boy?" Halimah questioned.
      "That was Saedyn," Professor Lethco said thoughtfully. "Son of the flame god, Thuc."
      Halimah furrowed her brow. "What would Thuc's son be doing here?" As she was talking, Ewen walked over to the goblet Favian had been drinking from. The green-haired boy casually picked it up and the goblet glowed green in his hand for a moment before he set it back down.
      "Magic suppressant."
      "Magic suppressant?" Halimah repeated. Even though magic suppressants only lasted for a couple of hours, that was already more than enough time to hide the sky god somewhere no one would find him. "Did Favian know he was drinking that?"
      Professor Lethco leaped up onto the table. "Probably not. The former gods have always been on good terms, and I'm sure he never suspected any ill intentions from Thuc's son."
      "Did Sayden put that in his drink?" Ewen asked uncertainly. "But why would he be working with night angels? And if he's the son of a former god, wouldn't that make him a wielder of soul magic too?"
      Halimah just let out a sigh. "We shouldn't linger here. Professor Lethco is right, we need to go see Gwenevieve as quickly as we can."
      After zooming the rest of the way through the Sand Dance District, the group entered the dense forests of the Everglade District.
      When darkness fully engulfed the forest, the trio found a small clearing to spend the night. The professor pulled out sleeping mats from his bag, and Ewen collected scattered branches for a fire.
      Halimah lay on her back with her head resting on her arms. It wasn't so bad sleeping under the cover of the trees. The fire crackling nearby was warm, and with heavy eyes, Halimah watched the stars flickering miles above through the leafy canopy.

    Chapter Three

      Halimah was floating in the void of stars, and the woman with violet wings was watching her keenly with sparkling coal eyes.
      "Do you know anything about the kidnapping of the former sky god, Favian?" Halimah decided to ask.
      "Maybe."
      "Then do you have any idea why he was kidnapped by night angels?"
      The woman shook her majestic head. "Ever since the Second War, us winged folk have been searching for hosts. Yes, both night angel and day angel. Everyone on Hali thinks that the day angels are so pure, so good, but little do they know, the day angels are looking for a wielder of void to act as their host."
      "Void magic? But void is the most destructive form of magic!"
      "It is also the rarest and one of the most powerful forms of magic along with soul magic."
      "What does a host do?"
      "The winged folk will be able to communicate with the person through their consciousness. They'll be able to talk to them and try to convince them to do certain things. They can control the power inside their host, but they can't do anything with it unless their host agrees. Only then can they channel the magic through the host and use it as their own."

~ 
      
      Halimah woke with a start. The sun was just barely beginning to show its golden head over the trees, and the forest was full of fog.
      "Ah, good." Professor Lethco's voice floated over to her. "You're awake."
      Halimah turned to find him and Ewen sitting in front of the fire.
      The professor handed Halimah a piece of flatbread. "After you've finished eating, we'll continue walking."
      As Halimah ate in silence, she thought back to what the night angel had told her the previous night. In comparison to the four main types of magic-life, water, fire, and air-soul magic was already rare. Children born to a mortal and a god were soul magic wielders. But void magic was something completely different: void magic wasn't something someone could just learn. Void magic was the darkness to soul magic's light. It was something anyone could be born with at random, but given that there could only be one void wielder per century, that's what made wielders of void practically a myth.
      
~

      "Hello again," the night angel said.
      Halimah opened her eyes and found herself floating in the void of stars. "I have soul magic. What do you want to do with it?"
      The woman angled her head to the side. "Use it to help people of course."
      Halimah frowned faintly. "You said that the winged folk can control the host's magic. Does it work the other way, too? Can the host control the winged folks' magic?"
      "The winged folk can lend their host power. You're a magic student. I'm sure you know that the stronger your magic is, the more it will take from you."
      Halimah furrowed her brow. Everyone knew this basic principle. But at the academy, her magic was average to the point where even if she completely exhausted herself with it, it wouldn't harm her in any way. But now with her new magic . . . Halimah wasn't sure what its limits were, and she was skeptical enough to know not to get ahead of herself and test it out.
      
~

	"We crossed the border to the Starlight District a few hours back, so the Temple of the Sea should only be a little further away," Professor Lethco announced. "We'll see it when we reach the top of this hill."
      They had left their wagon back in the forest since Professor Lethco had claimed walking would be good for them, and with all the hills in the Starlight District, all his previous visits had ended up with his carts breaking. Although they had been walking for hours, Halimah couldn't help but marvel at the landscape. The sky was painted with feathery white clouds, and birds chirped in the distance.
      "Can we please stop and take a break?" Halimah panted as they made their way up a particularly steep hill.
      Ewen didn't seem to be having a great time either: he was scowling even more than usual and kept muttering things about how he would much rather be back at the academy.
      "Look!" Professor Lethco exclaimed. "There it is!"
      At long last, they had reached the top of the hill. A lush valley spread out beneath them, and a beach of white sand bordered the ocean just beyond that. Sitting half on the sand, half over the water was a temple made of a crystal-like stone. It had large arched windows, and every inch of the structure gleamed in the midday light.
      The trio took in the view before beginning their descent down the hill. "Let's hope Gwenevieve is there," Ewen said with a sigh.
      When they reached the bottom of the hill, Halimah noted in delight that the grass around them was sprinkled with flowers in various shades of purple. But she didn't have time to admire them for long before Professor Lethco yelled, "Look out!"
      Halimah snapped to attention. Were the night angels here?
      But it wasn't night angels that the professor had warned her about. Instead, a huge wave of water was rushing toward them. Halimah braced herself for impact, but to her surprise, the water formed a sphere around them.
      "Don't move!" a girl's voice commanded.
      Halimah turned her head to find a girl around her age standing in front of them. The girl had violet eyes, freckles, and curly black hair that fell to her hips. She was also wearing a flowy blue dress.
      "You probably don't mean any harm," the girl continued, "but it's the protocol that I ask you to state your business here with the former sea goddess."
      There was something familiar about the girl . . .
      "Lyria?" Halimah and Ewen simultaneously asked in disbelief.
      "Ewen?" The curly-haired girl blinked. "Halimah? Professor Lethco?"
      "Ah, Miss Rahimi," Professor Lethco said happily. "What a pleasant surprise."
      The barrier of water around them vanished, and the girl's face broke into a grin. "Welcome! It's been so long since I've seen all of you."
      The professor nodded his furry head. "Yes, yes, indeed." Lyria Rahimi was ranked number one back at the academy, and Halimah had only crossed paths with her a handful of times on campus since their schedules had never aligned. It was true that Halimah hadn't seen Lyria around this year. It turned out that she was training as an apprentice under the former sea goddess, Gwenevieve.
      "Follow me to the temple," Lyria said eagerly. "I'll go tell the others about your arrival, and then I can take you to Gwenevieve."
      "Others?" Professor Lethco asked good-naturedly. "The other apprentices?"
      "That's right." Lyria gestured for the trio to follow her toward the temple. "There are two others. Originally it was just me, but then when Thuc vanished, his apprentice didn't have anyone to train her. Gwenevieve offered to mentor her for the time being too. And then Favian's apprentice just arrived yesterday. He's still a little shaken about what happened to the former sky god. Ah, here we are." They had reached the double doors to the temple, and Lyria opened them with a wave of her hand.
      The entrance hall was a spectacular sight: the floor and walls were made from the same gleaming stone as the exterior, and the large glass windows let in the dancing sunlight.
      "You must be exhausted from your journey," Lyria commented. "I'll take the three of you to our guest rooms. It gets dark in a few hours, so you'll probably want to spend the night."
      Professor Lethco inclined his head. "That would be wonderful."
      All of a sudden, a slip of paper appeared in the air in front of Lyria. She reached out a hand, frowned, and plucked it from the air. Halimah watched her expression change slightly as her eyes skimmed over the words.
      Lyria tucked it into a pocket in her dress. "Unfortunately, Gwenevieve just took off for Hali Central. She won't be back until dinner."
      "We'll just talk to her when she gets back," Professor Lethco reassured her.
      Lyria led them up the stairs to the upper level of the temple. "Anyways, these three rooms are yours for as long as you wish to stay. All of you should come down to the dining hall at six for dinner. Gwenevieve will be there, and so will the other apprentices. I think they'd be delighted to meet you."
      Halimah, Ewen, and the professor watched as Lyria turned and glided back down the stairs. Once she had vanished from sight, Halimah turned to address her professor. "Professor, could I have a word?"
      The cat nodded his head, and Ewen took it as his cue to enter his own room.
      Halimah opened the door to one of the remaining rooms and walked inside. The room was quite big, with a bed and couch sitting on opposite sides of the space. The back wall was made entirely from glass, and Halimah could see the calm ocean stretch for miles.
      Professor Lethco walked over to the couch and jumped up onto one of the cushions. "Ah," he said. "We can finally rest our legs."
      Halimah took a seat on the other side of the couch. "There are a couple of things I'd like to ask you."
      "Ask away."
      "What do you know about hosts for winged folk?"
      Professor Lethco just stared at her for a long moment. "If you'll excuse me," he finally said as he hopped down from the couch, "there are a couple of things I need to go and clarify." And with that, he vanished in a puff of plum-colored smoke.
      
~ 
      
      Six o'clock rolled around at last. And since the professor hadn't come back, Halimah left her room alone and headed down to the dining hall. The doors were already open, and Halimah walked straight into the large room. She quickly spotted Ewen seated at the polished wood table and slid into the chair across from him. "Have you seen the professor?" she asked quietly.
      "No," Ewen said with equal quiet. "Why?"
      Halimah shook her head. "Never mind."
      Lyria appeared in the doorway accompanied by two new figures. The boy on Lyria's left had long hair, dark skin, and wore a simple white tunic. The girl on her right had shoulder-length hair that was a shade of red so dark it almost looked purple. Unlike the olive skin tone Halimah, Ewen, and Lyria shared, she had a lighter shade and was dressed entirely in black.
      Lyria's violet eyes fell on Halimah, and she glided over.
      "Hi, Halimah, Ewen," she said with a polite smile. "Let me introduce you two to my friends. This is Fern." Lyria pointed to the girl with the dark red hair. "And this is Maliq." She pointed to the boy with the long hair.
      "Lulu, be careful where you're pointing, will you?" Maliq laughed as he and Fern took a seat on either side of Ewen. "The last thing we'd want is for you to wash our guests away with a tidal wave."
      Lyria giggled as she slid into the seat next to Halimah. The red-haired girl, Fern, remained unaffected by the exchange; her expression was blank and almost bored as she glanced out the window.
      "It's an honor to meet both of you," Ewen said. "What kind of magic do you two practice?"
      Maliq's eyes were bright. "I practice life magic. You see, even though I don't use air magic like Favian, he still chose me to be his apprentice. Fern over here practices fire magic. I don't think you've introduced yourself yet. What kind of magic do you use?"
      "I'm Ewen," Ewen said. "I practice air magic."
      "And you?" Maliq turned to Halimah expectantly.
      "My name's Halimah. I used to practice air magic too, but not anymore."
      Maliq opened his mouth as if to say something else, but then stopped when Lyria exclaimed excitedly, "Look! Gwenevive and the professor have arrived!"
      Halimah turned to the doorway to watch a beautiful woman in aqua robes glide into the room with Professor Lethco at her heels. So this was the former sea goddess in person. Her long turquoise hair rippled out behind her, and her golden eyes sparkled with centuries worth of wisdom. They all watched as Gwenevieve settled herself at the head of the table, and Professor Lethco took the chair next to her.
      "Thank you, Halimah, Ewen, and Christopher for joining us here for dinner," the former sea goddess said warmly.
      It took Halimah a moment to realize that "Christopher" must be the professor's first name, and another moment to realize she hadn't known that until now.
      The former sea goddess waved her hand. Dishes appeared on the table in a flash of aqua light. As they ate, Halimah decided to ask Maliq about what happened at the Temple of the Sky before Favian's kidnapping.
      "Here's the odd part," Maliq told Halimah around a mouthful of bread, "the day of his kidnapping, a boy came to the temple. He couldn't have been much older than me, but his hair was already streaked with silver. I remember Favian sent me to answer the door for him. One moment I'm talking to him, and the next I'm waking up on the sand next to the temple. I didn't even remember being knocked unconscious. But when I returned to the temple, both Favain and the boy were gone."
      Halimah frowned. She looked at Ewen to see if he had heard Maliq's story too. Ewen nodded at her to confirm that he had been listening.
      "Fern." Ewen turned his attention to the red-haired girl. "Do you remember anything about the night when Thuc was abducted?"
      Fern's expression remained one of boredom. "Just like Maliq, there was a boy with silver-streaked hair. I met him outside the Temple of Fire. I remember talking to him. The next thing I can recall was that I woke up hours later in the entrance hall. Thuc and his partner, Lianna, had vanished."
      Halimah and Ewen exchanged a glance.
      When they finished eating, Halimah, Ewen, and the professor stood up from the table and followed Gwenevive to her study. Neat stacks of books were piled in every corner of the study, and a circular window let in the light from the moon. The former sea goddess took a seat behind the polished wood desk in the middle of the room, and Halimah, Ewen, and the professor stood in front of her.
      "Gwenevieve," Professor Lethco said gravely, "I think you know why we've come here."
      "Christopher"-Gwenevieve looked down at the cat-"I am sure I do. Is it true?"
      "Maybe the girl is the key," Professor Lethco said as Gwenevieve's golden eyes swept over Halimah.
      Halimah inhaled sharply. "The key to what?"
      Gwenevieve's eyes shone. "The key to bringing peace to Hali. After all, you are the child of a god too."

    Chapter Four
      
      Halimah shook her head in disbelief. "I'm what?"
      "You're what?" Ewen echoed, thunderstruck.
      "I knew your parents," the former sea goddess said matter-of-factly. "Yasvitha, the Goddess of Life was a kind woman. And her partner, Farr, was a man of joy itself. Yes"-Gwenevieve's long turquoise hair caught the light-"before the war, Yasvitha gave birth to you. Infants are rare. They need to be protected at all costs. After all, they are the future of our world. Both your parents needed to fight to defend Hali, and ultimately, your mother became a mortal to stop the war. They wanted to try and live a normal life for you, Halimah. They loved their world and even named you after it. You are a wielder of soul magic. And so is Saedyn, the former flame god's son."
      "Favian the child of a god too, though," Ewen started as he furrowed his brow. "Wait, that's right-he was a wielder of soul. But then he took up his mother's position as the god of the sky. After that, his magic changed from soul to air."
      "On the topic of soul magic," Gwenevieve said as she addressed Halimah, "I will begin teaching you how to control your new magic tomorrow. I hope you are ready."
      
~
 
      Halimah woke to the sound of someone knocking on her door.
      The sun had just barely begun to show its golden head over the water. After rubbing the sleep from her eyes, Halimah slid out of bed and walked over to the door. "Who is it?" she called tiredly.
      "It's me." Ewen's voice sounded from the other side of the door.
      Halimah stifled a yawn. "Who's 'me?'"
      "Ewen!"
      "Okay, okay. Come in." Halimah beckoned the green-haired boy over the threshold before shutting the door behind him. "So," Halimah said awkwardly, "is there any particular reason why you're here?"
      "There is, actually," Ewen said as he refused to meet Halimah's eyes. "I didn't know about your parents. I'm sorry."
      Halimah blinked in surprise. "My mother passed away when I was eight, and my father when I was fourteen. I've learned to move on."
      "I just want to say I'm really sorry. From how you made your way around the school, you just seemed so joyful and carefree. I thought you had it all. I never had a good relationship with my parents. I think I was jealous and took it out on you."
      "I-apology accepted."
      Ewen sighed as he changed the topic. "It's an honor to be trained by a former god. Gwenevieve offering to teach you just like that-well, that isn't something that happens every day."
      "Are you jealous?"
      "If I'm being honest, yes. I am a little jealous."
      Halimah gave Ewen a small smile. "I'll ask the former sea goddess if she'd be able to train you too. I think it's only fair; I'm the one who got you dragged away from the academy. This is the least I can do to make it up to you."
      As the two of them headed downstairs to breakfast, a figure came running down the stairs to greet them. "I caught you just in time," Lyria said breathlessly. "Halimah, Gwenevieve sent me to tell you to meet her on the beach next to the temple. Ewen, my fellow apprentices and I want you to help patrol the valley. The more eyes the better. Gwenevieve has warned us about the night angels."
      As Lyria hurried off, Halimah automatically looked at Ewen.
      "What are you looking at me for?" the green-haired boy asked with a wry smile. "Go on-Gwenevieve is waiting for you."
      "I don't think I'm ready," Halimah said truthfully. "I'm about to have to relearn everything I thought I knew about my magic."
      "Think of it as just another class," Ewen said lightly before hurrying to catch up with Lyria. Halimah was left standing alone in the vast entrance hall. She drew in a deep breath, then released it slowly. Determination sparked deep inside her. She would master her magic for the sake our her parents-for the sake of the world they had given so much to protect. Today, Halimah was going to learn how to use her new magic.

    Chapter Five

	Halimah spent the morning relearning the fundamental basics of magic. And to her dismay, her progress was barely visible at all. Halimah staggered backward in defeat. Every inch of her ached, and her head throbbed painfully. The new magic surging through her veins was so foreign-so powerful to the point where Halimah struggled to shape it.
      "I think that is enough for today," the former sea goddess said lightly.
      "Yes," Halimah said breathlessly. "Thank you."
      "I will see you at the dining hall tonight for dinner." Gwenevieve turned and glided back to her temple.
      When the last of the former sea goddess's footsteps faded, Halimah flopped onto her back and threw an arm over her face to shield her eyes from the glow of the sun. It was so peaceful here on the beach. With the waves lapping gently against the white sand and the soft breeze on her face, Halimah was content to lie there forever. She had discarded her shoes a while back, and the sand was warm between her toes.
      "Halimah?" a voice asked.
      Halimah removed her arm from her face and spotted Ewen walking toward her. "What are you doing here? Isn't it time for lunch?"
      Ewen sat down on the sand next to her and looked up at the sky as well. "Gwenevieve didn't go easy on you?"
      Halimah just shook her head. "I've never felt so drained in my life."
      "I'm curious about the night angel you see in your head." Ewen casually changed the topic. "Professor Lethco and I were talking the other night. Can you describe her?"
      Halimah threw an arm over her eyes again. "She has hair like a living flame, coal-colored eyes, and violet wings."
      "Are you in a certain place when you see her?"
      "A void filled with stars. But in all honesty, I don't know how seeing a bunch of stars will help me with anything."
      Ewen laughed, and Halimah turned to him in surprise. She had never heard him laugh before, let alone seen him smile in a way that wasn't a sneer.
      "So what if it doesn't help you with anything?" the green-haired boy said, still laughing. "It must be beautiful, isn't it? That's not something everyone gets to see." The laughter faded from his eyes. "Why do you look so surprised all of a sudden?"
      "You should smile again. Laugh, more. I don't know. It's nice to see you smiling."
      Ewen blinked at her before bursting out in laughter again. "It's not as if I've never smiled before in my life."
      The two of them remained on the beach until the sun had fully disappeared, and the last of its rays melted into the star-strewn sky. Halimah hadn't realized how much time they spent talking until she looked up to find that the sky had melted into night.
      "Now this is beautiful," Halimah said as she gazed up. Purples and blues and pinks shot between the clusters of twinkling stars, and the two moons of Hali cast their silver light down on the world below.
      Ewen rose to his feet. "We should probably head back to the temple. Dinner starts soon." He extended a hand and helped Halimah rise to her feet.
      Lyria, Maliq, and Fern were already sitting at the long wooden table when the two of them arrived.
      "Halimah, Ewen." Lyria gave them a small smile as she waved them over.
      "Hi, Lyria." Halimah slid into the vacant seat beside Lyria, and Ewen sat down across the table next to Maliq.
      "So," Lyria asked eagerly, "how did training with Gwenevieve go?"
      Halimah sighed through her nose. "It's a good thing Gwenevieve is a patient woman."
      Lyria laughed. "I thought that too when I first started my apprenticeship here. When I wasn't able to master an enchantment right away, Gwenevieve would coach me and watch me practice for hours. She's a wonderful teacher-though I'll bet you that kind of patience only comes with being a couple of hundred years old."
      "Good evening Miss Samra, Mr. Hanif." Everyone turned to watch Gwenevieve and Professor Lethco stride into the room. The professor stopped at the foot of Halimah's chair. "I assume your lessons went well?"
      Halimah looked down at the cat. "Good evening, Professor. How has your day been?"
      The professor swished his furry tail. "I've been trying to find information on Saedyn."
      Halimah leaned closer. "Did you find anything?"
      Professor Lethco's whiskers twitched distastefully. "Unfortunately, my efforts so far have been in vain. Even with both Gwenevieve and myself asking around, no one seems to know anything about his current whereabouts. Or anything about him in general. Though, we have been trying to be very discreet as we don't want to cause any unnecessary panic."
      "Professor"-Lyria swiveled around in her chair to join their conversation-"I'm sure at this point everyone in Hali knows about the missing gods."
      "Indeed, Miss Rahimi," the professor said seriously, "they're all aware of the missing gods. But none of them know about Saedyn's involvement. And in fact, we still don't know if he even has anything to do with it. We don't want to start any false accusations."
      "Maybe you should try to get in touch with him," Lyria suggested.
      "We would," Professor Lethco said with a frown. "The only problem is since we don't know where he is, we don't know how to contact him."
      Lyria hummed as she brushed her curly hair over a shoulder. "I've never met the flame god's son before. Does he seem like the kind of person who would harm others?"
      "I'd like to say that no one in Hali is the kind of person who harms others for their own personal gain. Unless you count the winged folk."
      "That's it!" Halimah blinked. "Since Saedyn is the other host, he's probably been influenced by a night angel!"
      Lyria nodded along. "So then the night angels want to use him to get rid of the former gods. With the gods gone, they could stage a full-out war with the day angels without any interference," she concluded fearfully.
      "I couldn't help but listen in on your conversation," Maliq spoke up as he braced his arms on the table. "There has to be something we can do to prevent a third war."
      "I wouldn't worry about it now if I were you," Fern said silkily. "We still have Gwenevieve on our side."
      "I agree with Fern," Gwenevieve said lightly from the head of the table. "Let us not worry about anything right now. Tomorrow when all of us are rested and fed, we can discuss what to do next."

~
      
      "Greetings."
      Halimah didn't even need to look around to know that she was floating in the void of stars. "Do you want to start a war with the day angels?" she asked.
      The woman pursed her lips in agitation. "Why would we want to do that? We finally get to live a semi-peaceful life, and you think we'd want to go to war?"
      "Well," Halimah started slowly, "you do know that the gods are disappearing, right?"
      The night angel nodded.
      "We have a suspicion that the flame god's son, Saedyn, is involved in some way or another." Halimah closely watched the woman's expression, but the night angel gave nothing away. "He's a host too," she continued when the night angel remained silent.
      "That is true."
      "Do you know how I can contact him?"
      The woman's eyes widened slightly in surprise. "Contact him? Why would you want to do that? If he really is the one behind the kidnappings, that would be very dangerous."
      Halimah just looked at the night angel expectantly. "So there is a way?"
      The night angel's face was impassive for a moment before her lips twisted into their usual smirk. "There is." The woman flipped her long, flaming hair over her shoulder. The violet flames crackled, and Halimah instinctively flinched away. "But it requires quite a bit of magical energy. I doubt you could do it now, especially with your current skill level."
      "Then maybe you could do it for me. You told me a couple of days ago that the winged folk can channel their power through the host."
      "You really do want to contact him, don't you."
      Halimah nodded determinedly.
      The night angel lifted her arms in front of her. Flame sparked along the length of her wings. Halimah squinted against its radiance, and then she was sitting up in her bed back at the Temple of the Sea.
      She was there, but not at the same time. Everything was hazy. Her body was moving without her controlling it. Halimah's legs carried her out of bed, down the stairs, and out the temple's front entrance.
      Then the night angel's voice echoed in her head. "To perform this bit of magic, I need to move you far away from the others."
      Halimah was in a state of shock as her body floated off the ground and drifted over the ocean. Soon the Temple of the Sea was only a speck against the star-strewn sky. The vast ocean was spread out beneath her and the dark waters rippled peacefully. Eventually, she came to a stop in midair, and Halimah watched as her arms lifted in front of her. A moment later, she was enveloped in bright silver light.
      "I've got you connected," the night angel's voice said. "But I'm afraid you have to do the rest. I left you with the end of the string. You can choose if you want to pursue it or not."
      What string? Halimah thought back, since her mouth didn't work.
      The night angel didn't respond.
      Halimah sighed. Or at least she tried to. Halimah cast out her mind. The stars and the ocean faded away, and sure enough, there was a string. Not exactly a string, but a thread of silver pulsing through the darkness of the void. Reaching out, Halimah hesitantly twined her fingers around the end of it.
      Nothing happened.
      Halimah tugged at the thread. She didn't know what she was supposed to be doing, but she kept tugging. After what felt like an eternity, a faint pull rippled across the string from somewhere far away.
      Then all of a sudden, she was sitting in a grassy field. Sunlight filtered in from between the trees, and Halimah blinked as she looked around. The string was still clutched tightly in her hands.
      Something seemed off. The harder she looked at her surroundings, the more they seemed to waver and blur like smoke. And then there were footsteps. Halimah whirled around.
      A boy around her age was standing in front of her, and the other end of the pulsing silver thread glowed in his hand.

    Chapter Six

	Saedyn was the spitting image of his shadow back at the Temple of the Sky. He was clothed entirely in white, and his shoulder-length hair was tied back from his face. Even though he was young, his dark hair had almost completely turned the color of snow.
      "Who are you?" he said.
      Halimah opened her mouth and then closed it again.
      "I've never seen you before." Saedyn's amber eyes seemed to stare straight into Halimah's soul. "Why are you contacting me?"
      "I have a few questions to ask you." Halimah finally found her voice.
      Saedyn's eyes flickered briefly with sadness. "I could break this connection right now." His pale fingers tightened on the delicate silver thread.
      "Wait!" Halimah called. "I know you're a host."
      Saedyn's hands stilled. "And what if I am?"
      "You have the ability to communicate with the night angels. And recently, the night angels were seen kidnapping Favain, the former god of the sky. Do you know anything about this?"
      Something shifted behind Saedyn's eyes. "Gwenevieve sent you, didn't she."
      Halimah remained silent.
      Saedyn just angled his head to the side. "Yes, I was the one who orchestrated the former sky god's abduction, as well as my father's."
      Halimah flinched at the coldness of his voice. "Why are you doing this? A third war would be the end of Hali."
      Saedyn's tone was icy. "A third war will be the end of Hali!"
      And with that said, he yanked violently on the thread. The delicate string snapped in his fingers.
      Halimah's eyes snapped open as she was jolted back to reality. The silver glow around her was fading quickly. And then she was falling. Halimah yelped in surprise as she hit the surface of the dark water she'd been levitating above. She heard the splash in her ears moments before the cold crashed into her like a solid wall.
      Halimah's head broke the surface of the water and she gasped for breath. The frigid air stung savagely at her throat. Silently cursing the night angel, she tried in vain to swim in the direction of the temple. The sun was slowly beginning to rise, and the sky was lightening from dark purple to pink.
      Halimah thrashed around in the icy water. Her clothes were so heavy . . .
      Then something flickered in the distance. Whatever it was, it was rushing toward her on top of the water. As it neared, Halimah almost choked as she accidentally swallowed a mouthful of water. It was a dragon made out of water.
      The dragon glided across the surface of the ocean and scooped her out of the water in one of its claws. When they reached the beach, the water dragon set her down gently on the sand before bursting into droplets.
      "Halimah!" Lyria cried as she rushed over to Halimah. Her violet eyes were wide in concern. "What happened to you? You know what, don't tell me now," she said quickly as she helped Halimah to her feet. "We need to get you inside before you catch a cold." Blue light flared around Lyria, and then suddenly Halimah was dry again.
      Before they could enter the temple, the front doors flew open, and Ewen and Professor Lethco hurried out to greet them. "We saw Lyria's water dragon pull you from the ocean," Professor Lethco said worriedly. "Just what happened tonight?"
      "It was Saedyn who used the night angels to capture the gods," Halimah told them breathlessly.
      "You have to be careful, Halimah," Professor Lethco said stiffly. "What you just did-that was reckless. Just wait until Gweneveive finds out about this."
      Halimah stared at the ground. Maybe she had gotten ahead of herself-gotten a little too confident. Too reckless.
      "Come, Halimah," Lyria said gently. "Let's get you back to your room. I think you'll feel better after a good rest."
      "Okay," Halimah said, relieved to be led away from Ewen and the professor's reproachful stares. Lyria took her gently by the arm, and the two of them walked into the temple.
      
      ~ 
      
      "So, did you get what you wanted?" The night angel floated beside her. Her flaming hair rippled like water.
      Halimah was lying flat on her back with the stars twinkling in the void above her. "I'm just going to go ahead and ask it: were you purposely trying to kill me?"
      "Kill you?" the woman said in surprise. "Me? When Saedyn severed the connection, you regained control. It wasn't my fault I got kicked out."
      Halimah shot the woman a look. "I found out that it was Saedyn who was behind the gods' kidnappings. But why would anyone want to start a war?"
      The night angel picked at her nails. "Your guess is as good as mine."
      Then a thought popped into Halimah's head. "Since Saedyn is a host too, does he come to this void as well?"
      "He does. In fact, he's probably in this exact same void right now."
      "Really? Does that mean I can see him here?"
      "Silly, do you know just how big this place is? The void expands infinitely in every direction. You wouldn't be able to find him here even if you tried."
      "Maybe I can't. But maybe you can?"
      
~
      
      Halimah awoke to a tremendous headache. Even the slightest movement of turning her eyes sent a sharp pain shooting through her head.
      A knock sounded on the door.
      "Who is it?" Halimah asked dizzily.
      "Professor Lethco," the professor's voice called from the other side of the door.
      "You can come in."
      The door swung open, and the cat stepped into the room. "How do you feel?"
      "Terrible," Halimah answered truthfully.
      The cat leaped up to sit at the foot of her bed. "I told Gwenevieve what you said to us earlier-that it really was Saedyn behind the kidnappings."
      "Did she have anything to say about that?"
      "Yes, she's going to do an investigation. If Saedyn really is after the former gods, it won't be long until he'll try to come for Gwenevieve. You know . . ." Professor Lethco changed the topic, "It's almost time for dinner."
      It was then that the clouds in Halimah's head seemed to subside. "Dinner? Was I out all day?"
      "Everyone's been quite worried. Especially Mr. Hanif."
      Halimah stared up at the ceiling for a moment before sliding out of bed. "Let's not keep everyone waiting, then."
      In the dining hall, Gwenevieve swept into the room. Her turquoise hair floated behind her as if blown by a phantom wind. "Before we eat, I have some announcements to make," the former sea goddess said lightly. "Halimah confirmed that it was indeed Saedyn behind the kidnapping of both the former flame and sky god. I will talk to him."
      "I don't think it would be a good idea for you to leave your temple anytime soon," Maliq said worriedly as he addressed the former sea goddess. "It's not safe for you to go anywhere alone."
      "I agree," Lyria jumped in. "If you're going to go somewhere, let us accompany you. I don't know what kind of protection we can offer against night angels, but it's better than having you set off by yourself."
      Gwenevieve smiled softly. "I appreciate your concern, but I need to do this on my own. I have ways to stay hidden and undetected."
      "But-" Maliq and Lyria protested at the same time.
      Gwenevieve just raised her hand to silence them. "I am going to take my leave tomorrow at first light. My temple is in your hands for the time being."
      Halimah spent most of the dinner staring out the large windows lining the back of the dining hall, watching the ocean and its gentle waves. She watched the stars and how they cascaded through the crystal-like sky. Everything was going to be okay. Tomorrow, Gwenevieve was going to set out to talk to Saedyn. She would convince him not to start a war-not to destroy Hali.

    Chapter Seven

      "Welcome back!" Lyria and Maliq shouted happily.
      The former sea goddess smiled tiredly at them. "It is good to be back. Regrettably, I have some bad news to share with all of you. I spoke with Saedyn. He has no intention of giving up. But for now, as long as I am still here, Hali will be fine."
      "Do you know where Saedyn is?" Fern asked, and everyone turned to look at her. "If we know where he is, we can go there now and try to stop him from doing whatever he's trying to do."
      The former sea goddess sighed. "Since I contacted him magically, I, unfortunately, am not aware of his current whereabouts."
      Fern fell silent at that.
      
~ 
      
      Halimah awoke before the sun had even begun to show its golden head over the surface of the water. She hadn't been able to communicate with the night angel. In fact, for the past few nights, when she had opened her eyes in the void of stars, there was no one there. Trying not to dwell on it, Halimah quickly dressed and headed downstairs to the dining hall.
      No one else was awake yet, and the temple was silent. On her way to the dining hall, Halimah walked past the former sea goddess's study. The door was partially cracked open, and the light from inside filtered out into the hallway. She paid it no head until she heard the faint voices speaking from behind the door. Gwenevieve and Professor Lethco.
      Halimah paused for a moment but then shook her head. She knew better than to eavesdrop. She took a step past the study, but that was when she heard her name. Doubling back, Halimah pressed her ear as quietly as she could against the door.
