      "Are you sure?" Professor Lethco's voice said in exasperation.
      "If what Saedyn says is true," Gwenevieve was saying, "then we really are not left with many options."
      The professor's voice fell silent.
      "Halimah is stronger than she knows," Gwenevieve continued softly. "I have seen the raw power pulsing through her veins. But yes, at the end of the day, it is her choice. We cannot force her to do anything she does not want to do."
      "What would Yasvitha think?" Professor Lethco finally said. "How do you think she'd react if she could see her daughter now?"
      There was silence until Gwenevieve said, "I wish Yasvitha was still here. But during the war, she was severely injured. And then she became a mortal . . . If I had just checked on her and her partner more-"
      "Her last few years were some of the happiest in her entire life. You had your own injuries to nurse at the time."
      "She was like a sister to me."
      "I know."
      "They all were my dearest friends-Imellia, Yasvitha, Thuc. Lianna too. I miss Imellia. After that second war, I have not spoken to Thuc in years either. I think I am afraid that if I leave my temple, I will run into Rania."
      "Gwenevieve," Professor Lethco said quietly-reassuringly-"everything will be fine. It will take more than the threat of war to break our spirits. Besides, you have some of the best mages of their generation here at the temple standing with you. You should go talk to Rania."
      Gwenevieve's voice dropped to a whisper, and Halimah had to strain her ears to catch the next few words. "For her sake, I have been careful not to show my face. She wants nothing to do with me."
      "I doubt that. She's still your partner."
      Both of them fell silent, and Halimah decided this was a good time to move on. She silently backed away from the door and continued on her way to the dining hall. Halimah didn't know what to think. She felt guilty for listening in on such a private conversation, but at the same time, she had learned new information about the former sea goddess. Halimah sat alone in the dining hall and watched the sun slowly rise from the window.
      Halimah closed her eyes and concentrated. She could feel the magic begin to flow through her. The magic would bend to her will. When Halimah opened her eyes, there was a soft silver glow surrounding her. What should she try to create? Halimah went with the first thing that popped into her mind. Slowly, her magic took the form of a cat. Halimah watched in amazement as the silvery cat flicked its tail and twitched its whiskers.
      "Nicely done, Miss Samra," Professor Lethco said. Halimah turned to find the cat striding toward her. Her concentration broken, the silvery cat faded away, and the glow around her followed shortly after.
      "How's Gwenevieve?" Halimah asked.
      "She's still recovering from her trip," the professor told her with a sigh. "She's quite tired."
      It seemed that Professor Lethco hadn't noticed her eavesdropping earlier. And she felt guilty. "Um, Professor?"
      "Yes?"
      "Well, the door to Gwenevieve's study was open, and I accidentally heard you two talking." As she spoke, Halimah watched the cat for a reaction.
      The professor just leveled her a look. "It isn't polite to listen in on other people's conversations, Miss Samra."
      "I know. And I'm really sorry. I just couldn't help myself when I heard my name mentioned."
      "Ah," Professor Lethco said. "Gwenevieve and I were going to talk to you over dinner tonight about the role you might play later if things take a turn for the worse."
      Halimah opened her mouth to reply, but then movement at the entrance of the dining hall caught her eye. Lyria, Maliq, Fern, and Ewen were walking into the hall together.
      Just before they finished eating breakfast, Maliq rose to his feet, and an odd expression passed over his face.
      "Maliq?" Lyria's brow creased in concern. "What is it?"
      "The wards I set up around the temple were disturbed. Something's coming."
      Everyone sprang to their feet and rushed to the front of the temple. Halimah's jaw dropped in horror as she beheld the sight in front of her. About twenty night angels were flying toward the Temple of the Sea.
      "Shields up!" Fern cried.
      Five shimmering shields sprang into existence around the temple: water, fire, life, air, and a shield of plum-colored light which had to belong to Professor Lethco. Halimah had instinctively tried to shape her magic as well, but she quickly realized she didn't have the ability to make a shield anymore.
      When the night angel leading the group reached the first shield, she stopped in the air and looked down at the magic wielders on the beach below.
      "Hand over the sea goddess," the night angel called. Her flaming violet hair rippled behind her. "All we want is the former goddess."
      "We won't!" Lyria yelled angrily.
      "Then don't blame us if any of you get hurt," the night angel said silkily, and a ball of flame formed in her upturned hand. "ATTACK!"
      All twenty night angels tucked in their wings and dove straight down. They were nothing but violet blurs against the pale blue sky. Fire rained as the night angels blasted away at the shields.
      Halimah's stomach sank as she watched the first shield crack. And then the next. And the next.
      Lyria and Maliq hurried to try another tactic, and their elemental dragons sprung into the sky to meet the night angels. One or two of the night angels flapped upward to avoid the dragons, but there were just too many of them.
      Fern's shield of flame seemed to be holding out the longest against the night angels' bombardment, but cracks were slowly beginning to spiderweb their way across the shield's surface despite the red-haired girl's efforts to repair the holes.
      Beneath Fern's flame shield, Professor Lethco's shield of plum-colored light still glowed brightly. And then suddenly, a light flared across her vision.
      All of the night angels were thrown backward as a new shield, this one of pulsing turquoise light, surrounded the temple. Halimah looked around and instantly spotted Gwenevieve striding down the temple's steps. The former sea goddess's long gown and hair drifted behind her like ocean waves, and her golden eyes blazing as she beheld the night angels.
      The night angels blinked in shock as they pointed wildly at Gwenevieve. Quickly recovering, all twenty night angels dove again and rocketed straight at the former sea goddess's shield.
      "They will not be able to get past my shield," Gwenevieve reassured Halimah and the others as the night angels were thrown backward again. "I can hold them off long enough for all of you to run. They are after me."
      Fern's eyes flicked with flame. "We're not going to leave you!"
      The former sea goddess shook her majestic head. "I do not want any of you to get hurt."
      "We don't want you to get hurt either," Lyria countered, still conducting her water dragon to snap at the night angels circling outside the shield. "We-"
      But whatever Lyria was going to say was cut off as a blast of silver light exploded over the landscape.
      Halimah inhaled sharply. She knew who the light belonged to.

    Chapter Eight

      "Saedyn!" Maliq exclaimed as he took a step backward.
      Saedyn inclined his head in acknowledgment. Even though he was smiling, the gesture didn't reach his cold amber eyes. It was an awful smile-there was nothing warm in it at all. Saedyn's shoulder-length hair was tied back into a ponytail as always, but this time the entirety of his hair had turned a snowy white.
      Saedyn's eyes lazily moved over the group gathered behind the former sea goddess's shield. His gaze landed on Halimah, and his eyes widened in surprise and recognition. For a moment, the iciness seemed to vanish.
      You, he mouthed. Halimah just stared back with wide eyes.
      Quickly recovering from his shock, Saedyn's eyes turned steely again, and that awful smile crept back over his lips. "We meet again, Gwenevieve," he said. His voice was clipped and coated with frost.
      Gwenevieve frowned from where she stood on the sandy beach in front of the temple's entrance. "Leave here immediately, Saedyn. You have until three." The former sea goddess raised her hand three, holding up three fingers.
      "Three?" Saedyn laughed in feigned amusement. "Until you do what?"
      "One." The former sea goddess lowered a finger. "Two."
      "I dare you."
      "Three."
      "Do your worst!"
      The world exploded into light, both aqua and silver. Halimah sprinted to duck under the crystal-like staircase. Ewen quickly followed her, and they joined Lyria, Maliq, Fern, and Professor Lethco who were already crouching low under the steps. Ewen threw out a shield of solid air around the group, and all of them held their breath as they watched Gweneieve go head-to-head with Saedyn.
      Saedyn was throwing blast after blast of blazing silver light at Gwenevieve, and the former sea goddess skillfully countered each attack with her own aqua magic. Even though she was engaged in fighting, Gwenevieve's shield remained intact around the Temple of the Sea.
      The night angels circled in the sky above. Halimah watched as one night angel dove down behind Gwenevieve with a ball of fire forming in her hands. Halimah opened her mouth to yell a warning, but Lyria beat her to it.
      "WATCH OUT!" the curly-haired girl screamed.
      Too late. All the night angels were suddenly diving at once. They reached Gwenevieve at the same time and swarmed her in a whirlwind of violet feathers. Halimah's heart beat a mile a minute in her chest as she watched the former sea goddess vanish from view behind the swarm of night angels.
      Maliq and Fern sprinted toward Gwenevieve, but a shield of silver violently erupted around the temple. Maliq and Fern yelled in anger as they collided head-first with the silver barrier. "Let us out!" Fern demanded as she clawed at the shield with flaming hands.
      Ignoring her, Saedyn lazily walked over to where the former sea goddess now lay in a heap on the sand. "Take her away," he instructed the night angels. Instantly, two night angels swooped down to scoop up Gwenevieve. The former sea goddess's head lolled to the side like a rag doll, and without a backward glance, all twenty night angels flapped their violet feathered wings and took to the sky. They were gone in seconds.
      Saedyn turned to look back at the group trapped behind his silver shield. His amber eyes glinted. "What will you do now that your goddess is gone?"
      Maliq and Fern began shouting all sorts of threats in response.
      Saedyn only laughed in amusement before his voice turned to ice. "I'm warning all of you now to stay out of my way." Then silver light flared as it seemed to sweep over the entire Starlight District. Halimah could practically feel the magic crackling in the air.
      When the light cleared a moment later, the Temple of the Sea was engulfed in blazing silver flames. Halimah shrieked in surprise as she dashed out from under the stairs. Heat radiated in every direction, and flame covered every inch of the temple. Lyria grabbed Professor Lethco-the cat was too shocked to protest-and ran up beside Halimah. Ewen joined the group, and both he and Lyria flung up shields of pulsing magic.
      Saedyn's silver shield still surrounded the temple. They were trapped inside with the fire. Lyria desperately tried to use her magic to extinguish the flames, but the water seemed to have no affect on the silver inferno.
      Halimah whipped her head around to look back at Saedyn. For a brief moment, her gold-flecked eyes met Saedyn's amber ones. And then he was gone-vanished in a flash of silver light. Saedyn's shield winked out of existence, and all of them sprinted into the grassy field beyond, trying to get as much distance as they could from the burning temple.
      When they were far enough away from the temple, they stopped running and turned back to watch the roaring flames. Lyria sniffed from Halimah's side. "I can't believe it. Gwenevieve-the temple-everything."
      "Professor," Ewen spoke up after a long moment of silence, "where should we go from here?"
      "That, Mr. Hanif, is a very good question," the cat said. "Er, Miss Rahimi, would you care to kindly set me down?"
      Lyria sniffed. "Oh. I'm sorry, Professor."
      "Because of the recent circumstances," Professor Lethco told them, "Gwenevieve and I discussed what we would do if she ever was taken away. We agreed on finding her partner, Rania, in Hali Central and ask her to take care of the Temple of the Sea in Gwenevieve's absence. But obviously, that wouldn't be our plan of action now," the cat concluded as he gestured at the burning temple.
      Ewen frowned. "I think we should still go to Rania. She's Gwenevieve's partner after all. She might be able to help."
      "We should head off now," Halimah said anxiously. "The sooner we find Rania, the sooner we can stop Saedyn and get Gwenevieve back."
      "Wait." Maliq stepped up. "Are we all going to Hali Central? Now that all the former gods are gone, who's going to protect the people if anything dangerous shows us?" He sighed heavily. "As much as I want to go looking for the gods, it's our responsibility as apprentices to take over for them in their absence."
      "Maliq is right," Lyria said softly. Her violet eyes were still shimmering with tears. "It's up to us to protect the people of Hali."
      Fern stepped forward as well. "Then I guess this is where we part ways." Her tone was solemn. "I'll head north to the Temple of Fire."
      "And I'll go south to the Temple of the Sky," Maliq said.
      "I will go back to my home district of Firefly and watch over the Temple of Life." Lyria fiddled with a strand of her hair. "It wouldn't make sense for any of us to stay here at the Temple of the Sea. I'm scared to see what it will look like when the flames die down."
      Ewen nodded. Snow-like ash still clung to his green hair. "Halimah, Professor Lethco, and I will go to find Rania."
      Everyone fell silent for a long moment.
      Fern was the first to turn. "Goodbye, then." They all watched in silence as the red-haired girl made her way through the grass toward the mountains in the distance.
      "I guess I shouldn't stick around either," Maliq said sadly. "I do hope we have the chance to meet again. It was a pleasure to know all of you." He saluted to all of them before heading in the opposite direction as Fern.
      "You should go, too," Halimah said gently to Lyria. The curly-haired girl hugged each of them tightly before wiping her eyes with the back of her hand.
      Lyria smiled weakly. "We will meet again. I know it." She waved one last time before vanishing in a flash of blue light.
      Halimah stared at the burning temple. "It's down to the three of us again."
      
~ 

	The three of them had found Professor Lethco's wooden cart, and now as they zoomed along, the buildings of Hali Central were outlined against the distant horizon. As the road grew progressively more crowded, they climbed out of the cart and continued on foot. The grass and trees that lined either side of the path swayed peacefully in the light breeze.
      "Once we get into the city itself, we'll head straight for Rania's residence," Professor Lethco was saying from where he was perched on Ewen's shoulder. "Rania was originally from the Sunrise District, though in her early years, she traveled down to the Sand Dance District to study under the previous sky god, Imellia. Anyways"-Professor Lethco hopped down from Ewen's shoulder-"we have arrived. Welcome to Hali Central."
	Houses, big and small, lined the paved streets. People were milling about, and the sound of children whooping with laughter floated through the air. The sun shone brightly in the center of the clear blue sky as they entered the heart of the city. Professor Lethco led them past apartments and shops until they came to a quieter street.
      "Ah," the cat said as he stopped in front of a two-story house, "here we are."
      After getting a confirmation nod from the professor, Ewen stepped forward to rap his knuckles against the smooth wood. He stepped backward, and the three of them waited in silence. 
      "What if no one is home?" Halimah said after a while.
      Professor Lethco flicked his tail. "That is a good question."
      Ewen frowned and knocked on the door again. This time, footsteps sounded. Halimah held her breath as the door swung open.
      A woman around her mid-thirties stood in the doorway. She had glowing olive skin and thick black hair that was pulled back into a long braid.
      "Hello," Rania said as her deep bronze eyes swept over Halimah and Ewen. "Can I help you?"
      Professor Lethco gave a small cough from behind the two of them. "Greetings, Rania."
      Rania's eyes widened slightly as her eyes fell on the cat. "Christopher?"
      "Yes, yes," Professor Lethco said in a distracted manner.
      "If you're here for information about Gwenevieve," Rania said stiffly, "I'm afraid I can't help you. I have no clue where she was taken."
      "You know about her kidnapping?" Halimah asked quickly.
      Rania folded her arms and leaned against the doorframe. "The whole town knows. I'm sorry to disappoint you all."
      She made to close the door, but Professor Lethco hurriedly interjected, "Wait! Miss Samra here is Yasvitha's daughter-a wielder of soul magic."
      Rania furrowed her brow as if she was fighting some kind of inward battle. But then she sighed and stepped aside. "Come in."
      Halimah tentatively took a step over the threshold. Ewen followed close behind her. The interior of Rania's house was decorated in simple orange ornaments that gave Halimah the impression of miniature suns. Shelves full of books lined the walls of the living room, and piles of even more novels were stacked neatly under chairs and tables.
      "I wasn't expecting guests anytime soon," Rania admitted as she shut the door behind them and hurried over to make room for them on the couch. "Please, sit."
      Halimah and Ewen took a seat on the orange cushions. Rania sat down on the rug in front of them. "So," she said, "let's do some introductions, shall we? My name is Rania."
      "My name is Ewen," Ewen introduced himself. "I'm a student at Firefly's academy."
      "I'm Halimah," Halimah said. "I'm also a student."
      Rania pushed her braid over her shoulder. "Ewen, Halimah, Christopher, please tell me about the Temple of the Sea. From what I understand, it's currently on fire. How did it get that way?"
      Halimah and Ewen looked at each other.
      "It's the doing of the former flame god's son, Saedyn," Halimah decided to start.
      "Night angels attacked the temple," Ewen continued. "Twenty night angels and Saedyn himself came to take Gwenevieve away."
      "Night angels," Rania said thoughtfully, more to herself than the others. "Night angels . . . What I don't understand is why the night angels are working with Saedyn."
      "I spoke with him," Halimah said softly.
      Rania's head snapped up. "You spoke with him?"
      "I asked him if he was trying to start a war. I asked if he truly wanted to destroy Hali. His words were, 'A third war will be the end of Hali.'"
      "A third war will be the end of Hali," Rania echoed. "Then I guess we just need a way to save Hali."
      "Do you know of a way?" Ewen asked quickly.
      "I don't," Rania said slowly. "But I know where you can find one."
      "Really?" Halimah exclaimed at the same time Ewen said, "How?"
      Rania just shook her head. "Stay for the night. I'll spend tonight weighing our options. Tomorrow I'll have a solution for you. I hope all of you won't have any problem sleeping in the living room." Rania stood up from the floor and straightened her tunic. "Until then, enjoy your time in Hali Central."
      
~ 
      
      After a long day of meandering through the city, Halimah, Ewen, and Professor Lethco met up with Rania at a restaurant.
      "How have your past few hours exploring Hali Central been?" Rania asked as she closed her menu and set it down on the table in front of her.
      "I've never seen such a bustling city before," Halimah admitted. "It's so beautiful and full of life."
      "Yes, I thought so too the first time I came here." A small smile crossed Rania's lips. "That is also why I ultimately decided to make Hali Central my home."
      "Why didn't you stay with Gwenevieve?" Halimah couldn't help herself from asking.
      Rania just sighed heavily. "I think Gwenevieve doesn't want anything to do with me at this point. I don't know if she'd even want me back at the Temple of the Sea."
      Halimah frowned. "Gwenevieve doesn't seem like the kind of person who holds grudges."
      Rania was spared from responding as a waiter waltzed up to their table with a bright smile on his face. After ordering, Rania resumed their conversation. "Do tell me what Gwenevieve has been doing these days. Before she was kidnapped, I mean."
      "Before any of the kidnappings happened, Gwenevieve was training an apprentice," Professor Lethco told her importantly. "The other two gods were too. Thuc was the first to select a young and skillful mage to be his apprentice."
	Night had engulfed the city by the time the group had finished eating dinner. They were heading back to Rania's house, and the number of people crowding the streets was slowly dwindling. As they walked, they passed a group of middle-aged women talking in alarmed voices. Bits and pieces of their conversation floated over to them: "The Temple of the Sky is burning too?"
      Halimah looked at Ewen. He nodded. He had heard too.
      "Excuse me"-Ewen walked over to the women-"what was it you were saying just now about the Temple of the Sky?"
      "Dear, dear," one of the women said in a horrified whisper. "You haven't heard?" Halimah and Ewen leaned closer to pick up her words. "Earlier today, the Temple of the Sky was reported to be burning with silver flames."
      Halimah's stomach sank. Was Maliq all right? He had been heading for the Temple of the Sky. Was the Temple of Fire going to be targeted too? The Temple of Life? Halimah really hoped that Rania had the answers they were looking for.

    Chapter Nine

      "Last night," Rania started as she met their eyes one by one, "I saw many versions of the future. I seldom practice divination anymore, and last night reminded me why I stopped. What I saw terrified me; the sky was alight with silver fire, burning, burning. There were two sides tearing each other to pieces. The strange thing is, the people of Hali are fighting alongside the night angels."
      "Let me guess," Professor Lethco said, "we're fighting the day angels."
      "Yes." Rania's eyes were weary. "It's us and the night angels against the day angels."
      "Did you see Saedyn in any of these visions?" Halimah asked softly.
      Rania shook her head. "Strangely enough, I didn't see him in a single one. I searched and searched for him in each future I came across, but he isn't in any of them. I think-" she trailed off. There was an odd expression on her. "I think he might be dead."
      "Saedyn dies?" Ewen looked just as stunned as Halimah felt.
      "I wouldn't think too hard about it," Rania said tiredly. "I only searched through a handful of futures. But one thing is certain: if we don't do anything, destruction will be inevitable. There is a prophecy, hidden away somewhere on Hali."
      "A prophecy?"
      "This was never documented in the history books, but during the First War, a day angel and night angel fell in love with each other. They didn't want another war like the first one to break out, so they created this prophecy as a way to prevent another war in the future. They didn't want to see their world destroyed. Ultimately, it was because they forged the prophecy that they were murdered. Neither of them had much magic left, and they couldn't have resisted even if they tried. That was the true start of the Second War."
      "How do you know about the prophecy?" Ewen questioned.
      Rania traced the whorls etched across the surface of the wooden table with her fingers. "They told the gods. And then the gods told us. They told them how to find it. While we don't know the exact location, they told us that the prophecy responds to soul magic." Halimah felt both Ewen and Professor Lethco's eyes fall on her, but she kept her attention on Rania. "When all the gods combine their magic, it creates a magic in between soul and void. I think the winged folk designed it that way so if one god wanted to use the prophecy, the other three would have to agree as well. But in our current situation . . ."
      "I'm a wielder of soul," Halimah said quickly. "Is there some kind of magic I can do to locate it?"
      "To locate the prophecy's hiding place, you have to reach out with your magic and follow the pull of the soul. You will be the compass. Close your eyes," Rania said softly. "I'll guide you." Halimah did as she was told and shut her eyes. "Now, place your hands on top of mine. I will act as your anchor." Rania's warm fingers wrapped around her own. "Hold on tight," she whispered.
      And then Halimah was suddenly tumbling through a void of stars. She whizzed past flecks of light so bright that her eyes stung. Halimah flung out her arms in an attempt to slow her descent. And suddenly she stopped. Everything had gone silent. Even the ringing in her ears had subsided. From somewhere far, far, away, Rania's voice drifted over to her. "Find the light. Let it guide you."
      Halimah looked around. What light was Rania talking about? There were only stars.
      She took a deep breath and then began propelling herself forward through the void. Halimah waved her arms as if she were swimming and slowly drifted past stars and dust. What was she supposed to be looking for? Was it a bright light? A small light? One of the thousands of stars flickering lazily around her?
      Halimah summoned a small amount of her magic from deep inside her.
      And then Halimah felt it. It was so small, so faint, that it was no wonder she couldn't feel it until now. It happened again. A tug. It was tugging her toward the right. Halimah turned and waved her arms to drift in the direction of the pull. That way. It was over there! She flung out an arm toward the source of the tug.
      Halimah's eyes snapped open.
      "Looks like you found it," Rania smiled faintly.
      Halimah blinked in surprise as she realized her arm was still extended. She was pointing due east. "We should go now!"
      "Wait," Ewen interrupted. "Before we do anything, do we know how much time we have until things take a turn for the worse?"
      Rania's smile faded. "There's exactly a month before fighting breaks out and the world is consumed in flame. Halimah's pointing east-toward the Sunrise District. If you go by wagon, you'll reach the border in about a day. When you reach Sunrise, Halimah, you should search for the light of the soul magic again just like we did today to make sure you're heading in the right direction. One of you should act as an anchor," Rania added as an afterthought to Ewen and the professor.
      "Thank you, Rania," Professor Lethco said with a sigh. "We appreciate your help. We should head off now."
      Rania stood up. "Let me help you pack for your journey."
      She and the professor walked upstairs, leaving Halimah and Ewen alone at the table.
      "How far are you willing to go for Hali?" Ewen asked after a while.
      "My parents loved our world-they named me after it," Halimah replied. "I will defend it with my life. I'll make them proud."
      Rania and Professor Lethco returned from the upper story shortly. "I've packed food and blankets," Rania told them as she set the bags down on the table. "Feel free to borrow my wagon. I'm sorry I won't be going with you, but someone needs to watch over Hali Central, especially with all that's happening now."
      Halimah and Ewen stood from the table, and Rania walked them to the door. "Thank you again," Halimah said gratefully as they stepped out onto the street.
      Rania smiled warmly. "Of course."
 	"Oh, one more thing." Halimah looked back. "If you see Gwenevieve, try talking to her. I think you'll realize that she doesn't hold anything against you."
      "I've got the wagon set up," Professor Lethco called from the side of the house. Halimah flashed Rania one last smile before hurrying over to the professor.
      Fortunately, Rania's wagon was a lot nicer and a lot less rickety than Professor Lethco's had been. The trio waved goodbye to Rania, and the wagon took off down the street.
      
~

	As Rania had predicted, Halimah, Ewen, and Professor Lethco reached the border to the Sunrise District within a day. With all their traveling, the only district Halimah hadn't seen yet was the Crystal District. The Crystal District was the northernmost district one could go to, and it was home to towering mountains and sparkling snow. Crystal was also where the Temple of Fire was located. On the other hand, the Sunrise District was full of rolling green fields decorated with golden flowers. Fluffy clouds drifted through the pale blue and pink-streaked sky. The group had stopped by an inn in a small town to spend the night. Before the sun had begun to rise the next morning, they were off.
      It was the morning of their third day of travel, and the chilly wind bit mercilessly at Halimah's ears and nose. She had wrapped one of the wool blankets Rania had packed for them around her body, but that did nothing to keep the harsh winds from causing her eyes to water. It took her a moment or two to realize that the cart was slowing down.
      "Miss Samra, would you care to find which direction the prophecy's hiding place is?" Professor Lethco's yellow-green eyes seemed to glow through the fog.
      Halimah closed her eyes, but then hesitated and reopened them. "Are you going to be my anchor?"
      "Mr. Hanif would probably be the better choice." Professor Letcho held up his paws as if to prove something that Halimah had missed.
      "Alright." Halimah sighed and held out her hands.
      Ewen stared at her hands blankly before timidly placing his hands on top of hers. "Try to be quick, will you?"
      Halimah only had to close her eyes for a brief moment before she reached out an arm toward the light. Her eyes fluttered open. She was still pointing east, but this time, her arm was more to the right.
      "Perfect," Professor Lethco said, and the wagon began to move again.
      
      
~ 
      
      Much to Ewen's dismay, Halimah returned to the void of stars multiple times later in the day to check if they were still on the correct path. But by the time the sun had dipped beneath the horizon, Halimah didn't even have to close her eyes to feel the tug guiding her toward the prophecy's hiding place. It was a strange feeling-almost as if something was whispering to her. Beckoning her.
      The trio spent the night sleeping under the stars of the Sunrise District. The galaxy above them was filled with pinks, oranges, and reds.
      The next day, they rolled into a forest. The trees around them were tall even though their trunks were skinny. Leaves rustled above them as the wind swept through the branches.
      The pull was so strong now that Halimah was certain that whatever they were trying to find would make an appearance any second. They had left their wagon in a clearing and were now continuing by foot. All of a sudden, the tugging stopped. Halimah blinked and looked around in surprise. But there was nothing there besides the trees. Retracing her steps, Halimah backed up. The tug had returned. She took a step forward. It stopped again.
      "The pull stopped," Halimah told Ewen and the professor. "I think it's safe to say that the prophecy is hidden somewhere in this forest. We just have to look for it now."
      The three of them decided to split up and search the forest. If someone found something, they would alert the others immediately. But so far, none of them had found anything out of the ordinary.
      Halimah walked aimlessly through the trees. With aching legs, she sat down on an overturned log and rummaged in her bag for some food. After finding a snack, Halimah reached into her pack for her bottle. It was empty. Halimah frowned slightly. She had passed a small stream earlier. Standing back up, Halimah walked back the way she had come.
      Five minutes later, she came upon the stream. Kneeling down, Halimah filled her bottle with the clear water. She absently watched a cluster of miniature fish dance up the stream. Their scales sparkled as they reflected the light filtering through the trees. Then something caught Halimah's eye. Below the water-below the mud and dirt it flowed over-something glittered.
      Halimah blinked. There was a hole. But that couldn't be. The hole appeared to be an opening to some kind of space beneath the water. Something was sparkling in the space under the stream.
      "Hey!" Halimah yelled excitedly into the forest. "I think I found something!"
      Ewen and Professor Lethco came running.
      "Look." Halimah lowered her voice as she pointed at the hole under the water.
      Ewen's eyes widened as he knelt down beside Halimah to look closer. "The water is flowing right over it without falling through."
      Halimah nodded. "There has to be magic here. I'm going to take a closer look." She pulled off her shoes and socks.
      She made to step out into the water, but her foot passed right through the mud. It wasn't mud, she suddenly realized. It was an illusion.
      Halimah yelped as she fell through the water and into the chamber below.

    Chapter Ten

      Halimah heard Ewen and the professor yell her name as she landed painfully on her back. Dripping with water, Halimah slowly sat up. She was in a cave. Crystals of pinks and purples and blues grew on the walls, and each seemed to give off their own soft glow.
      "Are you alright?" Ewen was yelling from somewhere far above.
      "I'm fine. Come on down! I think I found the hiding place!"
      A moment later, two loud splashes sounded, and Ewen and the professor dropped to the ground beside her.
      "What is this place?" Ewen asked in awe as he surveyed the crystal-filled cave.
      Professor Lethco frowned at the water soaking his fur. "No wonder no one ever found this place."
      "How big do you think the cave is?" Halimah asked. Her voice echoed.
      Professor Lethco set off across the mossy floor. "Let's find out, shall we?"
      Halimah exchanged a look with Ewen before the two of them hurried after the cat. Somewhere far ahead, a silver light was glowing, and Halimah's breath caught in her throat. It was the same light she had seen when she had been in the void of stars. She quickened her pace. "That's where it is!"
      They passed under a stone arch and into a larger cave beyond. The crystals growing in this cave were pure silver, and Halimah had to squint against their brightness. In the middle of the cave, there was a stone pedestal. And on top of that pedestal, there was a box. It was whittled from dark brown wood and carved with intricate symbols. The three of them stopped in front of the box and stared at it.
      "How do we open it?" Halimah whispered. "I only need to look at it to know that it's been magically sealed."
      "It's probably written on the box," the professor said. He jumped up onto Ewen's shoulder to get a better view of the engravings etched on the box's lid.
      "I've never seen those symbols before . . ." Ewen started.
      "That, Mr. Hanif, is because this is the ancient language of the winged folk. Ah-ha. It says right here." Halimah watched the cat's yellow-green eyes move back and forth over the swirls. "Soul magic."
      "I can do that-"
      "I don't think you understand, Miss Samra. Opening the prophecy box will take a tremendous amount of magic. It will tax you deeply. It might even take a toll on your body."
      Halimah fell silent for a moment. "Just tell me what I need to do."
      Professor Lethco looked at her sideways. "You really want to do this?"
      "Yes." Halimah didn't even have to think about her answer. "This is my world too. I don't want to see any harm come to it."
      Professor Lethco sighed before jumping from Ewen's shoulder onto Halimah's. "Put your hands on the box," he instructed. "Close your eyes."
      Halimah rested both hands on the lid of the box. She could feel the carvings in the wood against her palms.
      "Channel your magic into the box until it yields to you. Channel your magic until it opens."
      Taking a deep breath, Halimah reached out and summoned her magic to her. When she felt it bubbling under her skin, Halimah released the magic into the box. She could feel the energy flowing from her into the whorl-covered wood. Instantly, she began to feel fatiuged.
      "What do you think you're doing?" The voice of the night angel rang in her head. "You don't have enough strength."
      The weariness crashed into Halimah like a wave. "I need to open . . . open this box . . ."
      "What's so important about the box?" the night angel questioned. "Is the thing in the box really more important than your life force?"
      "I need to open the box," Halimah said again. The energy was still flowing from her fingertips. The fog in her mind was growing thicker and thicker. The light around Halimah flared so brightly that her eyes began to burn. She quickly shut them as a sensation like fire began to pickle over her skin. It started as a mere tingle at first but rapidly grew into something much larger. Burning. Her skin was burning with a flame so hot she was freezing.
      Suddenly there was a clicking sound, and then she was flying backward. Halimah hit the ground with a thud and everything went black.
      
~

	"Halimah! Halimah! Wake up!"
	"Miss Samra!"
	"Professor, I don't think she's breathing!"
	"No, she is . . . just barely."
	"And her hands are like ice! Professor, do we have any blankets?"
	"Here-I have one in my bag."
	"This was a terrible idea! Why couldn't I have used my magic instead?"
	"The box only opens to soul magic, Mr. Hanif. Your air magic wouldn't work no matter how much you used."
	"Speaking of said box, the stupid thing didn't even have anything inside!"
      Halimah didn't have time to dwell on his words as a second wave of agony washed over her and she blacked out again.
      
~

      The next time Halimah regained consciousness, she painfully managed to crack an eye open to find herself lying on a pile of blankets in front of a warm fire.
      "Halimah!" Ewen rushed over to her. "You're awake!"
      "What happened?" Halimah asked groggily.
      "You got knocked unconscious," Professor Lethco answered.
      "How about after that?"
      "Well," Ewen said, "we're just relieved you woke up."
      "You've been asleep for three days," Professor Lethco added.
      "What about the box?" Halimah asked in a rising panic. She frantically looked around the cave, all the while trying her best to ignore the sharp stabbing sensation that occurred every time she moved.
      Ewen and the professor exchanged a glance.
      "What?" Halimah asked again, frantically this time.
      Ewen's brown eyes met Halimah's gold-flecked ones. "When you opened the lid, there was nothing inside."
      "Nothing?" Halimah's head went blank. "Can I see it? Please?"
      Professor Lethco nodded at Ewen, and the green-haired boy gingerly passed Halimah the wooden box. Carefully, Halimah took the box in her hands and lifted the lid. She stared blankly down at it. Her insides were just as empty as the box. But the box could only be opened by someone with soul magic . . . Professor Lethco had said it himself.
      Then Halimah's stomach plummeted. "It was Saedyn."
      Ewen and the professor nodded.
      "We came to that conclusion too," Professor Lethco said gravely. "It wasn't recent either. Ewen tried the same enchantment he used at the Temple of the Sky, but we couldn't find anything since it happened too long ago. Also . . ." the cat gestured to Halimah's hair.
      Halimah quickly glanced down at her hair. One thick strand of her hair had turned white.
      Halimah opened her mouth, but no sound came out. She closed it, still staring at the white streak in disbelief. "My hair," Halimah found her voice at last.
      "You used too much magic energy for your current state to handle," Ewen explained regretfully. "Soul magic isn't anything like your old magic."
      Halimah shuddered and pulled the blankets tighter around herself. "Have we been in the cave all this time?"
      "Yes," Professor Lethco said solemnly. "When you opened the box, you seemed to be in a lot of agony. We wanted to give you time to recover as much as you could before we set off."
      "Where are we going next?" Halimah asked. She refused to look at the white streak in her hair.
      "Back to my house," the cat said simply.
      
~

	The ride back to the Firefly District was by far one of the worst experiences in Halimah's life. Every time the wagon rolled over a bump, white spots exploded across her vision. Halimah was staring up at the sky, watching the fluffy clouds drift over the pale blue infinity. But wait . . . there was something there. Moving. Halimah blinked. The shape was still there and flying closer at a rapid speed.
      "Up there," Halimah said in alarm as she pointed a hand at the approaching winged folk.
      Ewen and Professor Lethco snapped their heads up to where Halimah was pointing. "Night angels!" Ewen exclaimed fearfully. "We can't defend ourselves! We're in the middle of nowhere!" It was true: the wagon was currently rolling through the open grassy fields of the Sunrise District, and there weren't any towns for miles.
      "Protect Halimah," Professor Lethco instructed as the wagon came to a sudden halt. "I'll try to call for help."
      Ewen flung up a shield of solid air around the wagon. Professor Lethco glowed with a plum-colored light and was muttering inaudibly under his breath.
      The first night angel landed on the grass a good distance away from the wagon. To Halimah's surprise, the night angel lifted her hands in surrender. "We don't mean any harm," she called. "We just want to talk."
      Ewen eyed the night angel suspiciously as two others landed on either side of the first. "How do we know you're not trying to trick us?"
      One of the night angels sighed as he folded his large violet wings behind him. "If we wanted to take you as prisoners, you'd already be miles away from here."
       Ewen continued to frown but waited for the night angels to continue.
      "We've been betrayed," the first night angel whispered.
      "Betrayed?" Halimah echoed.
      The night angel nodded. "Saedyn betrayed us."
      Halimah just stared at them.
      "And how do we know you're not making stuff up?" Ewen asked cooly.
      "You don't have to believe us if you don't want to," the first night angel said heavily, "but we've come to ask a favor of you."
      Ewen was silent for a moment. "What?" he finally said.
      "Please," the night angel said, and her sad eyes met each of their gazes. "Help us stop Saedyn. The girl is a wielder of soul. We need someone powerful to counter Saedyn."
      "How did you find us?" Ewen asked, still unswayed by the night angel's words.
      "Four days ago," the male night angel explained, "there was a burst of soul magic. It didn't take us long to track it."
      Halimah's heart sank. "Does that mean Saedyn knows where we are? What we've been doing?"
      The first night angel shook her head. "He doesn't know your exact location, but I don't think he sees any of you as threats either. He already took the prophecy from the cave a while back."
      Ewen arched a brow. "What exactly is he doing?"
      "He wants to remove the ancient magics from Hali once and for all. He wants to get rid of the gods and the winged folk."
      "Why did you join him?" Halimah questioned.
      "He didn't tell us what his true intentions were at first," the night angel said. "He told us he wanted to work with us to bring peace between the night angels and day angels. That is the one thing we night angels have been trying to do for centuries. Little did we know he had other plans."
      "How did Saedyn betray you?" Halimah asked quickly.
      "You know how he had us capture the former gods? Well, we found out that he was going to blame their abductions solely on us. With that excuse, he was going to spark a war between us and the day angels. A third war between the winged folk would be the end of us. We need someone to talk to the day angels for us-we need someone to convince them to join us in a battle not against each other, but against Saedyn."
      Halimah fell silent.
      "We need you to convince them to ally with us and the people of Hali," the night angel continued. "Saedyn's going to try to manipulate them into fighting us. We can't let that happen. We can't let him destroy Hali."
      "I'll do it," Halimah said determinedly as she made up her mind.
      The first night angel's face broke out into a smile. "Thank you."
      "I just don't want to see Hali destroyed either."
      After exchanging a nod, all three night angels spread their large wings and took off into the sky.

    Chapter Eleven

	"We have returned," Professor Lethco announced as his house came into view behind the dancing gold grass of the Firefly District. The wagon stopped in front of the house, and the three of them climbed out. Fortunately, Halimah had almost fully recovered during the past few days on the road and could now walk without the world spinning around her.
      Professor Lethco walked over to the door, and just like before, it swung open on its own accord. "Miss Samra"-Professor Lethco turned to address Halimah-"the guest room is up the stairs. It's the second door to the right. You need to rest."
	"I'm fine, really," Halimah tried to protest, but the professor wouldn't have any of it.
	"I'll prepare dinner in a few hours. I don't want to see you downstairs until then."
	Halimah sighed as she climbed the stairs to the guest room. After she took a seat on the bed, she gazed out the window at the peaceful fields. Even though this was the same place she had grown up in, something seemed different. The world itself hadn't changed, Halimah realized. She was the one who had changed. What would her parents think if they could see her now? They had kept their identities a secret for her sake. They just wanted her to be normal and happy.
	Halimah smiled to herself as she thought back to her parents:
      One night while her father was tucking her in for bed, young Halimah suddenly asked, "Papa?"
      "Yes, my golden one?" Farr responded with twinkling eyes.
      "Can you tell me a story?"
      "Ah, my golden one"-Halimah's father flicked her lightly on the tip of her nose-"it's getting late."
      "Please?" young Halimah begged.
      Farr sat down next to his daughter. "Alright. Which one this time? It will have to be short."
      Halimah's face broke out into a smile. "Can you tell me the story of the boy and the girl who fell in love? The story about the adventures they had together? The epic battles they fought?"
      Farr smiled at his daughter. "Of course." He leaned over to turn off the lamp on Halimah's bedside table, and the room fell into darkness. Then he snapped his fingers, and the hundreds of little fairy lights strung around the room flared to life. Farr cleared his throat. "Once upon a time, there was a young boy who met a young girl. They met in the Firefly District-the same one we live in now."
      Young Halimah sighed contentedly.
      Farr wrapped an arm around her shoulders before continuing, "The first time the boy laid eyes on the girl, he knew that he would love her even after the world faded away-even after its remains were nothing but dust drifting among the stars of the universe. Their first meeting was when the boy was walking along the sandy beach, gazing up at the sky. Then he noticed the girl standing all alone in the water. And she too was gazing up at the sky. The boy walked over to the girl and used his magic to conjure a bouquet of flowers from thin air. Those, he held out to the girl."
      "What type of flowers were they?" young Halimah interrupted.
      "Pink and gold and sparkly. Like the ones I always buy for your mother."
      "Oh! Those flowers!"
      "Yes, the girl turned around and giggled. And suddenly, the boy became quite shy and his face turned as red as a tomato."
      Halimah giggled.
      "The girl just smiled. She took the flowers from the boy and tucked one behind her ear. After that, the two of them became best friends."
      "When did the boy tell the girl that he loved her?"
      "I'm getting to that part. Besides, you already know the ending." Farr cleared his throat again before continuing. "Later, the boy moved in with the girl at her temple."
      "What did the temple look like?"
      "The temple was full of life. It was big and made out of a stone that sparkled in the light from the midday sun."
      "It sounds wonderful!"
      "One day, the boy and the girl were planting flowers in their garden when the girl said to the boy, 'this brings back memories of the first time you gave me these very same flowers.'
      "The boy smiled and said, 'That truly was the happiest moment in my life when I first met you.' And then-"
      "My, my, what kind of nonsense are you filling our daughter's head with now?" Halimah's mother's voice called from the doorway. Her dark hair glowed in the light from the living room behind her as she leaned against the doorway.
      Halimah turned to her mother. "Please, Mama? Can we finish the story?"
      Yasvitha's eyes danced with laughter. "You need to get some sleep. You have school tomorrow, remember?"
      Farr stood up and walked over to join Yasvitha by the doorway. Then both of Halimah's parents turned back to smile at her. "Sweet dreams, our golden one."
      Halimah watched her father and mother share a smile as the two of them stood silhouetted against the warm light from the living room.
      "Looks like I've interrupted your thoughts." Ewen's voice came from the doorway. Halimah turned around to find him leaning against the doorframe.
      "No." Halimah shook her head as she blinked away the slight stinging in her eyes. "It's fine."
      Ewen's expression was unusually gentle. "Are you thinking about your parents?"
      "Yes," Halimah said softly.
      "Would you like to talk about it?"
      Halimah fiddled with a strand of her dark hair, but then stopped when her fingers brushed the white strand. "That would be nice, actually."
      Halimah spent the next couple of hours telling Ewen about her father, her mother, and her childhood. Occasionally, she would hesitate, worried that she had been boring the green-haired boy with her rambling. But each time, Ewen just encouraged her to keep talking. He listened intently to everything she said, nodding or shaking his head at particular bits of information.
      When she was done talking, Halimah let out a breath. She felt much lighter.
      The stream of sunlight filtering into the room had turned golden in color as the sun began to sink, staining the sky outside pink and orange. Halimah and Ewen sat side by side, shoulder to shoulder.
      Halimah hugged her knees to her chest, hyper-aware of how her arm brushed against Ewen's. During her years in the academy, Ewen himself had scared everyone away from wanting to befriend Halimah. For the longest time, he had been her bitter rival. But now . . .
      "What about your parents?" Halimah asked softly. "What about your past?"
      Ewen dropped his gaze. "It isn't the most exciting story. Are you sure you want to hear it?"
      Halimah nodded her head as she smiled faintly. And so Ewen ended up telling Halimah how his parents favored his siblings over him. In the past, he always had to compete with his siblings for attention. His parents had never cared, and instead, encouraged their rivalry.
      When Ewen finished with his story, he stood up. "I have an idea. Come with me."
      Halimah blinked. "Didn't Professor Lethco say I can't go downstairs until dinner?" But she ended up following Ewen out of the guest room and down the stairs anyway.
      Ewen led Halimah out of the front door and into the field of golden grass beyond. Eventually, the two of them reached a small river. "Here!" Ewen said excitedly, hurrying over to the edge of the water. "Come look!"
      Halimah hurried over as well and curiously crouched down to see what Ewen had found. There, growing out of the mud next to the water was a patch of flowers. Their delicate petals were a soft pink in color, and the inner stamens were flecked with bits of glittering gold. These were the flowers from her childhood.
      Closing her eyes, Halimah cleared her mind of everything except the image of the flowers. Their size, shape, texture. She could feel the magic flowing through her. She would shape it to her will.
      When Halimah opened her eyes, there was a small pile of silvery flowers lying on the ground at her feet. Halimah felt a smile spread across her face.
      Ewen smiled back, and his green hair glowed in the dying light as he bent down to pick up one of the silver flowers. He twirled the stem in between his fingers before presenting the flower to Halimah. Laughing, Halimah took the flower and tucked it behind her ear. Her magic was finally hers to control again.
      
~

      
      "Do I know that Saedyn has betrayed us?" the night angel repeated Halimah's question. "I'm aware, thank you very much."
      "I'm going to try to talk to the day angels," Halimah told her. "We're going to try to convince them to ally with the night angels."
      "You do know that the only thing the day angels are interested in is a wielder of void. I'm sure if you brought a wielder of void to talk to the day angels, they'd happily listen to everything that person has to say."
      "But where can I find a wielder of void?"
      The night angel smirked as she flipped her flaming hair over her shoulder. "And that's the dilemma."
      
~
      
      Halimah woke the next morning to the sound of Professor Lethco's voice. "You'd better come downstairs, Miss Samra. A night angel is waiting outside."
      No longer tired, Halimah leaped to her feet and hurried down the stairs. She ran to the front door and threw it open to find Ewen already standing outside. He was suspiciously watching the night angel waiting a good distance away. "She was refusing to talk to us until we brought you down," the green-haired boy informed Halimah.
      The night angel turned to Halimah. "Wielder of Soul. Are you ready?"
      "Are we going to speak with the day angels now?"
      The night angel nodded. "I'm sorry, but we need to talk to them before Saedyn does."
      Halimah exhaled sharply through her nose. "Alright. Tell me what I need to do."
      "Find the king of the day angels-he's the one you'll need to speak to. I will create a portal that will allow you to enter the realm of the day angels. All you will need to do is step through."
      "Can I bring my friends with me?" Halimah asked as the gravity of her situation began to sink in.
      "You can bring the cat." The night angel nodded in Professor Lethco's direction. "The boy would attract too much attention."
      Professor Lethco jumped up onto Halimah's shoulder, and Halimah nodded to the night angel. The night angel held out her arms, and a sphere of golden light formed above her upturned palms. The sphere grew larger and larger until it was the size of a door. The night angel stepped backward, and the door solidified itself on the grass in front of her.
      The door swung open, and golden light radiated from the doorway. It was so bright that Halimah had to shield her eyes. "All you need to do is walk through the door," the night angel said quietly. "When you're done talking, come back through. We'll be waiting."

    Chapter Twelve

      Halimah squeezed her eyes shut as she passed through the brilliant golden light. Even though the radiance stung her eyes from behind her closed lids, she kept moving forward.
      When the light finally faded, Halimah slowly opened her eyes. She wasn't in the Firefly District anymore. Instead, she was standing in the middle of a paved street. Towering structures built entirely of stone reached toward the sky above her. The world was bathed in pale pink sunlight, and it would have been beautiful if Halimah wasn't worrying about what she was about to do.
      Tearing her eyes away, she turned back to the doorway from which they had come. It was almost completely invisible except for a faint outline of glowing gold light.
      Everything was silent. Eerily silent. Halimah felt her skin prickle. "We need to find the king," she said to Professor Lethco. "Do you know where he is?"
      The cat nodded. "We'll probably find him in the castle at the highest point of the realm of the day angels." The cat raised his head. Halimah looked up too.
      The castle was floating in the sky. It was barely a pinprick in the distance.
      Suddenly the sound of heavy wingbeats sounded, and Halimah barely had time to whirl around before two day angels touched down on the ground behind them. Both day angels had large feathered wings the color of metallic silver and piercing gemstone eyes.
      "An unwinged one," the female day angel said. Her lapis-blue eyes sparkled with curiosity. She appeared to be around the same age as Halimah and had silky hair the color of ink. "How did you get here?"
      The male day angel turned to the female with a skeptical look on his face. "Never mind that, now that she's here, we should take her to the king. The king will know what to do with an unwinged one. For all we know, they could be spies for the night angels."
      The female day angel shot the male day angel a look. "And what if they are? What if they want to talk about an alliance?"
      The male day angel sighed heavily as he ran a hand through his silver-blue hair. "Oh, not this again."
      "Not this again?" the female echoed. Her eyes flashed.
      "Forget it." The male day angel held up his hands in surrender. "If they do turn out to be spies for the night angels, there isn't anything I can say other than that they'll deserve what is coming to them." With that said, he rocketed into the sky and vanished behind one of the towering stone structures.
      The female day angel extended a hand to Halimah. "Take my hand," she said gently. "I'll take you to the king." Professor Lethco nodded silently from Halimah's shoulder. Reaching out shakily, Halimah placed her hand in the day angel's.
      There was a flash of light, and then Halimah was standing in front of a set of large double doors. She didn't need to ask to know that they were now inside the castle.
      "Be careful what you say," the day angel said quietly to Halimah. "The king is not one to be messed with. I'll wait for you outside." The day angel stepped over to the doors and knocked three times. "Your Majesty," she called, "you have visitors from the land of the unwinged folk. They request an audience with you."
      There was silence for a moment-silence so thorough that Halimah could hear her heart pounding away in her chest. She was positive Professor Lethco and the day angel could hear it too. Then a deep voice finally responded, "I will speak to them now. Let them in."
      The double doors smoothly swung open.
      "This must be the throne room," Professor Lethco whispered in Halimah's ear. But even if the professor hadn't told her, it was apparent that there was only one place this could be. The walls were made from a pale-colored stone, and large arches were cut in the place of windows. A soft breeze wafted in through the arches, and Halimah could see the sky and the clouds beyond.
      On the far side of the room and up a flight of marble-like steps was an elaborate throne. But it was the person sitting on the throne that captured Halimah's attention.
      The king of the day angels sat with his large silvery wings draped lazily over the back of the throne. He had long unbound silver-blue hair, pale skin, and wore the most intricately embroidered robe Halimah had ever laid eyes upon. The corners of his mouth flickered upward in a smile. Halimah resisted the urge to shudder. It was the most unnerving smile she had ever seen.
      "So," the king of the day angels said, and his deep voice reverberated throughout the room, "what brings you here?"
      "I'd like to speak with you," Halimah said. Her voice was much more confident than she felt.
      The king leaned forward on his throne, and his long silken hair cascaded down his back. "Speak. Let's hear what you have to say."
      Something about the king's mannerisms made Halimah feel uneasy, and she took a deep breath before beginning. "I don't know if you're aware or not, but strange things have been happening on Hali. All the former gods have been captured and are currently being held someplace unknown. On top of that, their temples have been set on fire with silver flames."
      The king nodded along. His face gave nothing away.
      "These actions were set in motion by Saedyn, the son of the former flame god," Halimah continued. "Now he wants to have the night angels fight the day angels. We can't let that happen-a fight like that will destroy Hali. We suspect he's going to come here. We think he's going to give you, the day angels, false information so that you'll go to war with the night angels. And a third war would bring disaster to Hali."
      "A war with the night angels," the king mused. "But wait, who is this 'we' you speak of?"
      "The night angels."
      "The night angels," the king repeated before shaking his head. His shoulders quivered in silent laughter. "They sent you here?"
      Halimah nodded. "They want to ally with the day angels. Against Saedyn. Please, Your Majesty, would you be willing?"
      The king leaned back on his throne. "Of course not."
      Halimah felt her heart sink. "I-I'm sorry?"
      "You think my subjects would willingly ally themself with the creatures they're instructed to kill on the spot? You think they would ally themselves with the things working in our very mines?"
      "How did things get this way? What did the night angels ever do to be worked as slaves?"
      The king of the day angels smiled a smile that didn't quite reach his cold eyes. "After the First War, we took a considerable amount of prisoners. We clipped their wings and brought them to work in our mines to craft weapons. I'm merciful, you see . . ." Then the king's eyes flashed. "You're a wielder of soul magic." This time his false smile evaporated completely.
      "I am."
      Slowly, the king rose to his feet, and his feathered wings flared behind him. "I see how it is. The night angels sent you here not to talk of peace, but instead to use you against me."
      "No!" Halimah shook her head, panicked. "Please, Your Majesty! The people of Hali and the night angels don't want to fight you. They don't want to see Hali destroyed."
      Then it clicked. Was the king apprehensive of her magic? The night angels had told her before that the day angels were after a wielder of void. It all made sense now. A wielder of void would be a weapon able to annihilate the night angels. So that meant a wielder of soul was a threat to the day angels.
      The king ignored her words. "I will let you go this time, Wielder of Soul," he said softly. His navy eyes glinted dangerously. "I want you to give the night angels a message from me. I want you to tell them that we'll deal with this Saedyn later."
      "Saedyn's a wielder of soul too!" Halimah cried desperately. "You'll need to be allied with the night angels to stop him!"
      "What makes you think he's so powerful?" the king of the day angels asked as he slowly descended the step of the dais. He drew closer to Halimah with each step.
      "If you go after the night angels," Halimah said quickly, "Saedyn will just go after you afterward. And then you'll have no one beside you to fight against him."
      "My answer is still no. Us day angels have been preparing for too long to stop now. The war is about to begin. I've waited a hundred years since the First War for this. The night angels have a week before we blast them out of the sky."
      Halimah didn't know what had overcome her as she took an angry step toward the king. She felt Professor Lethco's claws dig into her shoulder in warning. "You're going to put Hali at risk just because you don't want to coexist with the night angels?"
      "We can't coexist. Why live side by side when you can rule over them all?"
      "The night angels only want peace. They only wish to protect the people of Hali."
      The king clicked his tongue in amusement but took a step back as silver blazed in Halimah's eyes. "I will consider it." He turned and walked back up the dais to his throne. The king of the day angels waved his hand lazily. "You are dismissed."
      Halimah spun around and marched out of the throne room.
      The day angel that had brought them to the castle was waiting just beyond the doors. "How did it go?" she asked expectantly.
      "He said that he'd think about it." Halimah shook her head in frustration.
      "I couldn't help but listen in on your conversation," the day angel said quietly. "Just getting the king to think about doing something is impressive. Take my hand."
      Halimah twined her fingers through the day angel's, and they were whisked away in a flash of light.
      When they reappeared on the paved street lined with towering stone buildings, the cat leaped down from Halimah's shoulder. "While you were arguing with the king, I was using my magic to search for the kinds of weapons His Majesty was talking about."
      "Did you find them?"
      The professor nodded gravely.
      "Not all of us day angels agree with the king," the dark-haired day angel spoke up. "Did he tell you what he did to the night angels they captured after the First War?"
      "He told us that he had their wings clipped and-"
      "Clipped their wings?" the dark-haired day angel laughed humorlessly. "Yes, he did that and much, much, more. For the past century, the king has been using the imprisoned night angels as slaves. He's keeping them locked up underground, forcing them to craft weapons that will be used against the night angels. Even though I'm part of his court, I don't have much influence in the castle. With that said, I'll try my best to talk to the king-to make him see that allying with the night angels against Saedyn is the right thing to do."
      "Thank you." Halimah bowed her head respectfully.
      The day angel smiled sadly. "I'm just doing what I can to make sure that the king doesn't destroy any more of what we love during his conquest to rule the land and skies."
      Halimah thanked the day angel again and watched as the dark-haired female took off into the sky. Her figure disappeared from view in seconds.
      "Let's head back to the ground," Halimah said quietly to the professor. The cat nodded, and they stepped back into the doorway of glowing golden light.
      When the light faded, Halimah and the professor had returned to the golden fields of the Firefly District. The night angel who had created the golden doorway was sitting on the ground with her large violet wings draped over the ground behind her. When she noticed Halimah and the professor, she jumped to her feet with hopeful eyes.
      Halimah shook her head dejectedly. "He said he'd think about it."
      The night angel sighed heavily. "I apologize for not telling you more about the king of the day angels before you went to meet him. But we thought if you knew just how much of a snake he actually was, you'd be hesitant to speak with him."
      "Would you like to come in?" Professor Lethco asked as he gestured at his house.
      The night angel smiled but shook her head. "I appreciate your offer, but I need to head back and report to our queen."
      "Alright." Professor Lethco swished his tail. "Oh, before you go, I have a few things to tell you about the weapons I found in the day angels' realm. I'll leave you with a message to bring to your queen." The cat closed his eyes and began glowing with a faint plum-colored light. Slowly, a pulsing orb of light formed in the air in front of him.
      The night angel tentatively extended a hand and plucked the light out of the air. Her face paled, and she inhaled sharply before she took off into the sky.
      Halimah stared at the professor in alarm, but he just motioned for her to follow him into the house.
      "How did the talk go?" Ewen asked the moment the two of them stepped inside.
      Halimah just shook her head.
      Professor Lethco jumped up onto the arm of the couch. "The day angels have some very powerful weapons. They plan to exterminate the night angels."
      There was silence for a long period of time, then Ewen spoke up. "On a different note, Rania has vanished."
      "Vanished?" Halimah's heart sank.
      "Apparently it happened only yesterday," Ewen said gravely. "I just heard the news an hour ago when I went to the marketplace."
      Halimah shook her head hopelessly.
      "Don't worry," Professor Lethco said.
      "Don't worry?" Ewen echoed worriedly. "What do you expect us to do?"
      "There's still me."
      "And what can you do?"
      "I'm a cat," the professor said simply.

    Chapter Thirteen

      It was the next day, and Halimah was returning from the marketplace. She had just reached the professor's house when a flash of blue light had her throwing her arms up to shield her eyes.
      "Halimah!" a familiar voice exclaimed.
      Halimah blinked in surprise as the light cleared to reveal a girl in a light blue summer dress, a second girl clothed entirely in black, and a boy with long hair. Lyria, Fern, and Maliq were standing in front of them.
      The door to the house swung open to reveal Ewen and the professor. "Lyria?"
      Lyria was smiling faintly as her violet eyes sparkled. "I'm so happy we caught you!"
      "Lyria," Halimah said, still in a state of shock, "it's really great to see you too. But what are you doing here? I thought the three of you went to different temples."
      "We did." Lyria waved a hand as the wind blew strands of her curly hair in every direction. "But that isn't important right now."
      "We've found where Saedyn's been keeping the former gods," Maliq cut in seriously. "The three of us have been looking for you all week."
      Ewen frowned as he took a step forward. "You said you found where the former gods are. Where exactly is that?"
      Maliq sighed heavily. "He hid them in plain sight-they're locked up at the Temple of Fire."
      "Is there a reason you didn't just charge in there and free them yourselves?"
      "Oh, we tried." Lyria shook her head in discouragement. "We couldn't get in. There are wards placed around the temple that can only be broken with soul magic. We need your help, Halimah."
      "I say we leave now," Fern said importantly.
      "Now?" Halimah echoed.
      "How about we go inside and talk first?" Professor Lethco offered. "We have something you three might want to hear about the day angels and night angels."
      Inside the professor's house, Halimah and Ewen took turns explaining what had happened after the six of them had parted ways.
      "That doesn't leave us with much time," Maliq said as they finished. "I don't even know if we can rescue the gods within that time."
      "We need to try," Halimah said determinedly. "Let's go."
      The world flashed a flaming red as Fern transported them away from Professor Lethco's house. Halimah stifled her gasp of surprise as towering snow-covered mountains shot up to take its place. They had been teleported to the Crystal District.
      Halimah looked around at her soundings. Everything was still. Even the air was still.
      Lyria, Maliq, and Fern were standing to Halimah's left, and the former drew a map in the snow with her foot. The curly-haired girl and her companions didn't appear to be affected by the cold in the slightest.
      "Wait"-Halimah furrowed her brow-"where's the temple?"
      "Ah." Maliq's eyes sparked knowingly. "It's below us."
      Lyria nodded. "We're going to have to do a little walking. We couldn't risk accidentally teleporting into the wards."
      "Follow me," Fern said. "I'll lead the way."
      Carefully, the six of them began making their way down the ice-covered mountain. "Some of these mountains are actually made out of pure ice," Professor Lethco was telling Halimah from where he was perched on her shoulder. "In the right light, they sparkle like crystals. Hence how the district got its name."
      "Here we are," Lyria's voice called from around the rocky ledge. Halimah turned the corner and found that the others had stopped walking. At first glance, there didn't seem to be anything out of the ordinary about the path. But when Halimah took a step closer, an odd sensation washed over her. Something was whispering to her. Friend, the strange power called, I can sense your presence.
      "Who are you?" Halimah whispered. She could feel the stares of her companions on the back of her head, but she paid them no heed as she took another step closer to the whispers.
      Friend, the power called again-louder this time, I am at your command. What do you wish me to do?
      "Could you let us in?" Halimah asked as nicely as she could. "Please?"
      Of course friend, the power whispered into her ears and mind and soul.
      "Can my friends come too?"
      Of course, the power echoed, they may come if you will it. And then the voice faded. Halimah could no longer feel the tug.
      "I think the wards are down," Halimah said in shock.
      "They are!" Fern exclaimed. "Let's hurry!"
      The six of them hurried onwards, this time with Maliq in the front and Fern bringing up the rear. "There it is," Maliq said quietly as he motioned for everyone to halt. "That's the Temple of Flame."
      The Temple of Flame was one of the most breathtaking structures Halimah had ever seen in her life. It was built out of a reddish-orange crystal that seemed to pulse with living flame.
      "I thought it was on fire," Halimah said, still mesmerized by the colors.
      "It was," Lyria said. "Until a few days ago, that was. The fire just stopped. All the fires did. And look, there isn't even a scratch on the temple."
      "This way." Fern took the lead again and led everyone toward the front entrance. The inside of the temple was eerily quiet and each footstep echoed.
      "Now that we're inside," Lyria whispered to the group, "we should split up and search for the former gods."
      "Ah," Professor Lethco said from Halimah's shoulder. "There's no need for that, Miss Rahimi. Even with the wards back up, I can sense Gwenevieve's presence. She and the others are directly beneath us."
      "I was an apprentice here at the Temple of Fire before Thuc was kidnapped," Fern said quietly. "I know my way around. The stairs are this way." As they walked, the red-haired girl continued to talk, "Thuc's temple has a portion built entirely inside the mountain. It only makes sense that Saedyn's been keeping the gods there. Why didn't I think to check earlier?"
      When they reached the end of the hallway, Fern pushed open a door to reveal a staircase leading down into the heart of the mountain. After descending the steps, the group entered the underground portion of the temple. Doors lined the hall, and all of them were closed.
      "Professor," Halimah said as she looked around, "do you sense the former gods?"
      The cat shook his head. "I can feel their presence all around us. They're here somewhere-I just don't know which door . . ."
      Ewen walked over to the door closest to the staircase. "Well, we've got to start somewhere." The green-haired boy twisted the handle, and the door swung open to reveal an empty bedroom. "Not in here."
      And so the six of them began making their way down the hall, taking turns trying the different doors as they went. Halimah reached out a hand to open a door halfway down the hall. The door swung open swiftly, and Halimah nearly jumped out of her skin.
      She was standing face to face with a night angel. And not just any night angel-it was the night angel she had been seeing in her dreams.
      "You!" Halimah breathed. Halimah could hear Lyria, Maliq, Fern, and Ewen shifting into defensive stances behind her.
      The night angel angled her head to the side, and a faint smile played on her lips. "Shh." Her coal eyes sparkled knowingly. "I wouldn't wake him if I were you."
      "Wake who?" Halimah asked. She was too rooted to the spot to take a step back.
      "Saedyn, of course."
      Halimah craned her neck, trying to look past the night angel in the doorway, but the violet-winged woman was standing right in front of her. "What are you doing here?" Halimah said, still in a state of shock.
      "I could ask you the same thing. But do try to keep quiet, will you? Let the poor boy sleep in peace." And with that said, the night angel shut the door in Halimah's face.
      "What was that about?" Lyria asked weakly. "You know that night angel? And Saedyn is in that room?"
      In a daze, Halimah walked to the next door over and pushed it open. They still needed to find the former gods. And there, sitting in a chair on the far side of the comfortably furnished room, was Gwenevieve. The former sea goddess turned to look at Halimah and the others with an expression of mild surprise on her face. "What are all of you doing here?" she asked.
      "We're here to rescue you!" Maliq hurried into the room. "We need to hurry!"
      "None of us former gods are in any danger." Gwenevieve's golden eyes flickered as she let out a sigh. "Any of us could have walked out of the temple if we chose to do so."
      "What?" Fern shook her head in disbelief. "But we saw Saedyn capture you!"
      Gwenevieve looked at everyone in turn. "I think it is about time I told you the truth. The kidnappings were staged. In fact, I did not know about this until I went to speak with Saedyn. You all remember how I left the temple for a short period of time to talk to him. Saedyn asked me to listen to what he had to say. Saedyn loves this world as much as the rest of you. He was determined to do everything he could to protect it. He found the prophecy hidden in the Sunrise District. It showed him what he needed to do to save everyone. He had to unite the winged folk. Only then would war be prevented."
      "That's right." A familiar voice sounded from the doorway. Everyone turned to find Rania standing with her arms folded across her chest. Three other figures stood behind her: two men and one woman.
