The first man had dark skin and wore a robe that seemed to ripple with every color of the sky, the second man had a lighter complexion and long black hair, and the woman was fair with pale brown locks.
      Halimah knew who these people were. Favian the Sky God, Thuc the Flame God, and the latter's partner.
      "To be seen as such a threat, Saedyn needed to make it look like he was ridding Hali of its gods," Rania concluded.
      "What about the night angels?" Ewen asked. "Didn't they say that Saedyn had betrayed them? Didn't they say that Saedyn wanted to rule over Hali?"
      The woman who must have been Saedyn's mother shook her head gently. "Since you're here, you can ask him yourself when he wakes." She entered the room with Rania, Favian, and Thuc trailing close behind. "Saedyn has nearly exhausted himself to death," Saedyn's mother continued sadly. "He's been using too much magic too quickly. However, he was insistent that it was his responsibility to save us all."
      The door to the room swung open, and everyone whirled around again. This time, it was Saedyn who stood in the doorway. His white hair was unbound, and there was an expression of surprise on his face. But it faded almost instantly as his eyes turned cold. "I-"
      Thuc sighed. "You can drop the act. It's alright. We told them."
      Saedyn's expression changed again. The iciness of his eyes vanished. He just looked tired. Saedyn slumped down to a sitting position on the floor next to the door and pinched the bridge of his nose as if trying to ward away a headache. He took a shuddering breath, and when he spoke again, there was nothing of the previous coldness in his voice. "I don't know what would have happened if I were to use any more magic."
      "Our friends here would like you to explain what you've been doing with the night angels," Favian said lightly. "Do you feel up to telling them now that you're here? If not-"
      "I can talk." Saedyn brushed his white hair out of his eyes. "I owe all of you an explanation. What do you want to know?"
      "Why did they say that you betrayed them?" Lyria asked timidly.
      "It was part of my plan." Saedyn exhaled. He refused to make eye contact with anyone in the room. "We needed to get them on the same side as all of you and the day angels."
      "I'm honestly still surprised you believed the story my fellow night angels gave you about Saedyn wanting to take over Hali." The night angel from before stepped into the room. "Saedyn is the last person who would want to bring harm to anyone."
      Halimah blinked. "You told me you didn't know much about Saedyn. I guess that was a lie too, then."
      "No one was supposed to know about our plan except for Saedyn, the night angels, and us former gods," Thuc explained as he took a seat on the ground. Halimah, Ewen, Lyria, Maliq, and Fern followed his lead.
      "Saedyn's been preparing for this for a little over a year," Saedyn's mother said tiredly. "He was the one who convinced Thuc to take an apprentice long before we knew about his plan."
      "An apprentice?" Maliq asked. "Why an apprentice?"
      "Once the former gods were out of the picture, someone needed to go to the realm of the day angels," Saedyn answered tiredly. His amber eyes were blank. "They needed to be someone with strong enough magic in case things didn't go so smoothly. But then you showed that you had soul magic as well." The white-haired boy looked up at Halimah. "Like me, you're a wielder of soul. I knew that you would be the best choice to send to speak with the day angels. I knew that they wouldn't dare to hurt you." Saedyn leaned back against the wall and bleakly stared up at the ceiling. "If the day angels don't ally with the night angels, they'll stop at nothing to annihilate each other. And they won't care if Hali is caught in the crossfire."
      "You really don't care if everyone hates you?" Fern asked quietly.
      "I love my world," Saedyn said simply. "I love my family."
      Ewen arched a brow. "You're willing to sacrifice yourself?"
      "If I need to, I won't hesitate."
      "Now, now," Thuc said worriedly, "there's no need for anyone to be sacrificing themselves. After we prevent the day angels from annihilating the night angels, all of us will work together to clear Saedyn's name."
      They all turned to Saedyn, but the white-haired boy was still staring at the ceiling.
      "Using such large amounts of magical energy is quite agonizing, as you experienced for yourself," Professor Lethco murmured so only Halimah could hear. "At his age, it's a miracle Saedyn's still alive."
      Halimah flashed back to the cave where she had used her power to open the prophecy box. She shuddered as she recalled how her skin had boiled and froze until she passed out. That was how the white streak in her hair had come to be. Halimah cast another glance at Saedyn.
      "He's been using his magic to keep the fires around the other three temples burning," Favian said quietly. "The flames themselves don't do any harm to the temples but burn hot enough to keep any passersby away. And they attract the day angels' attention. As you've all probably figured out by now, soul magic is the only thing day angels fear-it's the only thing that can do any serious harm to them."
      "And void magic is the only thing that can do serious harm to us," the night angel said from where she stood on the side of the door opposite Saedyn. "Void magic and whatever kind of weapons the day angels have been working on. Word got out that they've been trying to simulate the effects of void. Fortunately, they still haven't found a true wielder of void," she finished in satisfaction. "Lucky for us, we have not one, but two wielders of soul."
      "We're coming up with a backup plan just in case things don't work out," Favian told them. "Maybe all of you will be able to help us out. Saedyn seems pretty confident in his own plan, but he shouldn't need to do this by himself. As of now, we're just hoping for the best and preparing for the worst."
      
~
      
      Later that night, Halimah found herself sitting next to Ewen and Lyria as everyone gathered around the large table in the dining hall for dinner. Saedyn was sitting between his parents, and his head was resting on the table in front of him. The night angel was nowhere to be seen, and Professor Lethco was talking animatedly with Gwenevieve and Rania.
      "So," Favian said as he leaned across the table to address Halimah, Ewen, Maliq, Lyria, and Fern, "we just received word from the day angels. They've decided to join the night angels."
      "That's wonderful!" Lyria exclaimed.
      "Yes"-Favian smiled as he turned to Saedyn-"this is very good news."
      Saedyn raised his head from the table. There was a crease between his brows, and he blinked slowly as if coming out of a daze. "They agreed to work with the night angels?"
      Thuc patted his son on the back. "They did. All we have to do now is figure out how to end the fighting completely."
      Suddenly Saedyn sat up straight. "I have a plan."
      
~

	Halimah had a hard time falling asleep that night. She rolled over in bed, and her eyes fell on where Professor Lethco was curled up across the room on a cushioned chair. Even though Halimah trusted the former gods, she still felt uneasy about the idea of spending the night alone in the unfamiliar temple.
	Eventually, sleep finally claimed her.
	Halimah opened her eyes to find herself floating in the void of stars. The night angel was drifting in the space in front of her.
	"I see you're back," Halimah said. "You were in Saedyn's head this whole time?"
	"That is correct."
	"Soul magic can counter void, right?"
	"Yes, why?"
	"If Saedyn's plan doesn't work . . . Someone's going to have to stop the day angels' void weapons."
	"You don't think Saedyn hasn't thought of that?" the woman said lightly. "Saedyn knows his plan has a very low success rate. When it comes to it, he's going to use the last of his magic to destroy the void weapons."
	"But that means that he'll die!"
	"The poor boy's already dying. He grows weaker with each passing day. His life force is fading. It took way too much out of him to decode what the prophecy needed him to do."
	"But-but he sounded so confident at dinner."
	"His parents were in the room." The night angel's eyes were sad. "He couldn't just tell them he was going to get himself killed."
	"I could use my magic," Halimah suggested. "I could stop the weapons."
	"You're not nearly strong enough, unlike Saedyn, who's had years of training with his soul magic."
	"No one should have to die. If it comes down to it, would you help me?"

    Chapter Fourteen

	Everyone in the Temple of Fire had been teleported by Professor Lethco to the summit of a snow-capped mountain a few miles away. Halimah sat in the snow with Ewen, Professor Lethco, Lyria, Maliq, and Fern. The six of them were bound by a thick chain of pulsing silver magic, and their backs were pressed together as they waited quietly. The former gods and their partners were tied up as well a short distance away.
      A strong wind whirled around them, sending snow flying in all directions. Halimah twisted her neck to watch Saedyn as he stood looking out over the mountains. The winged folk would show up any minute now. Everything was in place.
      The booming of hundreds of wings sounded in the distance. Halimah looked up just in time to watch the night angels and day angels descend from the sky. The night angels crowded on one side of the mountain, while the day angels crowded the other.
      Saedyn turned from where he had been looking out over the mountains. The coldness in his eyes was back, and all traces of exhaustion were gone as if it had never been there. "Hello," Saedyn said cooly as his amber eyes traveled over the winged folk.
      One of the night angels standing at the front of the crowd drew a sword of pure flame from the air and brandished it threateningly at the white-haired boy. "You have ten seconds to give us the former gods and the children," the night angel called.
      "And what if I don't give them to you?" Saedyn said in mild amusement.
      "We attack."
      "I wouldn't do that if I were you." Saedyn's amber eyes flashed. The chain of magic binding Halimah and the others flared and grew tighter.
      "Saedyn, was it?" a deep voice drawled from among the day angels. The sea of day angels parted to reveal the king. His feathered wings were covered in crystal-like armor, and his unbound silver-blue hair floated in the breeze behind him. "Hand over the former gods. Let's get this over with quickly."
      Saedyn frowned silkily at the king of the day angels. "I could end you right now if I so desired."
      The king of the day angels smiled, but there was a hint of nervousness in the way he took a step back. Then the king's navy eyes fell on Halimah.
      "I remember you," the king said.
      Halimah glared silently up at him.
      "Let us ask you again," a commanding female voice called from the crowd of night angels. "Free the former gods."
      The night angels parted like a wave to let the woman to the front.
      "That's the queen of the night angels," Professor Lethco said quietly. Halimah squinted as she tried to get a better look at the violet-winged woman. The queen had short-cropped hair and an authoritative presence that could be felt all the way from where Halimah was tied up.
      Neither the queen of the night angels nor the king of the day angels needed a crown to make their position clear.
      "Come and get them if you wish," Saedyn replied.
      The queen of the night angels flared her violet wings. "Have it your way." There was a tremendous boom as hundreds of winged folk took to the skies. Halimah squeezed her eyes shut as snow and wind pelted her in the face.
      The sky was full of violet and gray blurs as all the winged folk dove toward Saedyn. The white-haired boy just smiled. And then the world exploded in silver light.
      Halimah squeezed her eyes closed again as the light crashed over her with a radiance equal to that of the sun. Cries sounded from the skies as night angel and day angel alike were flung backward.
      "How can he still have that much magic?" Lyria whispered. "Earlier today he looked like he was going to collapse at any moment."
      The sky was alive with feathers as the winged folk countered Saedyn's attack. But the white-haired boy kept pummeling them with blast after blast of silver light.
      "Look!" Ewen said suddenly as he gestured with his head. "It's the king of the day angels!"
      Halimah craned her neck to watch the king of the day angels dodge Saedyn's magic before finally landing in front of the former gods. He examined the chain of pulsing silver light binding them with a faint frown on his face. A group of night angels flew down and landed next to the king. All of them cast him uneasy glances. Halimah couldn't hear what they were saying over the noise of the winged folk in the sky above, but it looked like the night angels had offered to help remove the chain. After all, soul magic wasn't fatal to them.
      Saedyn kept blasting the winged folk backward, but each time, the silver light dimmed. A blast hit the ground next to where the king of the day angels had landed, and he quickly took to the air, with the night angels following close behind. It was clear that Saedyn was growing weaker with every passing minute.
      Halimah watched wide-eyed as Saedyn swayed on the spot for a moment. But the moment passed and Saedyn returned to blasting the winged folk away.
      The sun had almost completely dropped from the sky, and the last of its fiery red light had melted into starry darkness. Then the queen of the night angels shot down like a bullet from the sky. Her wings a violet blur against the approaching night. A large number of night angels flanked her as they landed in a circle around the former gods.
      Then all of a sudden, a group of night angels flew over so quickly Halimah hadn't even noticed them. They surrounded Saedyn in seconds and bound his arms together with special magic-suppressing chains. Saedyn hissed and thrashed, but the night angels held him firmly. The chains binding Halimah to her friends vanished. Halimah didn't need to look to know that the one binding the former gods had disappeared as well.
      The queen of the night angels helped the former gods and their partners to their feet with a warm smile on her face. "You're free now," she said gently. Then she angeled her head in Saedyn's direction. "You should watch over this one."
      "Don't worry," Rania said as she leaned over to take Gwenevieve's hand. "We will."
      "Looks like the two of them have worked out their differences," Halimah said quietly to Ewen.
      The green-haired boy smiled. "I'm happy for them." Ewen's fingertips brushed Halimah's. Halimah blink in surprise, but then hesitantly twined her fingers through his. They were warm. Ewen gave her hand a squeeze.
      The queen of the night angels flapped her large violet wings and drifted over to where the king of the day angels was standing on the other side of the summit. The king tensed as the queen landed beside him.
      "What would you say to us keeping this truce?" the queen asked. "Let us put aside the years of being enemies. Let us start over as friends. We can work together." The queen of the night angels extended her hand, palm up, for the king of the day angels to take. "Let us start over."
      The king stared down at the queen's hands, his silver-blue hair waving behind him in the wind. All eyes were on them.
      "Sorry," the king of the day angels said at last. "But none of you night angels will be alive when the sun rises." Then the king whirled at the speed of light. He drew a sword of crackling magic from the air before swinging it straight at the queen of the night angels.
      Surprised, the queen darted to the side, but not fast enough. There was a terrible crunching noise as the king's sword plunged right through the queen's violet wings.
      Halimah watched in horror as the king twisted the blade deeper, and the magic of the blade turned the violet feathers to ash. The queen of the night angels screamed in pain as the king of the day angels violently yanked his sword out. Crimson blood sprayed. The queen of the night angels drew her own magical blade in an instant.
      Everyone was too shocked to do anything as the two rulers went head to head. Their blades clashed like thunder. The queen of the night angels was an impressive fighter. But the king of the day angels was just as good. The queen had already been weakened, and her ruined wings bled heavily onto the snow behind her.
      The former gods and their partners flared with light as they raised their arms, but then day angels appeared behind them and bound them from head to toe in magic-suppressing chains.
      A group of night angels rushed at the king, screaming angrily as they came to aid their queen. But another group of day angels flew up to engage them in a savage fight of flames and feathers.
      There was a blur of blue flame as the king of the night angels plunged his sword through the queen's torso and pinned her to the rocks. "You're going to love what I've prepared." The queen hissed, but the king just laughed as he continued, "I'll have to thank you for getting Saedyn out of the way for me. You didn't think we'd really ally with you, did you?" The king raised his arms to the heavens above. A blast of light shot into the sky and exploded in the air.
      Halimah slowly looked up, afraid of what she was going to see. Her eyes widened in horror as she beheld what looked like thousands of shooting stars flying at a rapid speed from the day angels' moon. And all of them were heading directly toward the night angels' moon.
      "Our weapons are full of void magic," the king of the day angels boasted with a mad gleam in his navy eyes. All the night angels gathered on the summit and took to the air. They howled with rage and misery as they charged toward the king. Without a glance at them, the king flung out an arm and blasted all the night angels out of the sky.
      The sky was on fire as silver streaked toward the night angels' moon. Soul magic. Soul magic could stop it. Halimah whirled around, but it looked as if Saedyn had come to the same conclusion. Somehow, the white-haired boy had broken free of the magic-suppressing chains and was now sprinting toward the edge of the mountain. Halimah's feet began to move of their own accord as she ran after him.
      "Wait!" Ewen's voice yelled from behind her. "Halimah!"
      But Halimah couldn't wait. Time was running out. If Saedyn used whatever remaining magic he had to stop the day angels' weapons, he would die. It had to be Halimah.
      Saedyn leaped off the side of the mountain. Instead of falling to his death, the white-haired boy began running up into the sky. Silver light flashed around his feet as he created platforms with each step.
      Halimah didn't let herself have a moment of hesitation as she hurled herself off the edge after him. She needed to keep running. And then she was moving upward into the sky. Silver flashed around her, but Halimah paid it no heed. The stars. She was going to touch the stars.
      "Halimah!" Ewen was screaming. He had stopped at the ledge of the mountain, unable to follow her any farther.
      "Saedyn!" Halimah yelled.
      The white-haired boy looked over his shoulder in surprise. "What are you doing?"
      "You're going to die if you use any more magic," Halimah shouted as the wind whipped her hair around her.
      Saedyn's amber eyes flickered with sadness. "I know."
      "Your family loves you!" Halimah cried. "You can't just leave them!"
      "You don't understand. It's because I love them so much that I'm willing to sacrifice myself."
      Halimah bit her lip. "I'm sorry about this." Halimah inhaled sharply, and the silver light flared brightly around her body. Saedyn's eyes widened in surprise as Halimah sent a blast of silver light at him. A second later, the white-haired boy was tumbling toward the summit of the mountain.
      Halimah continued to run up as the icy wind tore at her face. The stars flashed around her, guiding her forward. Then something caught her eyes. Toward the back of the trail of silver lights, some of the shooting stars were beginning to dip. They were heading down toward Hali.
      Halimah ran faster as her legs burned. Higher. Just a little higher.
      Then she stopped and turned to face the weapons head-on. The silver streaks grew brighter with each passing second.
      Halimah squeezed her eyes shut as she drew every inch of magic from inside her and flung it at the weapons. The impact almost sent her tumbling out of the air. But Halimah kept her balance. She was floating now-floating in the middle of the sky. Halimah flung her arms in front of her, channeling more and more and more energy at the void weapons. The night sky was illuminated with silver.
      Halimah's eyes widened as the weapons in the front began to melt away, disintegrating as they touched her soul magic. But there were thousands and thousands of missiles. And it was beginning to take a toll on her. Halimah started to panic. Her blood was starting to boil. Her skin started to freeze.
      Halimah kept channeling her magic at the weapons and expanded it so her silver light flared through the entire sky, destroying the weapons heading toward Hali.
      Pain. Halimah could barely breathe. But it was working.
      Then a little voice was whispering in her ear. "Halimah!" It was the night angel. "It looks like you're going to run out of power. Take my power, I know it's not much, but please use it."
      Suddenly the burning sensation decreased as Halimah felt a thrum of magic course through her. Thank you, Halimah silently thanked the winged woman as her head cleared.
      "You're welcome," the night angel's voice echoed. "And thank you."

    Chapter Fifteen

      Halimah was burning from the inside out, yet she hadn't even obliterated half of the weapons. There were still so many more. Black spots danced across her vision.
      No. She couldn't pass out.
      Screaming in a mixture of determination and pain, Halimah flung out even more magic. The silver light glowed brighter and brighter and brighter. The weapons were breaking apart-they were turning into powdery dust.
      Someone was howling in rage from the summit of the mountain miles away. The king of the day angels. But Halimah knew he wouldn't dare come up and stop her. Soul magic was fatal to day angels after all.
      A spike of agony shot through Halimah so thoroughly that she had to bite her tongue to keep from blacking out. Halimah's hair whipped into her face. She nearly blinked in surprise. It was white. All of it.
      Screaming through the pain until her throat was raw, Halimah blew through the last of her magic. It tore from her like a tidal wave and crashed into the remaining void weapons. Every last one of them had been turned to a fine powder.
      Then Halimah felt herself falling. She was so tired. So exhausted. The stars blurred past Halimah as she fell down, down, down. She was so far away from everyone on the summit.
      Halimah felt the wind rush past as the ground shot up to meet her. And then there was a rush of violet wings, and she was swept out of the sky. Through her blurred vision, Halimah could make out the flaming hair of a night angel.
      "You can thank me later," the night angel said softly. It was the night angel that Halimah had been talking to in her head.
      "Thank you," Halimah breathed. Her voice was raw.
      "Let's get you away from all of this." The night angel flapped her large feathered wings. But then there was an explosion of icy light. The king of the day angels had struck them down. They were both falling. Halimah felt herself tumbling from the night angel's arms. Everything was blurring. Halimah drew one final grain of magic out and flung it into the air. A beacon. Here! The light cried. Help!
      Halimah's limp fingers scraped the side of the rocks. Maybe she could grab on. No, she was too weak. Then someone grabbed her arm.
      Halimah looked up to find Ewen leaning over the side of the ledge. His hands gripped her arm firmly. "Hold on, Halimah!" Ewen called over the howling of the wind. His face was pale. Ewen pulled with all his might, but Halimah was still dangling in midair. "I'm not strong enough," Ewen panicked. "Professor! Help!"
      There was a flash of plum-colored light, and then two sets of magical hands were pulling Halimah up onto the powdery snow blanketing the mountain.
      Together, Ewen and Professor Lethco pulled Halimah onto solid ground. Halimah lay in the snow, gazing blankly at the star-filled sky above her. Ewen knelt beside her.
      "It's over," Ewen said gently as he took one of Halimah's hands in his own. "Halimah, are you alright?"
      Halimah just smiled. Everything was blurring. Then darkness finally swooped down to claim her.
      
~ 

	"You saved us all." It was the night angel.
	Halimah was floating in the void of stars. It was over. Then everything came rushing back to her. Halimah glanced down at her hair. All of it had turned white.
	"Thank you for saving me," Halimah said, still in a daze. "How can I ever repay you?"
	"You don't have to," the night angel said as she angled her head to the side. "You already did. You protected my home-my family and people. I'm forever grateful."
	"It's what anyone would have done."
	A faint smile played on the night angel's lips. "I'm just sorry I couldn't have been more of a help. After you passed out, things got crazy."
	"What?"
	"The king of the day angels was infuriated." The night angel closed her eyes as if reliving the previous events. "He tried to slaughter all of the night angels on the summit. There was blood everywhere. Luckily, the former gods were able to use their magic to force both sides to retreat."
      "What happened to the queen of the night angels?" Halimah asked quickly. "Is she alright?"
      "It would take more than a flaming sword to kill our queen. Your friends took it upon themselves to get the queen to safety. She'll be fully recovered in no time."
      "What happened to me? After I blacked out, I mean."
      "Your friends took you back to the Temple of Fire. Favian tried everything he could to heal you. I'm sorry."
      "Sorry?" Halimah blinked at the sadness in the night angel's eyes. "What do you have to be sorry about?"
      The night angel shook her head. Her expression was surprisingly soft. "I'll be happy to talk to you whenever you want. People are worried about you. I think it's time for you to wake up and tell them that you're fine." The night angel spread her violet wings, ready to take to the sky.
      "Wait," Halimah called.
      The night angel turned to look at Halimah over her shoulder.
      "I still don't know your name. What should I call you?"
      "My name," the night angel said slowly. Then she smiled. "My name is Sera."

~ 

	Halimah winced. Every inch of her was sore. Her head felt foggy. She couldn't see anything. Was it still night? How long had she been asleep?
	"Halimah!" Lyria's voice cried. "You're awake!"
	"Hi, Lyria." Halimah sat up in bed as she tried to squint through the dark to no avail.
	"It's good to have you back, Miss Samra," Professor Lethco's voice said happily.
	"Was I out for a long time?" Halimah asked, dreading the answer.
	"A whole week."
	That wasn't as bad as Halimah had thought. "Can we turn the lights on at least?"
	"The lights are on, Halimah," Ewen said quietly.
	"But I can't see you . . ." Halimah lifted a shaky hand to her face. She couldn't see her fingers. Everything was a dark and foggy blur.
      "Halimah," Ewen said gently. "You saved everyone."
      Halimah took a deep breath to steady her increasing heart rate. She could have died. But she hadn't-she had survived.
      "We're really sorry about your vision," Lyria said regretfully. "We tried everything we could."
      "It's alright, really," Halimah said genuinely. "I'm just happy I was able to get out alive."
      "We're happy, too," Ewen placed a hand on Halimah's shoulder. His touch was familiar and reassuring.
      
~ 

	Halimah sat next to Ewen and Professor Lethco in the dining hall later that evening. The former gods were sitting on the other side of the table, and all of them were talking in lowered voices. "The king of the day angels is angry," Thuc was saying. "He's bound to attack again. Next time, he'll come after us too."
      "Can you stop them the same way you did in the Second War?" Favian asked.
      "We had Yasvitha back then," Thuc said with a sigh. "We need four gods for that magic to work."
      "I can act as the fourth god," Halimah spoke up. Even though she couldn't see, she could practically feel all of their eyes turn to her.
      "Are you sure?" Gwenevieve's voice said.
      Halimah found herself smiling. "Hali is my home. I'll protect it with my life."

~ 

	After dinner, Halimah sat shoulder-to-shoulder with Ewen on one of the temple's balconies. The chilled wind bit at her face, but Halimah embraced it. "I think it will take a while to get used to this," Halimah commented.
	"You don't have to worry," Ewen said. "I promise I'll find a way for you to get your sight back."
	"Favian and the other former gods already tried everything they could. I heard that even Saedyn came by to try. Speaking of whom, how is he doing? I don't remember Saedyn being at dinner."
	"Ah," Ewen said with a heavy sigh, "Saedyn was injured worse than you. He was dying. I think you both were. Thankfully we had all three gods and their partners here to help you two make a recovery. I was really, really, worried about you, you know."
	"Ewen-" Halimah started as she turned her head at the sound of his voice. "Thank you for coming on this journey with me."
	"Halimah," Ewen said seriously, "I know my actions in the past weren't very admirable, but after getting to know you, I just want to continue hanging around you. I hope you can let me."
	Halimah smiled faintly as she rested her head on Ewen's shoulder. The green-haired boy wrapped a comforting arm around Halimah's back.

~ 

	From that point on, time felt as if it had sped up. Halimah, Ewen, and Professor Lethco returned to the Firefly District after bidding farewell to the former gods, their partners, Saedyn, Lyria, Maliq, and Fern.
      They had all decided it was best for Halimah to spend a couple of weeks recovering at the professor's house before she went anywhere, and now Halimah lay in the guest room.
      A knock sounded on the door. "Come in," Halimah called as she sat up.
	The door swung open with a creak, and light footsteps padded across the carpet. "Hello, Miss Samra."
	"Good morning, Professor." Halimah smiled as the cat leaped up to sit at the foot of her bed.
      "How are you feeling today?" Professor Lethco asked.
      "I'm feeling pretty good, actually."
"That's good to hear. Oh, it seems like Mr. Hanif has arrived."
      The sound of the front door opening and closing downstairs drifted up to the guest room. Shortly after, the door to the guest room opened as the green-haired boy entered the room. "Hi," Ewen said as he shut the door behind him.
      "Hi." Halimah gave a small wave in the direction of his voice.
      "Good morning, Mr. Hanif," Professor Lethco said. "I'll leave you two to talk."
      Once the cat was gone, Ewen took the professor's place at the foot of Halimah's bed. 
Halimah smiled faintly as Ewen twined his fingers through her own.
      
~ 

	Halimah spent the next few days walking with Ewen through the grassy fields of the Firefly District and along the serene beach.
      The green-haired boy held her hand at all times, guiding her carefully over uneven patches of ground. Halimah used her free hand to brush the dry grass with her fingertips. Today, they were at the beach again. Halimah dipped her hands into the cool ocean waves. She could smell the salt in the air-feel the soft winds blowing her unbound hair.
	Ewen laughed. "This really takes me back. I remember saving your life here."
	Halimah found herself laughing as well. "When you kiss me this time, will you also scowl and tell me it was a reluctant one?"
      "Of course not. Don't believe me? Then I'll tell you right now that I've fallen in love with you."

    Chapter Sixteen
One Year Later

	Ewen Hanif sat on a rock at the beach. It had been a year since Halimah had officially let her magic transition from soul to life. Even as a mortal, Halimah's magic now matched those of the former gods. With Halimah as the fourth god, everything seemed to fall into place. Some six months later, after finishing his semester and graduating from the academy, Ewen himself had become Halimah's partner. All these months he had searched far and wide to find a healer capable of restoring his partner's sight. But there had been no one. Ewen wasn't about to give up, though.
	"We better head back." Ewen stood up from the rock and brushed sand from his clothes. "Saedyn's going to arrive at the temple any minute."
	Halimah turned from where she was standing in the waves and smiled brightly.
      The two of them made their way along the beach hand in hand. When they reached the Temple of Life, Ewen helped Halimah up the crystalline steps. This was their home now.
      Saedyn was waiting for them in the entrance hall.
      "Hello," Halimah called.
      "Halimah, Ewen." Saedyn gave them a faint smile as he inclined his head politely in greeting. Ever since Halimah had taken up the position of acting goddess of life, Saedyn had taken it upon himself to visit every week. Even though Saedyn didn't say it, it was obvious he blamed himself for Halimah's lost sight. Saedyn wasn't the only one who visited constantly. Sera, the night angel Halimah had been communicating with, came to visit at least once a week as well.
      "The two of you can talk," Ewen said. "I've got a couple of errands to run."
      "Okay," Halimah squeezed Ewen's hand once before letting it go. Smiling, Ewen turned and headed back out of the Temple of Life.
      With a flash of green light, Ewen transported himself to Hali Central. He had put in multiple requests for the best healers the district had to offer. So far, Ewen had gotten no less than fifty different healers look at Halimah. Even though none of them had been able to figure out how to return Halimah's lost sight, Ewen wasn't going to stop looking.
      
~ 

	Ewen returned to the temple later that night to find Halimah sitting alone in the dining hall. Ewen slid into the seat next to his partner. "Were you waiting for me?"
      "I was." Halimah pushed a plate of food in front of Ewen. "I saved this for you."
      "Thank you."
      "Saedyn told me something interesting today," Halimah said lightly as Ewen ate. "He told me that he had been talking to Rania recently."
      "Does this have anything to do about the future?"
      Halimah nodded her head. "He told me that before the end of the month, the Wielder of Void will come to us."
      "Us?" Ewen said blankly. "Here? The Temple of Life?"
      Halimah looked up at the ceiling. "Rania also said that, apparently, this person will have good intentions."
      "So there is a wielder of void," Ewen said thoughtfully.
	For the next few days, Ewen found himself on edge. Part of him half expected the Wielder of Void to burst through the front door at any minute. Halimah had been more jumpy than usual too. But after a week passed and no one had broken down the doors, Ewen began to relax again.
	One morning, Ewen was working in the garden with Halimah. The two of them were talking quietly among themselves when the gentle tinkling of chimes sounded in the entrance hall. Someone was ringing the doorbell.
      With a quick word to Halimah that he would check who it was, Ewen got to his feet and made his way to the front doors. As he neared, Ewen heard a soft clucking noise coming from behind them. A chicken?
      Shaking his head in bewilderment, Ewen pulled open the doors.
      A scrawny boy around Ewen's age stood on the other side of the threshold with a brown-speckled chicken cradled tightly in his arms. The boy had hair the color of burnt wheat and was dressed in what looked like a mail carrier's outfit.
      "Hi!" the boy said in nervous excitement. "I heard that you were looking for a healer."
      The chicken the boy was holding gave a soft cluck.
      "Oh, this is Gloria," the boy said at the look of surprise on Ewen's face, "and my name's Crow Cledwyn."


    Chapter Seventeen
One Month Earlier

      Crow Cledwyn awoke to the sound of soft clucking. After blinking away sleep, he slowly opened his eyes to find his vision obscured by a mass of warm brown feathers.
      "Gloria!" Crow exclaimed as he rolled over to bury his head in his pillow. "It's too early." The sun hadn't risen yet, and the street outside his window was still bathed in darkness.
	Gloria clucked indignantly in response and began nipping at Crow's arm with her beak.
	Crow found himself laughing. "Okay, okay, I'm up now."
      After carefully setting the chicken to the side, Crow climbed out of bed and changed into his day clothes. As Crow finished pulling on his socks, Gloria nipped at his fingers in a way that meant the two of them better hurry up. In turn, Crow scooped Gloria up into his arms and hurried to the door of his tiny studio apartment. Gloria clucked in a way that said, I was trying to wake you up.
      Crow grabbed his letter-carrying bag from where he had hung it on the handle of the front door. Then, in one swift movement, he placed Gloria inside the bag and slung it over his shoulders. Crow took the stairs two at a time to the ground. His apartment was on the third floor of a four-story building a short distance from the heart of Hali Central.
      Crow ignored the strange looks people cast in his direction as he sprinted down the street. He had Gloria to thank for keeping him on top of things. Ten years ago, it was Gloria who found him. In fact, the newly hatched chick had followed Crow around for an entire day. Crow had wondered whether Gloria was lost and tried to help her find her way back home. But when there was no home to be found, Crow took the baby chick back to his apartment to care for.
      Crow arrived at the post office with five minutes to spare. "Good morning, Crow," Ms. Rosa called as Crow dashed past.
      "Good morning, Ms. Rosa!" Crow called back as he looked over his shoulder and nearly tripped over a stack of cardboard boxes. "I'm not late!"
      Ms. Rosa was the kind old lady who sat in the office every day magically sorting through the piles of mail. She was currently squinting through her thick glasses at the envelope floating in front of her. "I don't remember a time you were ever late." Ms. Rosa glanced around the heaps of overflowing envelopes levitating near her desk. "The boss told me to give these to you." The old lady pointed to a box of letters in the corner of the room. "These are yours for the day."
      "Go it!" Crow hurried over to the box and began transferring the letters into his bag. When he was done, he jumped to his feet and dashed back the way he had come. "Bye, Ms. Rosa!"
      
~
      
      The streets were slowly becoming more and more busy the farther the sun rose into the sky. Crow spent the day running around Hali Central delivering his letters. No one knew the city better than him-he had visited every part of it. Crow had let Gloria out of his bag hours ago, and the chicken now trailed behind at his feet.
      "I know we had to skip breakfast this morning," Crow said as he stroked Gloria's feathery head. The two of them had just sat down on a park bench for their lunch break. Even though the park was attracting more people as the lunch crowd increased, the empty space on the bench next to Crow remained unoccupied. People were casting looks in his direction, but Crow paid them no mind. "I just . . ." Crow trailed off as he split one of the pastries he bought in half and absently set the larger portion down in front of Gloria. "I was having that dream again."
      Gloria cocked her head to the side as she waited for Crow to continue.
      "I was standing in the middle of a field of green grass. And this girl with silver wings was there too. A day angel. She was in the sky flying. Wait-I know her name. I think it was Cora!"
      Gloria pecked at her pastry.
      "It couldn't just have been a dream." Crow gazed up at the white clouds wafting peacefully through the pale blue sky. "It can't be a coincidence that she keeps coming back. What do you think, Gloria?"
      Gloria just kept pecking away at her pastry.
      "I think it's strange too. Sometimes she speaks to me."
      Crow took a bite of his own pastry but found that he couldn't swallow. Sighing, Crow set his potion down in front of Gloria as well. The chicken looked at him and clucked in a way that said, This is why you're so scrawny, you know.
      Crow stroked Gloria's head before getting to his feet. But as he stood, the conversation of a group walking past caught his attention. "I still can't believe the night angels and day angels came down to the Crystal District to battle the former flame god's son," one man was saying.
      "Oh, it was terrible," a woman's voice piped up. "I thought the sky had exploded in a silver fire."
      Almost a year had passed since what had gone down on the mountains of the Crystal District, and yet it was still people's favorite thing to talk about. That day had been burned into everyone's heads. The night of the event, Crow had just gotten home from work and when the sky outside began flashing with pure silver light. He had stared out his window completely stunned before rushing onto his balcony to get a better view of what was happening. Blast after blast of silver light illuminated the mountaintops. Crow had remained on the balcony, too stunned to go back inside. That was when the sky exploded in silver fire.
      
~

	Crow was exhausted by the time he got back to his apartment late that night. He climbed the flights of stairs with much effort before searching through his bag for his keys. The apartment was dark, and Crow quickly lit a candle. He fumbled around in the dark for a good minute as he tried and failed to strike a match. Most people would use magic to light a candle or turn on a lamp, but Crow hadn't used magic in years. Once one of his co-workers had asked him why he never used magic. Crow responded that he didn't know how-which wasn't far from the truth.
	Ever since he was young, Crow had been left to fend for himself. And as a result, he had never gone to a proper school. There weren't many jobs in Hali Central that one could do without magic, but Crow had finally found an opening at the post office. Now he was just working until he could scrape enough money together to pursue a proper education.
	Crow sleepily poured a jar of preserved vegetables into a plate. This he brought over to the rickety table. "Dinner is ready," he called. Gloria clucked tiredly and flapped over to join him at the table. The chicken stared distastefully at the vegetables.
	"This is how we save money," Crow said with a shake of his head. "I know, I'm not fond of it either." As they ate, Crow looked out the window at the stars glittering in the inky sky beyond. His reflection stared back at him in the glass.
      Crow dropped his gaze. His co-workers claimed that he looked like a delinquent, and they weren't wrong either. Within the past year, Crow had gone through a series of growth spurts that had only accentuated the look. But he hadn't always looked this way. In fact, his co-workers claimed that he looked much more innocent when he was younger. Other people had seemed to think so as well and always pitied him when they found out he didn't live with his parents. It was dangerous for them to get too close, though, and Crow ultimately decided it was for the best if they kept their distance. But no matter how many times he sharply cut his hair, everything within-for the better or for the worse-remained the same.

~

	"Hello, Crow."
	Crow was standing in the middle of a grassy field. But when he looked closely, the image seemed to waver around the edges like smoke. "Hi, Cora."
	Cora gave Crow a small smile.
      "I told Gloria about you," Crow said mildly.
      "You did? What does Gloria think of me?"
      "I think she's grateful." Crow dropped his gaze. "I am too. I don't understand-why are you so nice to me?"
      Cora smiled sadly. "I've been trying to visit you more often, but things have been a little chaotic right now in the realm of the day angels. I have to be careful, too. I can't let the king find out about you."
      "So you're protecting me?"
      "Yes." Cora's lapis eyes seemed to stare into the very depths of Crow's hazel ones. "I'm doing everything in my power to keep you hidden."
      
~

	The following night, it was Crow's turn to lock up the post office after work. The building was quiet, and a stillness seemed to hang in the air. Anxious to leave, Crow walked over to the front door, but just as he placed his hand on the handle, a loud crash sounded from the back room.
	Without giving himself a moment's hesitation, Crow whirled around and sprinted toward the source of the noise. He flung open the door to find Ms. Rosa lying on the floor, her rickety chair in splinters around her.
	"Ms. Rosa!" Crow knelt next to the elderly woman. "Are you okay?" Crow sucked in a breath. Ms. Rosa's eyes were closed, and there was a bloody gash on her forehead. When the woman didn't respond, Crow began to panic. That was when he noticed blood dripping from the desk Ms. Rosa had been working on. Her chair must have collapsed, in turn sending the woman falling headfirst into the desk. She needed medical attention immediately, but it was late, and Crow was the only one in the post office.
      Gloria clucked worriedly from the doorway as Crow continued to panic. The nearest healer's clinic was miles away, and the blood wouldn't stop dripping from Ms. Rosa's forehead . . . A healer could use their magic to heal Ms. Rosa.
      An idea struck Crow. Just as he raised his hands, he paused. He hadn't used magic in years. He didn't even know if he still could. But he had to try.
      He was doing this for Ms. Rosa, Crow reminded himself as his hand shook. Crow hovered a hand over the gash on Ms. Rosa's forehead. After pushing everything else out of his mind, Crow took a deep breath as he closed his eyes.
      "Crow?" Cora's voice echoed in his head.
      "Cora?" Crow couldn't hide his surprise. "Please!" he begged as he got over his shock, "I need to heal her."
      "Alright," Cora said without any hesitation. "I'll guide you."
      Crow blinked as dark tendrils slowly began to spiral throughout the room. What was he doing? His heart rate was increasing too quickly. The faces of his parents flashed into his mind. He could see their horrified expressions as they beheld the dark magic.
      Crow drew even more magic from deep inside him. His palm glowed with darkness as he channeled his magic into stopping the flow of blood and clotting the wound.
      Heal, Crow begged his magic. Please heal her.
      Ever so slowly, Crow could see Ms. Rosa's skin begin to knit back together under his hand. Ignoring the way the tendrils sucked away the light as they danced through the room, Crow channeled even more of his magic. Finally, the glow faded from Crow's hand, and the light returned to the room. Crow slumped down against the desk, shaken. But he had done it: the gash on Ms. Rosa's forehead had closed completely.
      Warm feathers brushed Crow's fingers. "Hello, Gloria," Crow said tiredly. He took a shuddering breath. "I . . . my magic . . ."
      Gloria clucked softly as she pressed her head against Crow's hand.
      Suddenly there was the sound of something falling to the floor, and Crow's head snapped up to find one of his co-workers standing in the doorway.
      "Mr. Davan-" Crow jumped to his feet.
      "Crow." Mr. Davan just stared in shock. Then his expression contorted. "Crow, you use void magic!"
      "No!" Crow rapidly shook his head as Mr. Davan flung out a hand. Crow couldn't do anything but struggle as he was magically suspended in the air a moment later. "You must have seen it incorrectly! I was just trying to heal Ms. Ro-"
      "You could have killed her!" Mr. Davan bellowed. His words slurred together.
      Crow blinked. "Mr. Davan . . . have you been out drinking?"
      "Crow?" Ms. Rosa's voice had Crow quickly looking over at the woman.
      "Ms. Rosa!" Crow exclaimed. "You're okay!"
      "My goodness," Ms. Rosa said as she reached up to touch the spot where the gash had been on her forehead. "All I remember is that my chair broke, and then I hit my head on the desk . . ." She drew her hand away as she stared open-mouthed at the blood. Then her eyes traveled to Crow. "You-you healed me." She frowned as she looked between Crow and Mr. Davan. "My goodness, let the poor boy down."
      Mr. Davan glared but reluctantly lowered Crow back to the floor. "Ms. Rosa, this boy has evil magic. I saw it with my own eyes!"
      Ms. Rosa let out an amused laugh. "Nonsense. Mr. Davan, have you been drinking again? Did you get lost on the way home and wound up back at work instead?"
      Mr. Davan gave Crow one last suspicious look before he turned and marched out of the room.
      Crow hurried over to kneel next to Ms. Rosa. "I couldn't just let you lay there like that. I-"
      Ms. Rosa peered up at Crow through her shattered glasses. "Thank you, Crow."
      "You should probably get yourself some new glasses," Crow said softly.
      "You're right." Ms. Rosa frowned as she took off her glasses to examine the damage. Then her eyes widened. Ms. Rosa blinked slowly as her gaze traveled from her glasses to Crow.
      "What is it?" Crow asked worriedly. "Does something else hurt?"
      Ms. Rosa shook her head. "My dear boy! I can see you perfectly! In fact, I don't think I even need glasses anymore!"
      Crow blinked in confusion. "What?"
      "My vision," Ms. Rosa said in disbelief, "it's completely corrected itself." She shakily got to her feet. "You have some special magic, Crow."
      Crow quickly jumped up to steady the old woman. "Ms. Rosa, you should go home. I'll clean up here."
      Ms. Rosa nodded her head. But then suddenly she let out a gasp. "You're injured!"
      Crow's gaze instantly fell on where Ms. Rosa had rolled back the sleeve of his cardigan. "I'm fine," Crow said quickly as he let his arm fall from Ms. Rosa's grasp. He hastily rolled his sleeve back down to hide the numerous scars and gashes peppering his arm. "You should worry about yourself right now. Do you need someone to walk with you?"
      Ms. Rosa just gave Crow a worried look as she shook her head.
      
~

	That night, Crow quickly changed out of his work outfit and into his pajamas. The two moons of Hali were shining brightly outside the window. As Crow pulled the curtains shut, a metallic glint in the corner of the room caught his eye. Crow frowned to himself as he padded over to pick over the handheld knife lying there. Something flickered in his eyes as he stared at the blade, but it passed as he walked over to the kitchen counter and set the knife down in one of the empty drawers beneath it.
	After making his way back over to his bed, Crow yawned, flicked off the lamp on his nightstand, and finally burrowed under the covers.
	When Crow opened his eyes, darkness was pressing down all around him. In fact, it was so dark that he couldn't even see the hand he raised in front of his face. And that was when he heard the voices. They were just whispers-quiet enough that he had to strain his ears to make out what they were saying. As he made his way toward them, the darkness slowly began to lighten. Now he was standing in the living room of a small wooden house. Light filtered in between the branches of the towering trees outside. It was early afternoon, and a couple was sitting at the table: a man with hair the color of burnt wheat and a woman with hazel eyes.
      Crow turned his attention to the young boy sitting on the carpet in the middle of the room. The boy's eyes were wide in curiosity as he stared down at his hands. They were glowing with a vacuum-like darkness. Ever so slowly, tendrils of darkness began to snake their way through the room, dancing over the walls and floors.
      That was when Crow's mother screamed.
      Crow watched his younger self jump, and the darkness vanished from the room as quickly as it had appeared. But the damage had been done. Crow's mother wouldn't stop screaming. Her eyes were full of horror as she just stared at her son.
      Crow's father got to his feet and slowly walked over to the young Crow as if approaching a wild animal. "Get out."
	Young Crow was trembling from head to toe as his eyes filled with tears. "What did I do wrong?"
	"Get out of this house!" Crow's father roared. Then Crow was screaming as wind seemed to pelt him from all sides. All the air was gone. He couldn't breathe. Young Crow clawed at his throat as the air formed a vacuum around him.
      Then suddenly the air came rushing back, and Crow gasped for breath as he collapsed onto the floor in a daze. Suddenly he sat up. Those dark tendrils had filled the room again. His parents were staring at him in horror as the darkness crept toward them, and in that brief moment of shock, Crow ran. The door was too far away, and instead, Crow sprinted toward the window. Just as he tried to throw it open, a bolt of magic struck the glass next to his face. The breaking glass shredded his skin as he threw his arms up in front of his face.
      "I never want to see you again!" Crow's father bellowed as Crow finally managed to climb outside and tumbled onto the grass with a thud. "You wretched wielder of void!"

    Chapter Eighteen

	Crow awoke in a cold sweat. His skin was prickling. He could almost feel the shards of glass cutting into his flesh.
      Crow slowly sat up. He rolled out of bed and nearly collapsed as the room swam around him. With one hand against the wall, Crow stumbled toward the kitchen. In a blink, the handheld knife was in his hand. Just as he rolled up his sleeves, he paused. The scars scattered over his arm stared back at him.
      Gloria gave a squawk.
      The knife clattered to the ground as Crow looked at the chicken, startled. Crow slid to the floor but made no move to retrieve the knife. He had promised himself he would stop. As Gloria hopped over to comfort him, Crow pressed his hands over his face. When he finally calmed down, Crow glanced at the clock above his door. He still had about an hour until he usually woke up, but he was afraid he couldn't go back to sleep now even if he wanted to. Instead, he took a seat by the window, watching the stars dance outside until the sun came up and chased away the darkness with its golden radiance.
	
~

	When Crow arrived at work, the first thing he did was check on Ms. Rosa. The old woman was sitting in a new chair as she sorted through the stacks of letters on her desk.
      "How are you feeling?" Crow asked as he walked over.
	Ms. Rosa smiled as she looked up from her sorting. "Good as new."
	Then Crow lowered his voice as he glanced around the room. "Is Mr. Davan . . .?"
	Ms. Rosa lowered her voice as well. "I just spoke with him a few minutes ago. You don't have to worry-he doesn't remember anything from last night."
	Crow nodded in relief.
	"Ewen is looking for a healer," Ms. Rosa said after a long moment.
	"Ewen?" Crow said blankly. "Ewen who?"
      "The partner of the acting goddess of life," Ms. Rosa said knowingly.
      Now Crow remembered. Halimah Samra had been a wielder of soul. And a year ago, she took up the position of the acting goddess of life. Halimah had gone blind after the fight on the mountains, and now Ewen was searching for a healer who had the power to restore his partner's vision. "As much as I'd like to," Crow started, "I don't think I have the ability-"
	"Maybe you'll reconsider when you see the reward." Ms. Rosa leaned closer as she lowered her voice. "Ten hundred silver pieces!"
	"Ten hundred?"
	The old woman nodded. "You've always said you wanted to go to school. With this money, you'll definitely be able to afford all the books and equipment, and then some."
      "I'll give it a try," Crow said determinedly.

~

	After packing a couple of items from the few belongings he owned, Crow was ready for his journey to the Temple of Life. He had spoken with his boss, and the two of them came to the agreement that Crow could leave for a week. Before he left, Crow tried his best to make himself look more presentable. He got his hair evened out, and for the first time in a while, there was a smile on his face when he looked at himself in the mirror. If he succeeded, he'd be able to go to school.
	Crow scraped together the last of his monthly savings to pay a man with a cart to take him to the border of the Firefly District. From there, Crow made the rest of the journey on foot. Gloria clucked softly as they made their way through the tall fields of golden grass.
	Soon, Crow and Gloria arrived outside the Temple of Life. The temple was a gorgeous structure with large, arching windows, sitting half over the sparkling ocean and half over the sand.
      Gloria clucked happily and began hurrying toward the entrance of the temple. "Gloria!" Crow laughed as he ran after the chicken. "Wait up!"
      Crow finally managed to scoop the excited chicken into his arms outside the huge doors to the temple. Looking around, Crow's eyes landed on what appeared to be the doorbell. He gingerly pressed it, and the sound of soft chimes filled the air.
      Gloria flapped her wings, and Crow nearly dropped the chicken. "Gloria, please calm down! I can't hold you when you're so excited like this!"
      Then the doors to the temple opened. A boy only a few years older than Crow himself was standing in the doorway. He had vibrant green hair, and his brown eyes were wide with surprise as he beheld the chicken in Crow's arms.
      "Hi," Crow said. "I heard that you were looking for a healer." Gloria clucked softly in his arms. "Oh, this is Gloria"-he gestured with his head to the chicken-"and my name's Crow Cledwyn."
      "Ewen Hanif," the green-haired boy introduced himself. His face broke into a smile. "Please come this way. I'll have you wait in the dining hall. Halimah will be down in a couple of minutes."
      Ewen left Crow in the dining hall before heading back the way they had come. Crow took a seat at the table, and a few minutes later, Ewen returned. This time he was accompanied by a girl with thick white hair. Ewen helped the girl into the chair across from Crow before taking a seat beside her.
      "Hello," the girl said with a smile. "I'm Halimah."
      "I'm Crow. It's really great to meet you."
      Halimah's gold-flecked eyes stared unseeingly at some spot to the right of Crow. "I heard that you might be able to restore my vision."
      "I'll try my best," Crow said. The nervousness was creeping back into his voice.
      "It's alright if you can't," the acting goddess of life said gently. "Please don't push yourself too hard at my expense."
      Crow nodded, suddenly feeling much better. "I'll begin, then." He closed his eyes. How had he drawn the power from inside him again? He needed to replicate what he did the other day with Ms. Rosa.
      Ewen's gasp told Crow that the tendrils of darkness had begun to spiral through the room. Heal, Crow told the power. And then suddenly he was floating in the darkness.
      Crow waved his arms around only to collide with a large rocky shape. After a moment's hesitation, Crow placed a hand on the rock and let his magic seep inside it. Ever so slowly, the rock began to glow. As it grew even brighter, Crow could now make out the hundreds upon hundreds of rocks drifting in the darkness. Crow understood now. He had to light them up. One star at a time.
      Crow opened his eyes. "I think I can do it," he said breathlessly.
      "Thank you," Halimah breathed. "You're welcome to stay here at the Temple of Life as long as you need."
      Crow looked over at Ewen. The green-haired boy just gave him a smile and a knowing look that read, We knew you were a void wielder.

~

	That night, Crow found that he was too excited to go to sleep.
      The guest room was at least double the size of his entire apartment, and the huge bed was a hundred times more comfortable. Crow didn't know what sleeping on a cloud was like, but if he had to guess, it would certainly feel a lot like this.
      Gloria was already fast asleep on the pillow next to him. Crow had been able to light a handful of the stars in Halimah's consciousness before he became too exhausted to continue. Everyone had been right-magic took so much energy.

~

	"Guess what, Cora-I'm at the Temple of Life!"
	"That's wonderful." Cora smiled as she sat down across from Crow on the grass. "I'm assuming you've met Halimah. I've met her before too."
	"You have?"
	"Before she became an acting god, that is," Cora amended. "I took her to see the king of the day angels once."
	"Oh, Cora, I wanted to thank you for helping me heal Ms. Rosa."
	Cora smiled gently. "Void magic is one of the rarest forms of magic-and one of the most powerful along with soul magic. Just keep in mind every time you use your void magic, it puts you at risk of being spotted by the king of the day angels. Since you're only using small amounts, I've been able to mask it."
	"How do I know if I'm using too much?"
	"Don't push yourself. What makes void magic dangerous is that it doesn't take much training to master. As you are right now, you could probably do just as much with your magic as one of the former gods if you so desired."
      Crow frowned. "But I get tired really fast."
      "That's because you've hardly ever used your magic before."
      "What about soul magic though? Isn't soul void magic's counter?"
      "It is. In most cases, soul magic is used for good while void is used for destruction."
      "But I'm using my magic to heal people."
      "Void can be shaped to the wielder's will. And your will is for it to heal. A lot of past void wielders were blinded by the power they possessed and consumed by their magic, but I know your heart is in the right place."
      
~

	When Crow awoke the next morning, he walked downstairs to the dining hall with Gloria in his arms. Crow had agreed with Halimah and Ewen that he'd spend two hours every day before dinner to work on healing Halimah's sight. That meant he had most of the day to do whatever he liked. Crow rarely had this much free time, and he wasn't sure what he should do first.
	Suddenly there was the sound of someone clearing his throat. Crow looked down in surprise to find a gray cat staring up at him.
	"Oh, don't mind me," the cat said irritatedly. "Feel free to just walk past me."
      "I'm so sorry," Crow apologized hastily. "I didn't notice you sitting there."
      The cat flicked its tail distractedly. "Are you the healer?"
      Crow nodded his head. "I'm Crow Cledwyn. And this is Gloria." Crow set Gloria on the floor next to him.
      "Good day to you, Gloria."
      Gloria clucked in acknowledgment.
      "Er," Crow said awkwardly, "Gloria doesn't talk."
      "Oh," the cat said, a little put out. "Anyway, I'm Professor Christopher Lethco. It's a pleasure to make your acquaintance."
      "You're a professor?" Crow asked excitedly.
      "Indeed, Mr. Cledwyn," Professor Lethco said importantly. "I teach at the academy here in the Firefly District. I'm here today to see the acting goddess of life."
      The three of them made their way into the dining hall to find Halimah and Ewen already sitting at the long table. "Good morning," the acting goddess of life called from the head of the table.
      "Good morning, Halimah," Professor Lethco said.
      "Christopher!" Halimah said brightly. "Is that you? Thank you so much for stopping by."
      "Of course, of course," the professor said with a flick of his tail.
      After they finished breakfast, Crow found himself walking with the professor through the temple. Professor Lethco halted and turned to look up at Crow. "I heard that you're a wielder of void."
      "No," Crow said automatically. Then he sighed. "Kind of."
      "Kind of?"
      "I am a wielder of void," Crow amended. "I just haven't used my magic much."
      "Is there any reason why you don't?"
      "No, not really."
      

~

	Crow spent the morning walking up and down the sandy beach with Gloria. When he returned to the temple, he found Professor Lethco sitting next to the doors to the entrance. "Hello, Professor."
	The cat looked up at Crow. "Hello, Mr. Cledwyn. I was hoping to catch you coming in. Saedyn's in the dining hall. I thought I'd introduce you two. Both of you are wielders of rare magic, after all."
	"Saedyn? Saedyn as in the former flame god's son?"
	"Indeed."
      "I thought he went into hiding."
      The cat sighed. "That's what most people think."
      Crow curiously followed Professor Lethco into the dining hall where a boy around Crow's age was talking quietly with Halimah on the far side of the room. Both Halimah and the white-haired boy turned as Crow and the professor stopped in front of them.
      "Saedyn," the cat said, "this is Crow Cledwyn. Crow, this is Saedyn."
      Saedyn's eyes widened slightly as he looked at Crow. "You're a wielder of void." He had unbound white hair that fell just past his shoulders and eyes the color of amber. "I can feel my magic recoiling from you," Saedyn said softly. "Does yours do the same?"
      Crow looked at the other boy in confusion for a moment before he finally understood. Crow could feel the void magic inside him crawling. It was almost as if the magic knew there was a force in the room strong enough to oppose it.
      "It does," Crow said in equal quiet.
      "Sera has been informing me about the night angels," Saedyn said as he turned to address Halimah. "The queen has scouts keeping tabs on the day angels' movements. The king of the day angels appears to be up to something. If the king finds out about him"-Saedyn inclined his head in Crow's direction-"things will get ugly fast. Anyways, I should be going." Saedyn turned and brushed his white hair out of his eyes. "It was nice meeting you, Crow."
      "Wait," Crow said quickly. "I'd like to ask you a few things about your magic, if you don't mind."
      
~

	Crow was sitting in the grassy field under the vibrant blue sky. Cora was sitting in front of him, sunning her large silver wings. "I was wondering," Crow said after a while, "what is your relation to the king of the day angels?"
	"I hate him. It's hard not to when he was the one who killed my older brother."
	"The-the king killed your older brother?"
	Cora nodded solemnly. "I'm sure you're familiar with the story of the day angel and night angel who fell in love and tried to bring peace to the winged folk."
      Crow nodded, wide-eyed.
      "Well, my brother was the day angel in the story. The king didn't want peace, so he killed him."
      
~

	"Ewen, I have a favor to ask." Crow had just finished using his magic to help Halimah's vision. He was about to leave when he suddenly remembered something. "Do you think you could send a letter to my boss for me? I told her that I'd be back in a week, but with the way things look, I'll be away for much longer than that."
      "Alright," Ewen agreed. There was a puff of green smoke, and then paper and ink appeared in front of Crow.
      Five minutes later, Crow had finished his letter. He read over his work proudly before setting the letter off to the side to dry. Ewen looked down at the letter. "Almost everything on the page is spelled incorrectly. And your handwriting is ghastly."
      Crow's heart sank. "I've never been to school before."
      "I can help you write the letter," Halimah offered. "You can tell me the words, and I'll help you spell them."
      "Really?" Crow felt his spirits lift. "Thank you!"
      "Don't mention it," Halimah said with a smile. "The next time Professor Lethco comes to visit, I'll ask him if he has any availability to tutor you."
      Suddenly a flash of aqua light flooded in from the entrance hall. "Looks like Gwenevieve has arrived," Ewen noted. "You're welcome to come and say hello with us, Crow."
      Gwenevieve, the former goddess of the sea? Crow couldn't let this chance to meet one of the former gods slip. Crow quickly jumped to his feet and followed the two of them out of the room.
      A woman with long turquoise hair was standing in the middle of the entrance hall, her long gown rippling at her feet like ocean waves.
      "Good day, Gwenevieve," Halimah greeted the former sea god.
      "Likewise, Halimah," Gwenevieve replied.
      Halimah gestured in Crow's direction. "This is Crow."
      "Crow." Gwenevieve's golden eyes swept over Crow. "Wielder of Void."
      "Hello," Crow said timidly. "It's nice to meet you."
      
~

	The next day, Crow was drifting among the stars of Halimah's consciousness again. Each time he used his magic, he felt he could use more without tiring. As he moved from star to star, something snagged Crow's vision: a strand of silver was floating among the darkness. Curiously, Crow swam through the air toward it. Before Halimah had become the acting goddess of life, she had been a wielder of soul. The silver strand had to be made from soul magic.
      The closer Crow got to the strand, the further it seemed to move away. It was repelled by his magic.
      Crow took a deep breath as he reigned his void magic back in. Then ever so carefully, he reached out toward the thread. This time, it didn't drift out of reach. Crow wasn't sure what exactly he was doing as he closed his fingers around the thread, but he gently tucked the silver thread away for safekeeping.
	When night came, Crow went to bed early. After he opened his eyes in the void, Crow drew the silver thread from its hiding place. It floated in front of him-the only light in the surrounding darkness. Maybe it had been wrong for Crow to take it like that, but it didn't seem like Halimah had needed it. Or was even aware of it for that matter.
	Crow twined his fingers around the string and gave it a faint pull. Suddenly, he was falling. Down, down, down he went with the wind howling in his ears. Crow hit the ground with a thud and instinctively curled up as he lay there in a daze.
	The cold hit Crow a moment later. His teeth chattered in his skull, and it took him a few moments to realize he was lying in a mound of snow. He shakily got to his feet. The glowing silver thread was still clutched tightly in his fingers.
	The wind howled around him as it whipped the snow blanketing the ground into the air. It was night, and he was standing on the top of a mountain. The scene was blurred around the edges as if it were made from smoke.
	As Crow looked on, bursts of silver light exploded in the distance and illuminated the top of one of the mountains miles away. It was just like what had happened a year ago. Crow hurried through the snow, trying to get a closer look at the light.
	Just then, thousands of silver streaks shot into the sky. Panicking, Crow tugged at the string again. The world melted away as Crow tumbled through the air. His feet slammed into the ground moments later, and Crow fell backward into another drift of snow. Crow's mouth fell open in shock as he took in the scene before him: night angels and day angels were flying at each other as their echoing shrieks filled the air.
      Suddenly, a pair of arms grabbed Crow and pulled him up from the snow. Crow whirled around with wide eyes.
      "Crow?" Saedyn asked in surprise. "What are you doing here?" The white-haired boy didn't look angry-just confused. Unlike the other figures moving about, Saedyn was the only one who wasn't rippling like smoke.
      "I-" Crow started. "Where are we? What's going on?"
      "We're reliving the events that played out on the mountains of the Crystal District," Saedyn said as the wind swept his white hair in every direction. "Look, there's me."
      Crow turned in the direction Saedyn was pointing. Sure enough, a second Saedyn had just tumbled out of the air and landed on the snow with a thud. "What happened here?"
      "I got blasted out of the air by Halimah." Saedyn's amber eyes were sad as he explained. "She knew I was going to die if I used any more magic. We shouldn't stay here." Saedyn took hold again of Crow's arm, and the mountains melted away. The sounds of the fighting faded along with them until all that was left was a void of stars.
      Crow blinked as he looked around. "Where are we now?"
      "My head," Saedyn said simply as he let go of Crow's arm. "Would you like to tell me how you got here?"
      "This thread led me here." Crow showed Saedyn the glowing silver string wrapped around his hand. "I found it floating in the acting goddess of life's consciousness while I was working on healing her eyes."
      Saedyn sighed. "Is there any particular reason why you're here?"
      "Sorry. No, I was just curious about the thread . . ."
      "You should be more careful. For all you knew, you could have been walking straight into the hands of the day angels."
      Crow fell silent.
      "Beautiful, isn't it?" Saedyn said after a while.
      "What?" Crow asked, confused.
      "The void of stars."
      Crow raised his head to the twinkling pinpricks dancing in the surrounding darkness. "It is."
      "I'll admit it gets lonely here sometimes. It's nice not being alone here for a change." Crow watched Saedyn's face redden slightly as the white-haired boy dropped his gaze. "I'm sorry-I said too much."
      "Don't apologize," Crow said quickly. "I know what you mean. I'm usually in a void, too. But a void without stars. Just darkness."
      "Only darkness?"
      Crow nodded. "It used to scare me, but I'm slowly starting to get used to it."
      "Do you ever wonder what it would be like to be normal?" Saedyn looked at Crow. "To not have rare magic? I know I should feel special-honored even-but I don't. I just feel tired. Scared."
      Crow gazed upward at the stars. "I didn't choose to be a wielder of void."
      Saedyn sighed. "I completely understand."

    Chapter Nineteen

	Crow spent the afternoon working with Professor Lethco on his handwriting. It was difficult, but Crow was determined to learn.
      "Are you sure you don't want to take a break?" Professor Lethco asked. "Come, let's go take a walk along the beach."
	Before long, Crow was gazing out over the calm water. Professor Lethco walked over and sat down beside him. "You seem like you've got something on your mind, Mr. Cledwyn," the professor observed. "Let me guess, you found the link to the void of stars that the wielders of soul travel to."
      Crow stilled. "How did you know?"
      "I had a suspicion that you'd find it. Halimah herself can't travel to the void anymore, so I thought the link might be floating around."
	Crow spent the rest of the afternoon practicing his writing before moving on to work on Halimah's eyes. He went to bed early again that night and tugged on the silver thread. Like the previous night, he appeared on the snowy mountains of the Crystal District. Crow wrapped his arms around himself as the frosty winds blasted him full in the face.
      The sky was flashing with silver as Halimah and Saedyn ran higher and higher into the sky. Crow watched as Saedyn tumbled away from the stars before finally falling back to the snow with a soft thud. But something about Saedyn seemed different from the other memories reliving the battle above. This Saedyn wasn't leaving behind a hazy after-image like the rest of the memories.
      Crow quickly made his way through the snow. When he reached the white-haired boy, he dropped to his knees beside him. "Hey," Crow said.
      Saedyn blinked. "Crow?"
      "I don't think you want to lie in the snow all day." Crow offered a hand to help Saedyn to his feet. "It's cold."
      Saedyn smiled weakly as he took Crow's hand. "Thank you."
      "Did you notice me before I spoke to you?" Crow questioned as he followed Saedyn down the mountain and away from the fighting.
      "No." Saedyn's white hair was coated with ice as he shook his head. "It was supposed to be me. I was supposed to die."
      "What?"
      "The prophecy said so," Saedyn continued as he refused to meet Crow's gaze. "I knew from the start I was going to die. So why-why didn't I?"
      At a loss for words, Crow opened his mouth but then closed it again.
      "I was prepared to die. But Halimah stopped me. And now it's my fault she's blind." Saedyn fell silent.
      "I'm healing Halimah, though," Crow pointed out. "She'll have her vision back in no time."
      
~ 

	Crow spent the next day running along the beach with Gloria and working on writing with Professor Lethco. "Ah, yes," the cat was saying, "the acting goddess of life wanted me to tell you that Saedyn is coming to visit today."
	Crow's hand stilled over the letters he was writing. "He is?"
	Before Professor Lethco could respond, footsteps sounded, and Crow looked up as Halimah and Ewen entered the dining hall. "Hello," the acting goddess of life said cheerfully.
	"It seems like your lesson has been cut short," Professor Lethco remarked. "Remember to do your homework." Once the cat left, Crow hurried over to greet Halimah and Ewen.
      "We were wondering if you'd be able to start the healing earlier today," Ewen said. "Saedyn's going to be arriving soon."
      Crow nodded, and Halimah and Ewen sat down across the table from Crow.
      When Crow opened his eyes an hour later, he could sense someone else's presence before he even turned around. "Impressive," Saedyn said from where he was standing in front of the dining hall's entrance.
      "Saedyn!" Crow grinned.
      The white-haired boy smiled faintly. "Hello, Crow."
      Crow lowered his voice. "Do you think we could talk?"
      Sayden nodded.
      "Let's go talk somewhere else," Crow said as he glanced at where Halimah and Ewen were still chatting together in the dining hall. "How about we talk in my room?" When they reached his guest room, Crow took a seat on the floor in front of the large window, and Saedyn sat down across from him. "How long ago was it when you first found the prophecy?" Crow asked, getting straight to business.
      "I first came across it about two and a half years ago," Saedyn recounted. "The night angels were the ones who came to me and asked if there was anything I could do to help them. They told me about the prophecy and inquired if I was willing to get it."
      "What happened next?" Crow asked softly.
      Saedyn took a deep breath before continuing determinedly, "Opening the prophecy box was only the beginning. I still remember the first time I looked into the prophecy and asked it how I could protect everyone. It showed me my death."
