	During dinner, Crow listened to his tablemates discuss the best course of action to take regarding the king of the day angels. Professor Lethco had gone home for the night, and the temple was fairly quiet. Crow yawned, but then suddenly, a cold prickle shot through Crow's body.
      Confused, Crow looked around at the others at the table to see if they had felt the same thing. Halimah and Ewen were still talking, completely oblivious to the cold Crow had just felt. Crow felt Saedyn looking at him, and as their eyes met, it became clear that Saedyn had felt it too.
      "Halimah, Ewen," Saedyn interrupted them. His tone was serious. "There's been a disturbance in the air-in the flow of magic."
      Halimah's expression darkened as she jumped to her feet. "It must be the king of the day angels."
      Ewen jumped up as well. "Where?"
      "The same place as last time," Saedyn said grimly. "The mountains of the Crystal District."
      "I'll alert the former gods," the acting goddess of life said as she closed her eyes. She began to glow with a soft pink light. "The four of us will head there immediately."
      "I'll go too," Ewen declared.
      "Someone needs to stay and protect the temple," Halimah said worriedly.
      "I could stay here," Saedyn offered.
      Halimah gave Saedyn a grateful smile before she grabbed Ewen's hand, and the two of them vanished in a flash of light.
      
~ 

	Crow drifted through the void of stars as he waited for Saedyn to appear. He wasn't sure how much time had passed before he finally sensed the other boy's presence. Floating through the void, Crow made his way toward Saedyn's silvery glow. But when he finally found the white-haired boy, Crow froze. Saedyn was suspended in midair, with his eyes closed and hair billowing around him as if he were underwater. "Saedyn?" Crow asked hesitantly.
	Saedyn didn't respond. Crow floated over and grabbed hold of Saedyn's shoulders in an attempt to shake him awake, but Saedyn's head just lolled limply from side to side.
	Then Crow blinked as Saedyn started to fade away; his figure becoming more and more transparent. Suddenly Crow was struck with an idea. Opening his eyes, Crow forced himself out of the void. He was back in his room-back in his bed. It must have been the middle of the night. Careful not to disturb Gloria, Crow slipped out of his room, still in his pajamas.
	If he could find Saedyn and wake him up in the real world, the dream world would cease.	There were many guest rooms on the second floor of the temple, but Crow could sense Saedyn's magic. He knew where to find the white-haired boy.
	Crow sprinted the remaining distance to the guest room at the end of the hall. Without pausing to think, Crow pushed open the door and entered the room.
      Crow found Saedyn lying on the bed. He was still wearing the same outfit he had on during dinner, and he looked peaceful-despite the fact that his eyes were flickering behind their lids.
      Crow grabbed Saedyn's arm and shook him awake. "You're having a bad dream!"
      Saedyn's eyes fluttered open and he stared up at Crow in surprise. "Crow?"
      "You're awake." Relief flooded through Crow.
      "You didn't have to come." Saedyn sighed as he sat up to brush his white hair out of his face. "You came to the void of stars again?" the white-haired boy asked at last.
      Crow nodded. "Yes."
      Saedyn stood up to open the curtains. "Just a couple of years ago, I would have opened the curtains with magic. Now I can't bring myself to do so. I guess I still haven't fully recovered. I know anyone else would probably tell you off for meddling in their personal affairs, but I'm just really glad you got me out of the void. I'd rather not have to keep reliving the moment where my life force begins to ebb away."
      "Wait, you said your life force began to drain away. But was your eyesight affected?"
      "How did you know?" Saedyn's eyes widened. "My vision was significantly weaker after the events of the Crystal Mountains."
      "It was a lucky guess. I could fix it for you."
      "The same way you're healing Halimah's eyes?"
      Crow nodded. "Your hand," he instructed. "After some experimentation, I figured out that being in physical contact with the patient is ultimately more effective when channeling the magic."
      Saedyn extended his right hand, palm facing up. Crow reached out and hesitantly took the white-haired boy's hand in his own.
      The moment their fingers touched, Crow felt a jolt of static. It was almost as if his void magic didn't know what to do-it was reeling away and crackling with excitement at the same time. Crow tried his best to ignore it as he closed his eyes. Slowly, the room filled with dancing midnight tendrils.
	After what felt like hours, Crow finally drew himself back to reality. Dark tendrils were still dancing around the room when he opened his eyes, and as he watched, they gradually faded away in the brightness of the moonlight. Crow let go of Saedyn's hand. "Do you notice any difference?"
	"Yes." Saedyn's tone was surprised. "I can't believe it-I can see better already!"
      Crow smiled. "I'm glad I could help. I should probably get back to my room now before Gloria wakes up and finds that I'm missing. How about I work more on your eyes tomorrow?"
      "If you don't mind, I think I might take you up on that offer."
       
~

	When Crow awoke in the morning, he changed clothes before heading down to the dining hall for breakfast. As he neared the hall, Crow could make out voices talking quietly from within.
      After pausing at the doors, Crow tentatively peeked his head inside. Halimah and Ewen were back. The two of them were sitting at the head of the table, but they weren't alone: Gwenevieve was there too, along with a number of new faces.
	Crow quickly withdrew his head. He turned to retrace his steps and nearly collided with something furry on the ground. "Professor Lethco?" Crow exclaimed in a shocked whisper.
      "Good morning, Mr. Cledwyn," the cat said. His yellow-green eyes glowed as he looked up at Crow pointedly.
      "I'm so sorry!" Crow bowed his head apologetically. Then he dropped his voice, "The former gods are in there! All of them!"
      "Indeed." Professor Lethco nodded as he took a seat on the polished tiles. "Apparently they stopped a group of day angels last night from dropping some kind of weapon on the night angels."
      "The day angels are attacking again?"
      The cat sighed. "I'm here now to ask the former gods about the specifics." With a flick of his tail, Professor Lethco walked into the dining hall.
      Wait, Crow wanted to call after him. Crow turned to move away from the doors again, this time only to nearly walk headfirst into Saedyn. "I'm sorry," Crow apologized in embarrassment.
      "It's alright," Saedyn said mildly. "Are you not going into the dining hall?"
      "The former gods and their partners are there," Crow explained. "I don't want to interrupt their conversation."
      Saedyn smiled faintly. "Then I guess I probably shouldn't interrupt either. Would you care to take a walk outside?" Crow followed Saedyn out the front doors of the temple and onto the beach beyond. "My mother and father were in there," Saedyn told Crow as the two of them walked.
      "What are your parents like?" Crow asked as he watched the waves drift along the horizon.
      "My parents are kind," Saedyn said. "They don't want any harm to come to me, and they've done so much for me already. I want to help them protect the world they love too. What about yours?"
      "I don't exactly have parents anymore," Crow said quietly. Gloria brushed up against Crow's ankle from where she had been trailing behind.
      "I'm really sorry," Saedyn said sadly.
	Crow and Saedyn spent a good portion of the morning sitting with their backs against the large rocks at the far end of the beach. They talked about anything and everything that crossed their minds. "Were you homeschooled?" Crow decided to ask.
      "I was. With my magic being different, my parents took it upon themselves to teach me. I spent most of my childhood in the Temple of Fire. I didn't mind, though."
      Suddenly Saedyn inhaled sharply.
      "What is it?" Crow asked worriedly.
      The sleeve of Crow's cardigan had slipped up, and Saedyn was staring at the cuts and gashes that peaked out from beneath the sleeve. "Crow!" Saedyn exclaimed in horror. "What happened to you?"
      "This is nothing," Crow said as he hastily made to tug his sleeve back down.
      Saedyn shook his head in alarm. "This isn't nothing. Are you alright? Who did this to you?"
      Crow let out a sigh as he rolled his sleeve back up to show Saedyn his arm. "I did this to myself. I haven't exactly had the easiest time with my magic being the way it is, but I think I've slowly been getting better recently."
      Saedyn shook his head again, still horrified.
	After a while, Crow, Saedyn, and Gloria headed back to the Temple of Life.
      When lunchtime rolled around, Crow picked Gloria up from where she was jumping on the bed and made his way downstairs to the dining hall. Halfway down the staircase, Crow paused. Someone was speaking. A girl. Cautiously, Crow peered around the corner.
      Three people he had never seen before were standing in the middle of the entrance hall in front of Halimah and Ewen. The girl in the center was wearing a periwinkle summer dress and had long curly hair. She was chatting happily with Halimah. The boy to her left had long black hair, while the third girl had hair a shade of red so dark it could have passed for purple.
      Crow was debating whether he should go downstairs when Ewen spotted him. "Crow, would you like to introduce yourself to our guests?"
      "Oh, Crow," Halimah said, "I don't think you've met Lyria, Maliq, and Fern yet. The three of them are apprentices to the former gods."
      "I'm Lyria," the curly-haired girl said with a polite smile. "Nice to meet you."
      "Hi," Crow said timidly. "I'm Crow."
      "I'm Maliq," the boy with the long hair said.
      "And I'm Fern," the red-haired girl said shortly.
      Halimah smiled. "Come join us, Crow. We were just about to sit down for lunch."
      In the dining hall, Crow sat quietly between Maliq and Ewen. Footsteps sounded, and everyone turned to the doors of the entrance hall to watch the former gods and their partners step inside. There was silence as they settled themselves at the table until Gwenevieve said, "I think some introductions are in order."
      The woman next to the former sea goddess nodded. "My name's Raina. I'm Gwenevieve's partner."
	"I'm Favian," the dark-skinned man on the other side of Gwenevieve introduced himself. Favian was wearing a robe that seemed to flash with every color of the sky.
	"I've heard so much about you," Crow said as his words tumbled out in a rush. "About all of you former gods!"
	"I'm Thuc," the man sitting toward the end of the table spoke up, and his deep voice reverberated throughout the room. "This is my partner, Lianna." Thuc had long black hair and wore a robe of flaming orange. His partner, Lianna, was pale with warm eyes and a smile on her face. Saedyn sat between his parents and gave Crow a smile.
	"It's an honor to meet all of you," Crow said as he looked around the table in admiration.
	Favian's eyes twinkled. "And it's just as much of an honor for us to meet you, Wielder of Void."
	Lunch flew by quickly, and Crow found himself talking with everyone at the table. They were all very friendly, and he felt at ease by the end of the meal.
	Back in his room, Crow got to work finishing his assignment for Professor Lethco. The professor had instructed him to write a short story using the new words Crow had learned the previous day. A knock sounded on the door. "Who is it?"
	"Saedyn," Saedyn's voice called from the other side of the door. "I just wanted to stop by to say hello."
	Crow hurried over to open the door. "I've been writing a story for Professor Lethco," Crow explained as he beckoned Saedyn into the room.
	"Really?" Saedyn's amber eyes lit up. "If you don't mind sharing, I'd love to hear it."
      
~

	Crow floated through the stars of Halimah's consciousness, only vaguely aware that this time he had an audience. Crow opened his eyes and the dining hall reappeared around him. Clapping sounded, and Crow turned to find Lyria and Maliq applauding.
      "That was awesome!" Maliq said enthusiastically as Crow removed his hands from on top of Halimah's. "I've never seen void magic before!"
      "Yes!" Lyria agreed as her violet eyes sparkled. "It was beautiful."
      "Beautiful, but also dangerous," Fern said with a sigh.
      
~

	It was the middle of the night, and Gloria was sleeping on top of his chest. After carefully sitting up, Crow gently shook the chicken awake.
	Gloria clucked sleepily as she opened her eyes. "I'm going to go to Saedyn's room," Crow told her quietly. "I offered to help restore his vision again tonight."
	Gloria clucked twice as Crow slid out of bed.
      "You're asking why I'm doing this in the middle of the night?" Crow said as he padded over to the door. "Saedyn doesn't want his parents to know that anything is wrong with him. You're welcome to come along."
      When Crow reached the door to Saedyn's room, he knocked quietly. The door flew open almost immediately, and Saedyn beckoned him inside. "I'm really sorry we have to do this so late," Saedyn whispered as he shut the door behind Crow.
      "I don't mind." Crow set Gloria down on the floor. He took a seat too. "I brought Gloria along this time."
      The curtains were drawn back from the large window on the back wall of the room, and the glass was a reflective mirror as Saedyn lit the lamp on his desk. "Welcome, Gloria." Saedyn smiled faintly as he sat down across from Crow. The white-haired boy held out his hand, and Crow took it. Then Crow closed his eyes and let the darkness carry him to the void of stars.
    

    Chapter Twenty

	White spots bloomed across his vision from the lamplight, and Crow blinked as Saedyn's room came into focus. A moment later, exhaustion crashed into him like a wave. "All I need is a few more nights, and I'll have your sight completely restored," Crow said confidently.
	Saedyn didn't respond.
	Crow looked over only to find that Saedyn had fallen asleep. That was when Crow realized he was still holding Saedyn's hand. He tried to slowly unlace their fingers, but Saedyn wouldn't let go.
	Crow must have drifted off to sleep because the next time he opened his eyes, sunlight was streaming in through the window. Still groggy, Crow blinked once. Twice. Then everything came rushing back to him. Crow hastily sat up.
	"Good morning." Saedyn's voice brought Crow back to reality.
	"I'm so sorry! I-"
	Saedyn just smiled faintly. "You have nothing to apologize for. If anything, it was my fault for falling asleep first."
	Crow nodded, at a loss for words. "How's your vision?" he finally asked.
	"It's so much clearer already. Thank you."
	Crow found himself smiling back. "I'm glad."
      "I thought I might mention that last night was the first night ever where I didn't enter the void of stars. I just fell asleep and awoke in the morning without any visions at all."
      Crow furrowed his brow. "Come to think of it, I didn't awaken in my void either."
	"Oh." Saedyn frowned suddenly. "I think I forgot to tell you that I'm returning to the Temple of Fire today with my parents."
	"You're leaving?"
	"After lunch. But I'll be back next week. Would you like to take a walk along the beach again today? We still have plenty of time before lunch."
	Crow nodded eagerly.
      
~

	After Crow worked on Halimah's eyes, everyone at the temple sat down in the dining hall for dinner. Crow found himself talking with Lyria and Maliq again-which he didn't mind in the slightest, since both of them were lively and enthusiastic.
      "There's something I'd like to ask you three about," Crow said as he looked at his companions. "What's it like to go to school?"
      Lyria, Maliq, and Fern looked at him in surprise. Then to his relief, Lyria let out a giggle. "Up until recently, I was attending the magic academy in the Firefly District."
      "That's where Professor Lethco teaches," Crow recalled.
	Lyria nodded. "He was actually one of my professors. Ewen and Halimah used to go there too."
	Crow turned to Maliq and Fern. "What about you two?"
	"I go to school in the Sand Dance District," Maliq explained. "My favorite part about school is having the opportunity to meet new people and make friends."
	"I go to school in the Crystal District," Fern said when Crow turned to her. "I live for being able to learn new things every day."
	"It is pretty fun," Lyria agreed. "I bet you'd love school, Crow."
	When dinner was over, Crow headed to his room to go to bed.
	Crow opened his eyes to find himself standing in the infinite field of grass, the blue sky a peaceful ocean above. He didn't need to wait long as the day angel descended from the sky. "Hello, Crow," Cora said lightly.
      "Hello," Crow greeted her. "I was wondering if I could ask you a question. Last night was the first night I didn't enter the void," he explained. "And Saedyn said that he didn't enter his void either."
      Cora hummed thoughtfully. "I don't know if I mentioned or not that void and soul magic cancel each other out. If you two were in close proximity to each other, it would make sense that neither of you entered your respective voids. That aside, there's something I have to tell you." Cora's tone was grim. "The king of the day angels is planning to try to wipe out the night angels again. Last time his plan was to wipe out the entire night angel population in a series of quick and fatal blasts. But this time, I'm sure whatever method he's picked certainly won't be a quick and painless death for the night angels."
      "How much time do we have before he attacks?" Crow asked worriedly.
      "I'm not sure. The king's always been too suspicious of me to tell me anything important. I've been trying to do some investigating of my own, but as of now, I haven't been able to figure anything out."
      "How are we going to stop him?"
      Cora smiled sadly. "As long as the king doesn't get to you, there's still hope."
      
~

	Crow was back in the void.
      After tugging on the silver thread wrapped tightly around his fingers, Crow crossed the bridge into Saedyn's consciousness. Unfortunately, for the past few nights, Saedyn had been absent from the void of stars. Crow could assume that he had been speaking to the night angel because whenever that was the case, Crow wasn't able to communicate with him.
      As Crow floated among the stars, there was a flash of silver light. The darkness melted away to reveal the peak of a snow-capped mountain.
      It didn't take long for Crow to find Saedyn. He was tumbling through the air as he fell back down toward the mountain. Lifting a hand, Crow channeled his magic into a net. This was just a dream, after all. In a dream, he could control his magic in any way he wanted.
      The net of dancing dark tendrils flashed into existence and their shadows reached out to suck the light from the stars above. Saedyn hit the net with a soft thud. He blinked. "Crow?"
      Crow waved. Then after running over, Crow lowered the net to the ground and allowed Saedyn to climb to his feet. "I wasn't going to just let you fall."
      Saedyn laughed. "Thank you for catching me."
      Crow bowed dramatically before laughing as well.
      
~

	When Crow awoke the next morning, he changed into his mail carrier uniform and trudged downstairs for breakfast. Gloria hopped along at his feet. But as Crow neared the dining hall, he stopped as he witnessed a peculiar sight.
	Lyria, Maliq, and Fern were crouched next to the closed doors, their ears pressed against the wood. Crow walked over to the trio. "Good morning."
	Lyria and Maliq nearly jumped a foot into the air as they whirled around. "Crow!" Lyria said in a shocked whisper. "You nearly gave us a heart attack!"
	"I'm sorry," Crow whispered back apologetically.
      "The two of them are listening in on the conversation between the acting goddess of life and her night angel friend," Fern informed him. "I can't say I approve, but here we are now."
      "I think you'd probably be able to hear better if you went inside," Crow noted as he crouched down next to the doors as well.
      Only a couple of seconds had passed before the doors to the dining hall opened. Lyria, Maliq, and Fern hastily scrambled to their feet.
      Halimah, Ewen, and a night angel stood in the doorway. "Hello," Halimah said brightly.
      "Good morning," Lyria said with equal brightness. "I hope you don't think we were trying to eavesdrop."
      Halimah just laughed. "Next time just knock. You're all welcome to join our conversation."
      Crow noticed that the night angel at Halimah's side was watching him.
      "Hello, Wielder of Void," the night angel said with a smile.
      "Hi." Crow found himself shrinking backward. The night angel's piercing eyes seemed to stare into his very soul.
	"Saedyn's told me a lot about you," the night angel continued. "I want to thank you for looking after him."
	"You don't have to thank me," Crow said in surprise.
	The night angel sighed. "I do. I doubt anyone else would have found out about his eyesight, let alone try to fix it. My name's Sera, by the way."
	"I'm Crow." Crow smiled up at the night angel. "And this is Gloria." Crow gestured at the chicken in his arms.
	Sera raised her brows as her eyes fell on Gloria. "Why hello there, Gloria. I see you have lovely wings like me."
	Gloria clucked happily.

~

	A couple of days later, Crow was heading down to the dining hall for breakfast, Gloria hopping along at his feet.
      Lyria, Maliq, and Fern had left the previous morning. The trio bid Halimah, Ewen, and Crow farewell before departing for their respective temples. Now the temple was a lot quieter in their absence. After pushing open the doors to the dining hall, Crow's foot froze midair as he made to cross the threshold.
	Saedyn was sitting at the wooden table with a smile on his face. "Surprise."
	"Saedyn!" Crow exclaimed as he rushed over to the table. "When did you get here?"
      "I just got here less than an hour ago, actually."
      Gloria flapped her wings and clucked excitedly.
      "Gloria's happy you're back too," Crow translated.
      "Hello, Gloria," Saedyn said warmly as he reached out a hand to stroke the chicken's feathers.
	That night, Crow made his way across the hallway to Saedyn's room. Before he could even reach out a hand to knock, the door swung open, and Saedyn beckoned him inside. Crow set Gloria down on the floor as Saedyn quickly shut the door behind him. "Thank you for coming," the white-haired boy said.
	"Of course."
      Saedyn smiled faintly as he extended his hand for Crow to take.
      Crow placed his hand on top of the white-haired boy's, and the void of stars came into existence. He moved from star to star and found himself in front of the final one in no time. After placing his hand on the stone, Crow watched it glow and glow and glow.
      The following night, Crow found himself hurrying across the hallway to Saedyn's room. He didn't need to go there anymore, given that he had completely restored the white-haired boy's vision, but he found himself leaving his own room regardless.
      Quietly, Crow knocked on Saedyn's door. He didn't have to wait long as the door swung open. Saedyn stood in the doorway. His expression was only mildly surprised.
      "Hi," Crow said as he dropped his gaze to the floor. "I, uh . . ."
      Saedyn just smiled faintly as he beckoned Crow inside. After that, they talked for hours before Crow grew too tired to keep his eyes open anymore.
	When it came time for Saedyn to return to the Temple of Fire, Crow found himself missing the white-haired boy even before he departed. The next month was more of the same: lessons every afternoon with Professor Lethco and healing sessions with Halimah in the evenings. And then there was the ever-present worry hanging over their heads of what the king of the day angels was up to.
	When Saedyn visited the temple, the two of them would spend the day together walking along the beach and then talking in the white-haired boy's room at night.
	Lyria, Maliq, and Fern stopped by a few times during the month to say hello, and Halimah's vision was significantly improving. In fact, the acting goddess of life could now see in heavy blurs of color.
	Right now, Crow was sitting at the desk in his room as he worked on his assignments for Professor Lethco. Gloria had fallen asleep next to the glass inkwell, her head tucked under a wing. A short distance away, Saedyn was lying on Crow's bed, caught up in reading a novel. His white hair was slightly longer than it had been a month ago and kept falling into his amber eyes.
	Crow looked up from his writing to watch as Saedyn brushed loose strands of hair away from his face. His eyes never even left his book once.
      Suddenly, an alarmed voice rang through his head. "Crow!" It was Cora. Her voice was panicked. "I've discovered what the king's been working on all this time! It's Flames of Ice!"
      Flames of Ice? Crow thought back. What's that?
      "Us day angels specialize in ice-based magic the same way the night angels specialize in fire-based magic," Cora explained quickly. "It's a magical flame of pure ice-fire so cold it turns everything it touches to ice. The king plans to unleash it on the realm of the night angels! The fire is nearly unstoppable. Everyone and everything it touches will freeze. Then the king plans to fly in and use his magic to shatter the newly crystallized kingdom."
      Do you know when the king is going to unleash the flames?
      "No." Cora's voice was strained. "It's not done yet either. The king used a tremendous amount of power just to ignite a spark in the heart of the frozen flame. That's what that first disturbance you felt was-it took the king weeks to recover. There was also an attack on the night angels that day, but he never expected that to succeed. It was just a cover-up. Now he's been having the day angels slowly channel magic into flame now instead of all at once."
      So we just need to prevent him from using the flame?
      Cora sighed in defeat. "I don't know if there's anything we can do about it, but the queen of the night angels could probably stop the flame."
	The queen can stop it? Crow thought hopefully. What if we just warned her now? I know someone who can get the message across.
      "Please do." Cora's voice seemed to relax slightly.
      "Saedyn," Crow said as he jumped up from his chair.
      The white-haired boy looked up from his book, instantly concerned as he took note of Crow's tense figure. "What's the matter?"
      "Cora found out what the king of the day angels is planning. She said he's working on something called 'Flames of Ice.' Apparently it's a fire that can freeze whatever it touches. The king wants to freeze the entire realm of the night angels and then shatter it to pieces."
      Saedyn shook his head in alarm. "I'll tell Sera. We can't let that happen."
      "I know," Crow agreed as a slight tremor crept into his voice. "There has to be something we can do too, right? I mean, we have magics different from the others . . ."
      "Crow?" Saedyn asked with wide eyes as Crow trailed off.
      "I just had the craziest idea."
      Saedyn smiled faintly. "Let's hear it."
      Crow took a deep breath. "You're a wielder of soul. And soul magic is the one type of magic that is fatal to day angels."
      Saedyn angled his head to the side.
      "If we could somehow get you up to the king of the day angels . . . That way he won't be able to use his Flames of Ice."
      "Say we do go with that plan," Saedyn said slowly. "How would I even get into the realm of the day angels? The king knows to stay away from me at all costs." Then Saedyn's eyes widened in realization. "Are you going to get me up there?"
      "Since the king doesn't know about my existence yet, I feel like we could use that to our advantage."
      Saedyn frowned. "We'd need to think this through very carefully. There's no denying he'd be suspicious of you at first. I get the feeling you'd have to become someone the king could trust to even pull it off."
      "What do you want me to do?" Crow asked uncertainly.
	"I think the first thing we should work on is your expression," Saedyn said importantly. "You can tell a lot from a person by just looking at their eyes. You should try to make them cold. Like this." The white-haired boy closed his eyes for a moment. When he reopened them, the spark in them had vanished, and the amber glow was no longer warm. Instead, they had turned to ice. He blinked, and the ice melted away. "I always hate doing that," he said with a shudder.
      "I don't like that either," Crow said quietly.
      Saedyn smiled sadly. "Something tells me to get the king of the day angels to trust you, you're going to need to put on a dark persona like his."
      A knock sounded on the door. "Mr. Cledwyn?" Professor Lethco called from the hallway, "I've come to get you for our lesson."
      
~
      
      During dining, Crow couldn't help fidgeting. He and Saedyn had concluded that they should tell Halimah and Ewen about their plan the next time they saw them. Which just so happened to be now.
      Crow glanced over at Saedyn, and the white-haired boy turned to meet his eyes. Saedyn nodded slightly. After taking a breath, Crow cleared his throat to get his tablemates' attention. "Saedyn and I found out what the king of the day angels has been up to," Crow started as Halimah and Ewen turned to look at him. "We thought of a way to sneak into the realm of the day angels. But we need your help."
      "What exactly is the king up to?" Halimah said weakly.
      "The king's been creating Flames of Ice. He's going to try to attack the night angels again."

~

	Crow was sitting on the beach, gazing out over the calm water. Gloria sat on his lap, and her soft body was a warm ball of feathers.
	Footsteps sounded behind him, and Crow turned. For a moment, his eyes widened as he caught a glimpse of snowy-white hair. It was Halimah.
      The acting goddess of life smiled at Crow as her long gossamer dress flowed around her legs. "Hello, Crow."
      "Hello." Crow smiled tiredly as Halimah took a seat next to him.
      "You seem like you've got something on your mind," Halimah said lightly. Her long white hair rippled in the wind as she stroked Gloria's feathers.
      Crow turned back to the ocean. "Everything is just . . . It's kind of overwhelming all of a sudden."
      Halimah nodded sympathetically. "Just a year ago, I thought the same thing. Back then, as a wielder of soul, there were a lot of times when I felt overwhelmed as well. But I had friends-so many wonderful friends who supported me the entire way. Ewen, Professor Lethco, Lyria, Maliq, Fern, and everyone else. Friends are some of the most important people in life. They help us climb to our feet when we've fallen down-help us rise and triumph and succeed."
      Crow raised his head to look at Halimah, but the acting goddess of life was just staring over the ocean. Her cloudy eyes were bright with determination.
      "Keep your friends close, Crow. With them at your side, you can accomplish the impossible."
      
~

      At night, Crow would tug on the thread connecting him to Saedyn and meet the white-haired boy in the void of stars. From there, the two of them would look through Saedyn's memories of the Crystal Mountains and find all the moments with the king of the day angels for anything that might be able to help them.
      Fortunately, they still had plenty of time. Cora had been providing Crow with daily updates on the king's progress with the weapon and had predicted it would take the king a couple of months at the very least to commence an attack.
	That night, Crow was sitting next to Saedyn. The two of them silently sat on the white-haired boy's bed as they listened to the rain pattering on the temple roof. At some point in time they had joined hands, and how their linked hands rested on the blankets between them.

~
      
	Since the majority of their plan was going to take place at the Temple of Fire, the former gods had concluded that they should relocate everyone involved to said location. And that meant that Crow was going to go too.
	Crow was extremely excited about getting to see the legendary structure built into the side of one of the Crystal District's mountains in person. But that also meant that today was going to be Crow's last day at the Temple of Life. As Crow walked through the gleaming halls of the temple, he couldn't help but wonder if this would be the last time he'd ever be here.
      It was raining too much to walk along the beach, so Crow and Saedyn decided to go to the indoor garden instead. They sat on the grassy ground as the rain dripped down the sides of the glass walls outside. The pleasant fragrance of flowers filled the room, and Gloria clucked happily as Crow set her down next to him.
      "Are you afraid?" Saedyn asked quietly.
      "Yes," Crow admitted. "I am."
      Saedyn sighed. "I had the opportunity to face the king of the day angels in the past, but I was too scared to take it. At the time, my magic was unstable. I think I was scared to die at the hands of someone like the king."
      "I'm really happy you didn't die," Crow said softly. "If you died, I never would have gotten to meet you."
      
~

	Crow sat at the dining hall table across from Halimah. After placing his hands on top of the acting goddess's, Crow closed his eyes as he entered the void.
	Bright stars greeted him as he opened his eyes. The hundreds of lights were pulsing and flickering softly. But there were still hundreds of stars left to light back up.
	Drawing his magic up from deep inside him, Crow felt his determination and resolve grow. This was his magic. If he wanted to fix Halimah's vision fully, why could he do just that? And with that in mind, Crow released the grip on his magic, and everything exploded in a burst of roaring midnight.

    Chapter Twenty-One

	"Crow?"
      Crow opened his eyes to find Halimah staring at him. The clouds in her gold-flecked eyes had vanished entirely. She blinked once. Twice.
      "Halimah?" Ewen asked in concern.
      The acting goddess of life turned to look up at her partner. "I can see again," Halimah whispered. "I can see light and color, and-" Halimah looked back at Crow with wide eyes. "I can see you. Thank you."
      "Thank you," Ewen echoed.
      Crow nodded.
      "Well," Ewen said after a while, "I'll make sure to get the reward money to you before we depart for the Temple of Fire. You've earned it, Crow."
      The money! Crow had completely forgotten about that part of the agreement. "I-" Crow started. Something about taking the money felt wrong. He knew it was why he decided to come to the Temple of Life in the first place, but . . .
      "Don't." Ewen cut Crow off with a look. "Don't tell me that you won't accept the money."
      "Yes." Halimah nodded as she elbowed Ewen playfully. "We insist."

~

	Crow awoke early in the morning to pack his few belongings. Crow and Saedyn met Halimah and Ewen in the entrance hall as they prepared to depart. "We're going to teleport directly into the Temple of Fire's entrance hall," Halimah explained as heavy rain tapped loudly on the roof high above. The acting goddess of life closed her gold-flecked eyes, and pale pink light flared around her, engulfing the entire entrance hall.
      When the light faded, Crow blinked in awe. He was now standing in the entrance hall of a completely different temple. The walls were made from a red-orange stone that seemed to pulse and glow with living flames. Snow was falling outside the large arched windows, and the white was a stark contrast to the warm flames.
      Crow rushed over to the window. He pressed his hands against the frosted glass and looked out at the tiny flakes drifting about the crystal-like mountains. Saedyn walked over to join him with laughter dancing in his amber eyes. "You've never seen a snowfall before?"
      Crow shook his head.
      Just then, an overjoyed shriek had both Crow and Saedyn whirling around. Lyria had appeared in the entrance hall. "Halimah!" Lyria embraced the acting goddess of life tightly. "I heard about your vision! I'm so happy for you!"
      Maliq and Fern entered the entrance hall as well. Both of them had smiles on their faces.
      "Thank you, Lyria," Halimah said with a laugh. "I have Crow to thank."
      "Hello everyone," a new voice called. Crow looked over to watch as Thuc and Lianna walked over to join Halimah and Ewen in the center of the hall.
      "Mother, Father," Saedyn greeted them. "Crow and I are going to head upstairs first."
      Thuc smiled warmly. "Go ahead. Gwenevieve, Rania, and Favian are going to arrive sometime in the afternoon. Just be sure to meet us in the dining hall for dinner. We might even have a few other special guests joining us."
      Other guests? Crow didn't have time to dwell on it as Saedyn excitedly tugged on his arm and led him toward the staircase to the upper story of the Temple of Fire. "You want to go outside in the snow, right? It's always really cold outside. I'll find you something warmer to wear."
      Saedyn led Crow through a doorway on the second floor of the temple, and they entered what resembled a normal living room complete with a couch and many bookcases. More doors stood on the other side of the living room, and Saedyn guided them to the one on the far right. "This is my room," Saedyn explained.
      The first thing Crow observed about the room was the writing desk tucked away in one corner and the wardrobe in the other. The walls of the room were a fresh cream color, and Crow noticed that someone had hand-painted little flame-like designs in a red-orange paint around the windows.
      Saedyn went to the wardrobe and began rummaging around for a warm outfit. "Here you go," the white-haired boy said as he handed Crow a pair of trousers and a tunic. "While you change, I'll head downstairs to try to find you some snow boots." Giving Crow one last smile, Saedyn turned and hurried out of the room.
      Crow smiled faintly at the place where the white-haired boy had vanished. Then after setting down his bag, Crow changed into the outfit Saedyn had picked out for him. When he was done, Crow walked over to the mirror on the wardrobe door. "What do you think, Gloria?" Crow looked back over his shoulder to where the chicken had hopped out of his bag.
      Gloria clucked approvingly.
      
~

	After spending time hiking around in the snow, Crow and Saedyn made their way to the dining hall for dinner. When they arrived, Lyria, Maliq, and Fern were already sitting at the long table.
	"Hello!" Lyria's eyes sparkled as she smiled politely.
      Maliq saluted in their direction. "It's been a while since we've all sat down for dinner like this."
      Crow nodded in agreement as he and Saedyn slid into the chairs across from the trio. It had been quite a few weeks since they had all seen each other at the Temple of Life. Halimah and Ewen entered the room a few minutes later, closely followed by Gwenevieve and Rania.
      "Hello, Mr. Cledwyn," a familiar voice said from the floor. Crow looked down in surprise to find Professor Lethco.
      "Hello, Professor!"
      The cat leaped up onto the table with a flick of his furry tail. "Thuc and Lianna thought I might be useful, so they kindly asked me if I'd like to come along to their temple as well. Oh, speaking of whom, here they are right now."
      Turning around, Crow watched as the former flame god and his partner entered the hall. But they weren't alone; they were accompanied by a tall woman in flowing golden robes. Her violet hair was cropped in a pixie cut, and the violet feathered wings protruded out of her back.
      Crow heard Lyria inhale sharply from across the table. "It's the queen of the night angels!"
      Crow stared as the queen walked past and pulled up a seat next to Gwenevieve. The two women greet each other like old friends. Which they probably were, Crow concluded.
	After they finished eating and all of the plates were cleared away, Halimah and Saedyn began to explain the plan to the queen of the night angels. Crow sat quietly at Saedyn's side. Even though Crow was probably the most important one in the plan, he found that he didn't have much to say.
      "Crow." the queen of the night angels was looking right at him.
      Crow blinked.
      The queen just smiled. "It's been quite some time since I've been in the same room as a wielder of void."
      Crow nervously returned the smile.
      "On a more serious note, the king of the day angels is not someone who can easily be fooled."
      Crow swallowed. "I'm aware."
      "I'm sure that you're also aware that the king and I have a long history as well."
      Crow's eyes widened as he shook his head.
      The queen of the night angels sighed as she braced her arms on the table in front of her. "Before there were separate realms for the night angels and day angels, we all lived together as one united people. One day, a young male proposed that there should be someone who everyone would look up to-someone who would take it upon themself to protect everyone. His idea was accepted, and he was appointed king. He was clever beyond his years and his mind was his strongest weapon. Now that there was a king, it was only fitting for there to be someone at his side. A queen. And he wanted me.
      "But at the time, I was already in love with another male. A night angel. Things got bloody quickly, but the night angels stood by me. They wanted to see the king off the throne. They wanted me on it instead. When we couldn't agree, we separated. Us night angels went to one of Hali's moons, while the day angels to the other.
      "I knew the majority of the day angels rejected the king's ideas and philosophies, but they were too terrified about what he'd do to them if they rebelled." The queen ran a hand through her short hair. "Those poor day angels. Not a day goes by when I don't think about what I can be doing to help free them from the king. So when I heard about your plan, I knew I needed to help. If any of you ever need me at all, please, don't hesitate to ask."
      
~

	Crow awoke the next morning to the soft rays of the sunrise streaming in through the window. Yawning, he sat up in bed and rubbed the sleep from his eyes.
	Saedyn was asleep next to him, his white hair spilling over the pillow like fresh snow. The two of them had stayed up late discussing the plan, but Crow couldn't remember when he had fallen asleep. Timidly, Crow reached over to brush Saedyn's hair away from his face. The white-haired boy's eyelids fluttered open as he looked up at Crow.
	"I-I'm sorry." Crow dropped quickly his hand away.
	Saedyn just laughed as he sat up as well. "You don't need to apologize." Crow blinked as Saedyn caught his hand and gently rolled back the sleeve to examine the scars that covered Crow's arm. "When you were packing the other day," Saedyn said quietly, "I saw that knife in your bag."
	"I've stopped using it," Crow said truthfully. "I've come to realize my magic isn't a bad thing. I'm able to heal people after all."
	The two of them spent the majority of the day walking around the Temple of Fire. After dinner, Thuc surprised Crow by offering to teach him how to have better control over his magic.
      When night fell, Crow and Saedyn were back in the white-haired boy's room.
      "Hey," Crow said quietly. His voice echoed in the silence. "I realized that I've never seen you use your magic before."
      Saedyn hummed thoughtfully. "I think you're right-I don't even remember the last time I used my magic myself."
      "But you're still going to be able to blast the king of the day angels, right?"
      Saedyn sighed. "I can still do that. But I think I've come to associate my magic with pain. It did this to me, after all." He gestured to his hair. "My father actually came up with a way for me to channel my magic through a magical book to help mitigate fatigue, but I've been hesitant to do anything with my magic."
      Crow held out a hand as he sat up. "I don't think associating pain with your magic is going to be healthy. I don't think it's a bad idea to start working to change that."
      The white-haired boy seemed confused, but he took Crow's hand anyway.
      Crow adjusted their hands so their palms were pressed together and their fingers were lined up. "I'm going to use some of my void magic," Crow explained. "Don't worry-it's only going to be a little bit. If you feel comfortable, maybe you can try to match it with your soul magic."
      Saedyn nodded hesitantly.
      Exhaling slowly, Crow let his magic fill the room. Tendrils of darkness danced around his hands, and they lazily floated over to drift around Saedyn's as well. "Just try to use a little of your magic," Crow encouraged softly.
      The white-haired boy took a breath, and then suddenly the room was illuminated in silver. Crow could see Saedyn's wide eyes as they reflected the silver glow.
      "How do you feel?" Crow asked.
      Saedyn stared in amazement at the light. "Fine."
      The two of them were silent for some time as they watched the tendrils of darkness swirl around the pulsing silver stars.
      
~

	The following morning, Crow stood in the empty dining hall across from Thuc. Thuc had insisted that he teach Crow a few tricks that could come in handy while in the realm of the day angels.
      "Your magic is your friend," Thuc said knowingly as he lifted a hand. Flames burst into existence at his fingertips, and the magic streamed through the air like a golden banner.
      Crow watched open-mouthed as Thuc simultaneously shaped the flames into a snowflake, a cat, and a chicken. "Impressive!"
      Thuc smiled as the flames vanished. "The only limit of your magic is your imagination. If I'm being honest, I never thought I'd get the opportunity to meet a wielder of void, let alone teach one. You can't blame me if I'm a little excited."
      Crow let out a laugh. When he first came downstairs for the magic lesson, he hadn't known what to expect. But there was something calming about Thuc's energy.
      "Okay, let's see," Thuc said importantly. "The first thing you should know is how to create an alarm system just in case someone decides it might be particularly funny to try to sneak up on you." And so the former flame god spent the next hour showing Crow how to create and perfect an undetectable warning system. "I think you're getting the hang of it," Thuc said encouragingly as Crow placed a line of void over each of the dining hall's large windows. "This kind of magic doesn't stop people from getting in, but it will alert you of their presence. Anyways, I think that's enough for now. You should go take a break-you deserve it."
	Beaming, Crow bowed respectfully before hurrying out of the hall. This had been his first magic lesson.
	
~
	
	Over the next few days, Crow observed that Saedyn had started using his magic for small things like lighting lamps and candles. Saedyn had told Crow that he would try channeling his magic through the magical book, and now the book could always be seen with him.
	Crow spent the mornings and afternoons with Thuc learning more about his void magic. Crow was pleasantly surprised with himself at his ability to quickly pick up information and replicate Thuc's magic. But maybe that was just because the former flame god was such a good teacher: he was always patient and encouraging whenever he gave Crow instructions.
	Sera visited the Temple of Fire daily to report their progress to the queen of the night angels. While she didn't stick around long, the night angel made sure to greet Halimah and Saedyn each time she visited.
	Now currently sitting on the floor in Saedyn's room, Crow wondered what the realm of the night angels was like. Gloria sat on his lap and was clucking contentedly as she nipped at Crow's fingers.
	"We've come so far together, Gloria," Crow said softly.
	Gloria puffed out her feathers as she nuzzled her head against Crow's hand.
	"Saedyn will take good care of you when I'm away," Crow told the chicken. "Be good, okay?"

~

	The rest of the week flew by in a blur of activity, and before Crow knew it, the time to put their plan into action had arrived.
      Standing outside the Temple of Fire, Crow looked back at all his friends.
      Saedyn stepped forward. "Please stay safe."
      Crow offered him a smile. "I will. Take care of Gloria for me."
      "Are you ready, Mr. Cledwyn?" Professor Lethco asked from the snow-covered ground.
      Crow nodded, all too aware of his steadily increasing heart rate. "Ready."
      "Good," the cat said simply. Then the world disappeared in a flash of plum-colored light as Professor Lethco transported the two of them away from the temple.
      When the light cleared, Crow was standing in the middle of a dense forest. This was the Everglade District.
      "Good luck, Mr. Cledwyn," Professor Lethco said importantly. "I wish you the best." And with that said, the cat vanished in another flash of light.
      Crow stared blankly at the spot where the professor had been standing. The sounds of birds chirping floated toward him from the trees, and rays of afternoon sunlight filtered in through the leaf-covered branches.
      Crow turned around and set off through the trees. He could do this. In fact, Thuc had drawn a map and shown Crow the way to the small cabin tucked away between the trees. They had gone over the paths until Crow had them memorized by heart.
      Before long, Crow was standing in front of the wooden cabin. This was the place he was going to stay until the day angels found him. In exactly an hour, Cora would drop all the shields she had placed around Crow to hide his magic. And after that, it would only be a matter of time until the day angels swooped in to collect him for their king.
      Exhaling slowly, Crow stepped inside the cabin. The furniture was slightly worn, and the lamps flickered softly. It was made to look like Crow was living there for years.
      After what seemed like nothing short of an eternity, Cora's voice drifted through his head. "Okay, Crow. Are you ready? I'm going to drop the shields." Then her voice drifted to Crow again a moment later. "It's done. I'll see you at the castle. Good luck."
       
~

	Crow was waiting in the living room. It was late evening, and the sun had dropped completely from the sky. Everything was silent over the past week until the wards he had set up around the cabin were suddenly disturbed. Crow jumped to his feet, and his heart nearly jumped from his chest when a loud knock sounded at the door.
      Crow walked over to throw open the door.
      Two day angels stood on the porch: one male and one female. Their metallic silver wings glinted in the lamplight. "Wielder of Void," the female day angel said, "our king has found you at last."
      "He requests that you enlighten him with your presence," the male day angel added as he looked down at Crow.
      Crow met each of their gazes. "King? What does he want?"
      "He's been searching for you, Wielder of Void." The female day angel extended a hand toward Crow. "Come with us."
      "Why should I?"
      "If you worked for our king," the male day angel said, "you'd have the opportunity to do something great with your magic."
      Crow pretended to be considering their words. "Say I do come with you," he said slowly, "would there be a reward?"
      The female day angel nodded. "Yes: power."
      


    Chapter Twenty-Two

	Crow casually leaned against the wall as he eyed his surroundings. After he agreed to go see the king, the day angels teleported him to a large room and told him to wait for the king to call him inside.
	"Wielder of Void," a deep voice called from behind a pair of double doors. "Enter."
	Without giving himself a moment's hesitation, Crow pushed open the doors and stepped into the throne room.
	The entire room was cut from a polished white marble that reminded Crow eerily of bone. Large arches open to the elements lined the walls like windows, and stars twinkled lazily in the sky outside. At the back of the room, a gigantic throne sat on top of a glimmering staircase. But it was the person on the throne that Crow's eyes fell on immediately.
	The male had long unbound silver-blue hair, pale skin, and glittering navy eyes. He wore an intricately embroidered robe of frost-colored fabric. "Hello, Wielder of Void," the king purred. His voice rumbled through the room.
	"Your Majesty." Crow quickly bowed. The screaming in his head was so loud it was a miracle the king couldn't hear it. Crow's voice was screaming in his mind to get as far away from the king as he could. "I heard that you could give me power."
	Crow looked up to watch as a thin smile played across the king's face. "I can. Tell me, Wielder of Void, what is your name?"
	"Crow."
	"Crow," the king echoed. "How old are you, Crow?"
	"Sixteen."
	The king leaned against the arm of his chair as he rested his chin on his hand. "Already craving power at such a young age?"
	"My parents abandoned me as a child when they found out I was a wielder of void. Is it wrong for me to want revenge? Is it wrong for me to want the power to prove that I'm everything they feared I would be and more?"
	"Wrong?" Amusement flickered in the king's eyes. "Not in the slightest. I can help you, Crow."
      Crow forced himself to look intrigued. "Really?"
      "Yes," the king said simply. "I can help you-if you help me."
      "Deal."
      The king's navy eyes glittered. "I'm looking forward to working with you, Wielder of Void. Let's talk again tomorrow." As if on cue, the doors to the throne room opened, and a female day angel walked in. Her lapis eyes were downcast.
      Crow's heart nearly skipped a beat, but he didn't let it show on his face. Crow could see the king watching him out of the corner of his eye.
      "Cora," the king said lazily, "show Crow to his room."
      "Yes, Your Majesty." Cora shakily bowed her head. Then she turned back to Crow. "Come with me, Wielder of Void."
      Even as Crow followed Cora out of the throne room, he could feel the king's eyes on the back of his head. This had to be a test of some sort.
      They walked in silence, and the only sound was the echoing of their footsteps over the cold marble floor. Cora led Crow up a flight of stairs and down a long hallway. "These are the guest rooms," Cora said flatly. Even without the king around, they still needed to keep up the act. "You can stay in the first room on the left."
      Crow inclined his head as Cora walked over to hold the door open for him. As Crow entered the room, he paused in the doorway and pretended to examine the carvings etched into the frame. "Are you alright?" Crow whispered.
      "I should be asking you that," Cora whispered back. Her voice was so quiet it was nearly inaudible. "Don't worry about me right now-just be careful around the king." With that said, Cora bowed her head and closed the door.
      After carefully locking the door, Crow went a step further and used his magic to draw lines by the door and all of the windows. If anyone tried to come in, the magic would alert him.
      The guest room was fairly empty; the only furniture was the large bed in the middle of the room. Even as Crow sat down on the bed, his eyes kept darting back to the door. The silence roared in his ears. Paranoid. He hadn't even been at the castle for an hour, and he was already paranoid.
      
~

	Crow was floating in the dark void. Scared. Alone. Crow was about to let his fear take over when he remembered the glowing silver thread wrapped around his fingers. For a moment he just stared down at it. Then he tugged on the thread, and the void faded away to a star-filled infinity.
      "Crow," a voice called from somewhere behind him.
      Crow slowly turned around, and a smile grew on his face.
      
~

	"The king requests your presence in the dining hall," a male voice announced.
      Crow stepped out into the hallway where the day angel was waiting. Crow silently followed him down the marble halls. Before they reached the doors to the dining hall, the day angel whirled around with worried eyes. "Whatever the king wants you to do," the day angel said in a desperate whisper, "for the sake of the winged folk, please don't do it!"
      Completely caught off guard, Crow had to remember to keep his expression in check. "What do you mean?"
      The male dropped his voice even lower. "The king's going to try to use you to annihilate the night angels!"
      "You don't want that to happen?"
      The day angel shook his head sadly. "None of us want it to happen, but we can't oppose him out of fear of what he might do to our families."
      Crow looked at the day angel for a long moment before stepping around him and continuing into the dining hall.
      "Welcome, Crow." The king of the day angels was sitting at the head of a long stone table. "Have a seat." The king gestured lazily to the chair across from him at the opposite end of the table. After Crow sat down, the king continued, "I was wondering if you'd care to give me a display of your magic."
      "Right now?"
      The king nodded.
      Void exploded through the dining hall as the dark tendrils rocketed in all directions. The light filtering in from the windows seemed to be sucked away by a vacuum as shadows took their place. Crow let his magic flicker for a few more moments before reigning it back in. The sunlight returned to the room. "Was that satisfactory enough for you, Your Majesty?"
      The king nodded, and there was something triumphant flickering behind his cold eyes.
	Crow spent the rest of the week making sure that he did the exact same thing every day. In the mornings he would go down to breakfast. After breakfast, Crow would walk around the upper levels of the castle. Then he would go back down for dinner before finally heading back to his room for the night.
	All the while, he continued to communicate mentally with Cora and Saedyn. He would give them daily updates on what was happening-which really was not much. Fortunately, he didn't have to wait much longer. A few days later, Crow was back in the dining hall for breakfast. The king sat at the head of the table like usual, and his navy eyes glittered with malicious intent.
	"Crow," the king said after a while, "would you care to come with me? There is something I'd like to show you."
	"Alright." Crow put on a mask of mild interest as they stood from the table. They took staircase after staircase down into the very heart of the castle and only stopped when they reached a door cut from stone.
	The king signaled to the guards in front of it to open the door. The two day angels clapped their hands together, and the door swung open effortlessly. A single pedestal sat in the middle of the windowless chamber, with a pulsing crystal-like orb proudly displayed in the air above it. Even standing at a distance, Crow could practically feel the power radiating off it in waves.
      "What is that?" Crow feigned ignorance as he forced himself to take a step closer.
      "Careful now," the king said lazily. "This is dangerous magic. But it just so happens that the Flames of Ice isn't nearly the most powerful thing in this room."
      "What do you mean?" Crow asked as he kept his eyes glued to the light hovering in the air.
      "You," the king of the day angels said lightly. "Your magic is much more powerful than that little blue orb." The king's navy eyes glittered. "Everyone who's challenged me will fall very soon."
      Crow leaned casually against the wall to stop from shaking. "Isn't exterminating everyone a little much?"
      "You haven't killed anyone before, have you, Crow?"
      "No." Crow shook his head as he refused to back down from the king's stare.
      "Death," the king said quietly, "death is the ultimate power-the ability to control who lives and who dies." His was masked in shadow as he looked down at Crow. "You're still so young. When I was your age, I had just begun my conquest for power. You and I are cut from the same cloth, Wielder of Void."
      
~

	To his dismay, Crow was joined by the king of the day angels and his attendants at dinner that night. As they finished eating, a knock sounded on the dining hall doors. "Your Majesty," a hesitant voice called. "I have an update from the mines."
	The king frowned. "Enter."
	Crow blinked in surprise as the doors swung open. It was the male day angel who had begged Crow not to help the king the other day.
      The day angel stepped into the room with downcast eyes. "There were two suicides in the mines today," the day angel reported. "The overseers couldn't stop the night angels in time."
	The king got to his feet slowly. His face was face impassive. "Two suicides?"
	The day angel nodded shakily.
      "Our workforce is smaller than it's ever been as it is!"
      "Your Majesty, if you hadn't slaughtered half of them-"
      The king raised a hand, and there was a flash of light. The day angel was thrown to the ground. His shrieks of agony filled the hall. Crow watched in horror as the day angel's wings seemed to slowly bend inwards on themselves, and then suddenly a sickening crunching noise echoed through the room. Everyone fell silent as the crimson blood began to trickle from the day angel's broken wings.
      The king of the day angels let his hand fall back to his side. "As much as I would like to stick around, there are some matters that need my attention," the king said more to himself than the others in the room. And without a backward glance at the day angel on the floor, the king glided from the room with his attendants following close behind.
      Crow was left alone in the vast dining hall to stare down at the day angel. This had to be a test to see what Crow would do. He could feel eyes on his back.
      As casually as he could, Crow walked from the table to where the day angel lay in a trembling heap on the ground. Crow needed to help him. He couldn't just leave him there suffering.
      Scream, Crow mouthed. The day angel's eyes widened in surprise as Crow lifted a foot and placed it lightly on the male's back. As the day angel had been instructed, he let out a convincing shriek of pain.
      Drawing his void magic to him, Crow channeled it through where his foot came in contact with the day angel. Heal, Crow commanded his magic. Crow wasn't sure if he could mend the broken bones, but doing so would probably be too risky to begin with. The most he could do for the day angel at this point was to numb the pain until the male could be properly treated.
      After removing his foot, Crow turned and walked out of the hall without looking back. For the next hour or so, the day angel wouldn't be able to feel any pain.
      Crow continued on his way and didn't stop until he reached his room. After locking his door behind him, Crow redrew the void lines around the windows. Once he pulled all the curtains shut, Crow slumped to the floor, completely nauseated from what he had just witnessed.
      
~

	The sound of birds chirping filled the air, and Crow could feel the warm rays of the sun beating down on his face. He slowly opened his eyes to find that he was lying on the dirt-covered ground among shards of broken glass. He could see his family's cottage out of the corner of his eye.
      Squinting against the brightness, Crow twisted his head to examine his arm. He winced. Maybe he shouldn't have looked. But then Crow's eyes fell on his hand. His fingers were clenched tightly in a fist as if he had desperately tried to hold onto something.
      Opening his hand, Crow's eyes widened as he took in the delicate silver thread pulsing gently on top of his palm. The world melted away in a flash of silver, and when the light faded, Crow was floating in a void of stars.
      "Saedyn!" Crow exclaimed as the white-haired boy floated in front of him.
      Saedyn offered Crow a hand. "Would you care for a change of scenery?"
      Crow took his hand, and the void of stars faded away to a long stretch of beach. It was the beach next to the Temple of Life. Millions upon millions of stars twinkled playfully in the night sky above, and the smell of salt filled the air.
      "What do you think?" Saedyn smiled faintly as the ocean lapped up against the powdery sand just feet away.
      "Thank you for taking me here."
      The two of them walked along the shore until they reached the rocks at the end of the stretch. Crow lifted his head to the stars as he took in all the bursts of pink, purple, and indigo.
      "The ocean seems to stretch on infinitely, doesn't it?" Crow said after a while.
      "As infinite as it may seem, if you keep moving forward, you'll eventually end up back where you started."
      "And where's that?" Crow inquired sleepily.
      "Home."
      
~

	"The king requests your presence, Wielder of Void."
	Crow was led to the king's study, and now he was trying his best not to fidget in his seat. "I'm here, Your Majesty."
	The king turned to face Crow from where he was pacing in front of the large window on the back wall of the room. "Last night, my attendants informed me that you were quite interested in that servant in the dining hall." The king's navy eyes flickered.
	"It felt like I had power." Crow held the king's gaze. "You said you could give me power."
	"Power," the king said softly. "Power is what people like us live for." The king took a seat on the chair opposite from Crow, and for a brief moment, the sleeve of his intricately embroidered robe slipped back.
      Crow blinked. Faded cuts and scars peppered the king's arm. And on the pale skin of the king's inner arm, there was a dark spot that resembled a bruise. But it wasn't a bruise-the darkness seemed to have tainted the veins around the spot as well. "Your Majesty, what's that on your arm?"
      "These?" The king of the day angels looked down at his arm. "When you're alive as long as I've been, you're bound to make enemies and get injured at some point in time."
      Crow pretended to lose interest. "Alright."
      As the king absently rolled his sleeve back down, Crow's head spun. Liar, he wanted to call the king out. But as it was now, it would do Crow more good to drop the topic.
      The king of the day angels waved a lazy hand. "The real reason I called you here today is to talk about your role in my plan to annihilate the night angels."

    Chapter Twenty-Three

	Crow had been in the realm of the day angels for nearly a month now. And today was the day he, Saedyn, and Cora agreed on to put the second phase of their plan into motion.
	Crow made his way to the dining hall for breakfast. When he entered the great room, the king of the day angels was already sitting at the head of the table. Crow inclined his head before pulling up a chair at the opposite end of the long table. "Morning, Your Majesty."
	A thin smile played on the king's lips as he waved a hand. Plates of food appeared on the table. As Crow reached for a plate, he pretended to freeze. Lowering his hand, he slowly looked around the room. "Did you feel that, Your Majesty? There's a magic out there like mine."
      "The Wielder of Soul!" the king of the day angels hissed. "Do you know where he is?"
      "The blast came from directly below us. I think he's trying to enter the realm of the day angels."
      The king slowly got to his feet. "He will pay."
      "Your Majesty"-Crow stood as well-"allow me to take a group of day angels and cut him off."
      The king frowned as he considered Crow's offer. Then he nodded. "I'll summon a league of warriors immediately."
      Five minutes later, the doors to the dining hall flew open as ten heavily armored day angels entered the room. "The Wielder of Soul has come out of hiding at last," the king of the day angels primed his warriors. "You and the Wielder of Void will depart now to put an end to him."
      The armored day angels dropped to their knees in unison. "Yes, Your Majesty."
      The day angels took Crow with them as they descended down to the lands of Hali. When they landed, Crow observed his surroundings. He was back in the Everglade District, and the late morning sunlight filtered in through the leaf-covered branches high above. The familiar smell of pine and earth was prominent in the air.
      Crow turned to face the armored day angels. "The Wielder of Soul is in this forest. He couldn't have gone far. The eight of you spread out and search the forest around us." Crow gestured to a group of day angels. "The two of you come with me."
	Without waiting for a reply, Crow took off at a run into the dense trees. Dashing over rocks and roots, Crow drew closer and closer to Saedyn.
      A flash of brilliant silver light exploded in the trees next to Crow. Skidding to a stop, Crow lifted his eyes to the trees in front of him.
	Saedyn was sitting in the branches of a particularly tall tree, his white hair pulled back from his face in a ponytail. He gave Crow a wink.
	A loud clanking noise sounded as the two day angels tailing him finally burst out of the trees behind him. Putting on a mask of mild amusement, Crow angled his head to the side. "Hello, Wielder of Soul."
	"Wielder of Void." Saedyn inclined his head.
	"He wishes to kill our king," one of the day angels hissed. But both of them were extremely tense, and neither made any move to advance.
	"Is that so?" Crow said in mild amusement. "You want to kill the king?"
	Saedyn nodded. "I need to make everything right."
	"Prepare yourself, Wielder of Soul." Crow sent a blast of void magic at Saedyn. Saedyn skilfully countered the blast, and silver light flared through the trees. The moment the two magics hit each other, they vanished as if they had never existed. When used against each other instead of alongside each other, soul would cancel out void.
	Crow let his void magic ripple off him in waves and engulf the forest in shadow. Even the sky seemed to go dark as the tendrils of void greedily sucked away all the light. Then silver light flared again to illuminate the empty darkness with twinkling stars.
	Crow made a show of looking angry as he whirled on the day angels at his back. "Don't just stand there! Get him!"
	The two day angels exchanged a glance. "We can't get close to him-soul magic is fatal to us."
	Crow sent another wave of void at Saedyn. This time, the white-haired boy pretended to be caught by surprise and let the void crash into him. He tumbled out of the tree and hit the moss-covered ground with a thud. Saedyn was back on his feet in an instant to dart into a thicket of trees. Crow sprinted after him. He could sense the day angels trailing them from a distance.
	Reaching out with his magic, Crow crafted a trap and set it in Saedyn's path. A moment later, pulsing chains sprung up to wrap around the white-haired boy. Crow walked over as Saedyn struggled in vain to free himself. He reigned his void magic back to him, and the forest was flooded with light once more. "I think it's about time that you meet His Majesty," Crow said.
      Saedyn's eyes widened convincingly in horror. "I can't use my magic!"
      "That's right." Crow crouched down next to the white-haired boy. "My magic cancels yours out."
      Wingbeats sounded as all ten of the day angels landed on the ground behind Crow. "The Wielder of Soul has been detained," one of the day angels exclaimed. "Good work, Wielder of Void. You should kill him now!"
      Crow didn't take his eyes off Saedyn. "I think the king would reward me if I deliver you to him." He snapped his fingers, and Saedyn fell unconscious. After getting to his feet, Crow marched over to the awaiting day angels. "Let's take him back to the castle."
      "Are you sure?" one of the day angels asked hesitantly. "He won't wake up, will he?"
      "Of course he won't wake."
      Looking more reassured, two day angels walked over and gingerly picked Saedyn up. One of the day angels scooped Crow up as well, and then they took to the skies.
      
~

	Crow stood outside the doors to the throne room, carefully keeping Saedyn magically suspended in the air. The armored day angels stood against the wall, with their eyes glued on the white-haired boy as if he were a bomb that would go off at any moment.
	Holding his breath, Crow knocked on the door. "I've brought you a gift, Your Majesty."
	"Enter," the king's voice rumbled. The doors swung open on their own accord, and Crow stepped inside.
	The king of the day angels was sitting on his throne, with two attendants standing at the bottom of the staircase. Crow watched the king's navy eyes glint as they fell on Saedyn.
      "Your Majesty"-Crow bowed-"I present to you the Wielder of Soul."
	The king of the day angels slowly rose from his seat, and his robe swished around his feet as he made his way down the stairs.
	Crow waved a lazy hand, and Saedyn drifted over. Just a little closer, and then the king would be fully in the range of Saedyn's magic. "He didn't go down without a fight," Crow said. "But I managed to capture him in the end."
	"Perfect."
	"Oh, and one more thing, Your Majesty."
	"What is it, Crow?"
	Crow held the king's gaze, refusing to back down for a final time. "For the record, you and I are nothing alike."
      As if on cue, Saedyn's eyes snapped open. Crow jumped backward as the white-haired boy flung out his arms. The king's expression of shock was the last thing Crow saw before the room exploded in silver light.
	When the light faded, Crow slowly opened his eyes. He nearly staggered. A day angel was lying on the polished floor. But it wasn't the king.
      The king of the day angels was still standing. Crow's heart sank. The king had moved so swiftly that he had been able to throw one of his attendants in front of him to take the brunt of the blast.
      Saedyn threw another burst of light at the king, but it wasn't nearly as bright as the previous blast. The king conjured a shield, and the silver light ricocheted off. In a panic, Saedyn tried again. But Crow could see that the magic was already taking a toll on the white-haired boy.
      The king's eyes flashed. "So the two of you work together. I should have known." Just as the king raised his hands, turquoise light erupted through the throne room, and the king staggered backward. When the light cleared, Gwenevieve and Favian were standing in front of the king. The two former gods glanced back at Crow and Saedyn.
      A flash of pale pink light flooded the throne room as Halimah and Thuc appeared. Both of their eyes widened as they took in the scene before them.
      The king's features were painted with amusement. "All of the former gods are here in my castle . . ." Then his eyes fell on Halimah. "You," he hissed, "I should have killed you when I had the chance! Guards, capture them!"
      The door to the throne room burst open as the armored day angels waiting outside charged in. Favian was there in an instant to meet them with a flash of sky-blue light.
      Crow watched in horror as more armored day angels shot in through the glassless windows, diving at Gwenevieve and Halimah. Not only had both women depleted their magic by teleporting to the castle, but now they were terribly outnumbered. Crow lifted a trembling hand as he drew his void magic to him, but then something flashed in the corner of his vision. It was Thuc.
      "Saedyn, Crow," Thuc yelled as he sprinted toward them, "grab my hand!"
      "Father!" Saedyn cried, reaching his free hand toward the former flame god.
      Getting over his shock, Crow really did summon his void magic this time. Darkness exploded through the room, and the day angels were thrown backward. Their shrieks of outrage filled the air, but Crow knew they wouldn't stay down for long.
      Thuc reached his son and quickly took his hand. Gwenevieve, Halimah, and Favian used the opportunity to dash over as well. Gwenevieve grabbed Thuc's outstretched hand, Favian took the former sea goddess's, and then Halimah reached out to take the former sky god's. Just as Halimah's fingertips touched Favian's, the acting goddess of life was aggressively jerked back.
      Silver feathered wings flared as the king's remaining attendant took to the air with a thrashing Halimah in her arms. The goddess of life struggled, but her efforts were in vain. She had already been significantly weakened, and now the magic she threw at the day angel was easily batted away.
      "Halimah!" Thuc yelled.
      Favian sent a blast of light at the day angel holding Halimah captive, but a swarm of armored day angels swiftly rose up to deflect it. Ten day angels, twenty day angels, thirty, forty, fifty . . . Crow's head was spinning too much to count properly.
      "Go!" Halimah cried. Her voice was shrill. "Go!"
      The throne room melted away in a flash of fiery-red light. With the king's infuriated screams ringing in their ears, the group vanished from the castle.

    Chapter Twenty-Four

	The light cleared to reveal the interior of the Temple of Fire. Crow sank to the ground. He had failed. Not only had he failed himself, but he had also failed everyone else as well. And now Halimah had been captured by the king of the day angels.
	"Where's the king?" Lyria hurried over expectantly. But once she took a closer look at their expressions, the color drained from her face, and she clasped her hands over her mouth.
	Maliq's eyes widened as he and Fern rushed over to join Lyria. "What happened?"
	"What happened?" Ewen echoed as he scanned the group. "Where's Halimah?"
	Thuc sighed heavily. "Things didn't go exactly as planned."
	"Halimah's still up there?" Ewen asked, thunderstruck. "With the king?"
	Favian nodded regretfully. "She told us to go. With the situation being as it was, Thuc didn't have much of a choice."
	Ewen was still teetering between disbelief and shock before he angrily turned to Crow.
	Thuc held up a hand before Ewen could open his mouth. "No one's at fault here. It's the king himself who was quicker than we expected."
	"If anyone's at fault here," Saedyn said quietly as he looked up at Ewen, "it's me. I was the one who missed the shot."
	All Crow could do was stare at the ground. He couldn't bring himself to meet anyone's eyes.
	"How about the two of you go upstairs," Thuc suggested to Crow and Saedyn. "Lianna's in the hall outside. She's heard everything."
	Nodding, Saedyn gently helped Crow to his feet before guiding him out of the chamber. Crow could practically feel everyone's eyes on their retreating figures.
      The moment the doors swung shut, a blur of red-orange hurtled toward them. And to Crow's surprise, Lianna swept both of them into a tight embrace. "You have no idea how worried I was about you two." Lianna's voice shook. "When you took longer than we planned, I thought the worst had happened. But here you are now-safe and sound."
	"We failed," Crow whispered.
