	Lianna pulled back to hold Crow's gaze. "We can talk about what to do next later. Right now, I'm just happy the two of you are alive." Lianna released them a moment later with a sad smile on her face. "Rest. You need it."
	Saedyn gave his mother a nod before leading Crow up the staircase. When they reached Saedyn's room, excited clucking greeted them as Crow opened the door. "Gloria!" Crow dropped to his knees as the brown-speckled chicken jumped into his outstretched arms. Crow buried his face in Gloria's soft feathers. "I've missed you so much!"
	Gloria clucked happily.
	Saedyn rummaged through his closet for a clean outfit. "Here, I thought you might want to change. I'll go fetch something warm from the kitchen."
	Crow accepted the clothing and nodded his head as Saedyn left the room to give him some privacy. When Crow finished changing, he scooped Gloria into his arms and walked over to the window. Snow was falling outside. The view was so different from the stretch of empty sky outside the floating castle in the realm of the day angels. Just watching the snow seemed to have a calming effect. Crow absently stroked Gloria's feathers as the icy flakes danced lazily on the other side of the glass.
	Crow slowly placed his right hand on the window. The glass was cold. As Crow removed his hand, the sleeve of his tunic slipped down. He made to roll the sleeve back down, but he found his eyes lingering on the scars peppering his arms and the small bruise-like mark between his wrist and elbow. Crow stared at the mark for a good minute before finally pulling his sleeve over it.
      If only Crow had waited for a time when the king had been alone in the throne room, this could have been avoided. If only Crow had come up with an idea on how to lure the king's attendants away-to keep them busy. If something happened to Halimah, Crow would never forgive himself. This had been his plan. His idea. Had he really been so naive to think that it would have worked?
	The door to the bedroom opened, and Saedyn walked in with a steaming mug of tea in either hand. When he spotted Crow, the white-haired boy set down the mugs and hurried over. "This isn't your fault," Saedyn said determinedly. "We'll work out a plan tomorrow. And this time you won't be alone in the realm of the day angels." Saedyn just wrapped a reassuring arm around Crow's shoulders.
	Crow breathed in Saedyn's scent of crisp autumn leaves and snow. "I wasn't completely alone. Cora was there too . . ." Crow quickly looked at Saedyn. "Cora will protect Halimah, right? She'll keep her safe?"
	"If I were the king of the day angels, I would keep her alive so that she'd have to be rescued. He still needs you, Crow. He's waiting for you to fall back into his hands."

~

	The following night, Crow and Saedyn sat shoulder to shoulder on the floor across from the window. They were huddled under a warm blanket as they silently watched the snow dancing in the wind. As time went by, Crow couldn't seem to shake the feeling of guilt. Even so, that was in the past. He couldn't change what had happened. He had to live in the now, not the then. Had to live in the is, not the what-ifs.
	Gloria clucked softly as she brushed up against Crow's hand.
      Who was Crow living for? Well, that was easy. He was living for Saedyn and Gloria. Lyria, Maliq, and Fern. The former gods and their partners. The night angels and the day angels. The people of Hali. He was living for the people he loved. Love. That was it, Crow suddenly realized.
      The king of the day angels had never loved before, nor had he been loved before. He had never known the joy of the most powerful magic of them all. And Crow felt sorry for him.


    Chapter Twenty-Five

	Halimah winced as she sat up. The chill of the stone floor seeped right through her clothes. After brushing her white hair out of her eyes, Halimah looked around as everything slowly came into focus. The bars of her cell stared back at her. It was dark, and the only light came from a row of dimly lit lamps lining the walls outside her cell. Halimah lifted a hand to her face, and her eyes widened as she took in the shackles around her wrists.
      Halimah tried to summon her magic to her. Nothing happened, and she tried again with the same result. The chains were suppressing her magic. She fiddled with a strand of her hair. Was she terrified? Yes. Scared? Well, she'd be a fool if she wasn't.
      As she sat there, Halimah racked her brains for all of the information she had learned about the king and the realm of the day angels back at the academy. Soul magic was fatal to day angels. Even though she was no longer a wielder of soul, the king of the day angels wouldn't be able to tell that she had lost all of the magic, would he? If she could convince him that she could still perform soul magic . . . Well, there was no telling if he'd even come down to the dungeons to check on her. If the king had just left her here to rot, that was a different problem.
      Suddenly, the sound of footsteps sounded in the distance. In turn, Halimah climbed to her feet, ignoring the quivering of her knees. If it was the king of the day angels, she'd face him head-on.
      As the footsteps grew louder, Halimah realized that more than one person was approaching. Three people. Halimah had prided herself on her ability to judge how many people were in a room by their footsteps when she was blind.
      A moment later, the king of the day angels came into view. Like always, his long silver-blue hair was unbound, and the silky strands glowed in the lamplight as he stopped in front of the bars.
      Two female day angels stood behind the king. Halimah's heart began to pound twice as fast as she recognized the day angel who had dragged her away from the rest of her allies. When the day angel noticed Halimah's eyes on her, she sneered coldly.
      Halimah turned to look at the other day angel instead, and her jaw nearly dropped. The second female day angel had long inky hair and eyes the color of lapis. She was the one who had flown Halimah and Professor Lethco to the castle a year ago! If the day angel recognized her, the blank expression on her face didn't show it.
      "These two are my attendants," the king of the day angels said in mild amusement. "Usually I'd have someone else standing here"-he waved a lazy hand at the dark-haired day angel-"but currently he's still recovering from the damage one of your friends caused."
      Halimah held the king's gaze. "I'm sure you're aware that I used to be a Wielder of Soul."
      The king's smile faltered as he narrowed his eyes.
      "I wouldn't get close if I were you," Halimah said cooly.
      "You can't," the king said.
      Halimah forced herself to smile. "Come closer and you can find out for yourself."
      The king was smiling again, but there was an uncertainty in his eyes now. With a wave of his hand, the bars of Halimah's cell sank into the ground with a soft hiss. "Cora," the king said lazily, "why don't you go and greet our new friend?"
      Fear flickered in the day angel's lapis eyes as she took a cautious step forward.
      "Now, touch her arm," the king commanded.
      Slowly, the day angel reached out a trembling hand toward Halimah. The day angel placed a tentative finger on Halimah's lower arm, and Halimah nearly jumped in surprise as the dark-haired day angel sprung away, hissing as if she had been burned.
      For an instant, the king looked horrified.
      "She speaks the truth, Your Majesty," the female day angel panted as she clutched her finger.
      The king's eyes narrowed, and with a snap of his fingers, the bars of the cell violently shot back out of the ground. "You're lucky that you're no use to me dead." The king's metallic silver wings flared as he turned back to Halimah. "But once I get the Wielder of Void back, it will only be a matter of time before I destroy you and everything you hold dear."
      Once the king and his attendants were gone, Halimah slumped to the floor.
      
~

	Halimah awoke to the sound of footsteps in the distance, and she evened out her breathing in a pattern of heavy sleep.
      The footsteps drew closer and closer until they finally stopped outside her cell. The was a soft click as the bars slid open and another dull clank as someone set down a tray on the ground. The bars were back up almost immediately, and the footsteps retreated as quickly as they had come.
      Halimah waited another few minutes before opening her eyes. A small tray of food sat inside her cell next to her. Tentatively, Halimah reached out and picked up the loaf of bread. Her chains snaked across the ground as she pulled the tray closer to herself to examine its contents.
      One loaf of bread, a plate of some soggy-looking vegetables, and a bowl of water. Halimah picked up the plate of vegetables.
      The plate . . . As Halimah ran a finger on the plate, her heart rate quickened. Paper. Someone had stuck a note to the bottom of the plate.
      Gently, Halimah pried the piece of paper free from the plate. Then making sure that no one was watching, she unfolded it and held it up to the light.
      Goddess of Life, the note read, I am going to help you escape from the castle. There is a map of the castle on the back of this note. - Cora.
      Halimah's eyes lingered on the signature. She flipped the paper over a moment later and stared at the hand-drawn map of the castle. She located the throne room almost instantly and traced her way down the page to where Cora had labeled the dungeons. But as her eyes skimmed down the page, they stopped in a room in between the dungeons and the throne room.
      The keep of the Flames of Ice, Cora's neat scrawl read. Would the king still use it against the night angels? Either way, it was a powerful, powerful, weapon. If only there was a way for Halimah to steal it . . .

~

	The next time food was delivered, Halimah waited for the day angel's footsteps to vanish before excitedly pulling the tray over. She quickly found the new note stuck to the bottom of the plate and eagerly unfolded it.
	Once you're out of your cell, run to the throne room and jump. I will have allies stationed below to fly you to safety. There is a key to unlock your chains inside the bread. I advise you to keep one chain on you while you make your escape. Magic-suppressing chains don't only make your magic unusable, they also hide the presence of your magic from others. If the king senses your magic, he'll be able to find your location instantly.
	Once you unlock one of the shackles, wait for your magic to replenish. When you're ready, wait for your next food delivery. I'll cause a distraction to keep the king and the other guards away from you, but you'll have to be quick. - Cora.
	
    Chapter Twenty-Six

	Crow sat quietly at the dining hall table as he listened to the heated debate between the former gods. Snow was falling heavily outside the large windows lining the walls of the dining hall. It had already been three days since Halimah had been captured, and none of them had been able to come up with a plan. Whenever someone proposed a new idea, the flaws were pointed out almost immediately and it was back to the drawing board.
	"Our queen's offer to help still stands," Sera spoke up from where she sat with her arms crossed over her chest. Her violet feathered wings were folded neatly behind her, and she had come to the temple in the queen's stead to try and help out.
	"That is very kind," Gwenevieve said as she turned to the night angel, "but I think it would be for the best if the queen stayed in her realm. The king of the day angels could decide to attack at any moment. Someone needs to be able to protect the night angels if that happens."
      Lyria, Maliq, and Fern were sitting across from Crow and Saedyn, and the trio kept a low profile as they let the former gods and their partners talk. So far, Crow hadn't contributed anything to the table either. His last plan had been a disaster, and he wasn't sure if he'd be able to stomach a repeat of the events that had played out.
	Eventually, Thuc stood from his seat at the head of the table and signaled the end of their meeting. As Crow and Saedyn made their way out into the entrance hall, Crow noticed Ewen pacing back and forth. After silently pointing this out to Saedyn, the two of them made their way over to the green-haired boy.
	"Hello," Ewen said as they approached.
      "Hello," Crow greeted him with a friendly smile.
      Ewen just frowned. "Look, you don't have to pretend that everything is alright." He sighed and turned to look out one of the large windows as if he could see all the way to the realm of the day angels. "I just want her to return safely."
      "We know," Crow said sadly.

~
      
      "Crow," Cora's voice called through the darkness of the void.
      Crow squinted. "Where are you?"
      "I can't stay long," Cora said quickly. "The king has his attendants watching my every movement. I can't use too much magic either. That's why we're not in the field like usual."
      "Do you know if Halimah is okay?"
      "Halimah is safe for now."
      "Listen, the former gods are working on a plan to rescue her."
      "That's what the king hoped for." Cora's tone was worried. "He wants you back, Crow. He can't complete his plan without your void magic, so he's using Halimah as bait. You can let the others come, but you should stay on the ground where it's safe."
      Crow opened his mouth to respond, but Cora was gone.
    

    Chapter Twenty-Seven

	Halimah's magic had grown tremendously over the past few days. The waiting was by far the worst part, and after what felt like nothing short of an eternity, Halimah's ears picked up the sound of approaching footsteps.
      A male day angel stopped outside the bars of Halimah's cell. With a flick of his hand, the bars retracted, and he leaned down to set the tray of food on the ground. The moment the tray touched the floor, Halimah sprung into action. After leaping out of the cell, Halimah whirled around. Pink light flared, and the day angel fell over, unconscious.
	Halimah quickly dragged the day angel into the cell. Then with a wave of her hand, the bars sprung back into place. Without looking back Halimah sprinted down the hall. There were more day angels ahead, and her magic stealthily knocked them out.
      Halimah hurried up the stairs. The world grew brighter and brighter the higher she ascended. Pushing open the door at the top of the stairs, Halimah stumbled out into the hall beyond. Tall windows lined the walls, and the night sky sparkled brightly outside.
      Just like she had seen on the map, Halimah ran down the hall before turning left. The Flames of Ice was only a few flights of stairs ahead. Rounding the corner, Halimah nearly crashed into a pair of stunned-looking day angels. The moment the day angels realized what was going on, they drew blades of magic from the air and lunged at her.
      As Halimah dodged the swinging blades, her eyes fell on the panels on either side of the door. Two day angels needed to put their hands there to open it. So once Halimah rendered the day angels unconscious, she carefully levitated them with her magic and pressed their hands to the panels.
      There was a rumbling as the stone door swung open. The room inside was small, and the only light came from a pulsing orb levitating above a pedestal. The orb was the size of a small rock and the color of a freshly cut sapphire.
      Halimah created a vacuum with her magic and used it to snatch the orb out of the air.
      As Halimah ran out of the room, she could hear a commotion coming from the lower levels. Something was happening in the dungeons. Silently, Halimah thanked Cora for whatever kind of distraction she had managed to cause.
      Halimah darted into the throne room to find it empty. She slowed to a stop next to the large arches as she clutched a painful stitch in her side. Then her breath caught in her throat as she took in the ocean of stars glittering outside the large arches cut into the wall. A soft breeze drifted through the room to rustle her hair.
      Jump. She was supposed to jump off the edge of the castle.
      As Halimah made to take a step forward, an arm suddenly swung out of nowhere and collided with her head. White spots flared across Halimah's vision as she staggered.
      "So we can touch you after all, you pretty little liar," a female voice purred.
      Halimah nearly froze. It was the same day angel who had pulled Halimah away from the other gods.
      The day angel looked down her nose at Halimah in amusement. "The king and the others are currently in the dungeons. But I've alerted all of them of your presence. They'll be here any second now. You have nowhere to run."
      There was a loud boom as the doors to the throne room were thrown open. Halimah snuck a glance over her shoulder to see the king of the day angels enter the room, and his face twisted in rage.
      Halimah just flashed the king a smile before leaping into the open air. In the moments it took gravity to kick in, time seemed to slow. As Halimah's momentum carried her forward in slow motion, she took in the thousands of stars around her. She could see the galaxy-the swirls of vibrant color were like splattered paint. And for a moment, everything was calm.
      And then suddenly, time sped back up. Halimah's stomach dropped as she plummeted down, down, down.
      With the wind roaring in her ears, Halimah tumbled through the air in a free fall. There was a rush of feathered wings as someone swooped her into their arms. "Goddess of Life," a female voice said in greeting.
      "Hello," Halimah said, still shaken. She craned her neck around to try to see the female's face.
      "Under the cover of night," the female told Halimah as they flew, "the king's guards won't be able to track us. We sent out decoys just in case, but everything has been going smoothly. I'm taking you to meet the others."
      "The others?"
      "You'll see," the female said knowingly.
      Halimah fell silent as they continued to fly through the gradually brightening sky. Would the king connect Cora to her escape from the castle? Halimah hoped the day angel was alright.
      
~

      After what had to be at least an hour of flying, the day angel began to slow as a large tower-like building came into view. The sun was just beginning to peak its golden head above the horizon, and the sky was painted a soft rosy pink.
      Halimah could now see the day angel more clearly: the female had brown sun-kissed skin and long silky hair the color of ink. She was clothed entirely in black to blend in with the night, and her silver wings were powdered with charcoal.
      "This is our headquarters," the day angel explained as they swooped in through an open window.
      The moment they landed, a loud cheer erupted from inside the building. There was a crowd of about ten day angels in the room, and all of them were clapping and smiling in welcome.
      "Headquarters for what?" Halimah asked, wide-eyed as the day angel set her gently on the ground.
      The day angel smiled. "The rebellion."
      "Navi," someone called from the crowd. "Welcome back!"
      "It's good to be back." The inky-haired day angel waved. "Has Nihira returned yet?"
      "Not yet," the same day angel replied. "Your sister will probably be here any minute, though."
      "Goddess of Life." All the day angels in the room bowed their heads respectfully.
      "Did Cora arrange this?" Halimah questioned curiously as she looked around the room. "Thank you for helping save me."
      "You know Cora?" Navi said brightly. "My twin sister, Nihira, and I worked out most of the details. And fortunately, we had enough people working for us in the castle to pull it off."
      Suddenly there was a rush of wings as a new day angel swooped in through the window. After landing gracefully on the floor, the day angel shook back her sheet of silky hair before walking over to Navi. Apart from the difference in their clothes, the new day angel, Nihira, was the spitting image of her sister.
      "We should lie low for the next few days," Nihira spoke up. Her voice was soft like a morning breeze. "The king isn't happy that we took the acting goddess of life away. He sent his guards after us, but we managed to lose them in the main city."
      Smiling apologetically, Navi turned back to Halimah. "I don't think we had a proper introduction. I'm Navi, and this is my sister Nihira. The two of us are the leaders of this rebellion against the king. To make sure we aren't caught, our forces are spread out across the entire realm. This building is just our headquarters."
      "I'd like to say there's about ten thousand of us," Nihira said quietly. "That's the number that has officially registered, but there are thousands more who are unofficial and support us."
      "Our goal is to overthrow the king and put an end to his tyranny," Navi said determinedly. "We will avenge our night angel sisters and brothers. We will create a world where we can live together in peace."
      The other day angels in the room cheered and pumped their fists in the air.
      Navi laughed. "Alright everyone, back to your positions. You know the protocol."
      The day angels saluted the sisters before turning and exiting through a door in the corner of the room.
      "Every once in a while," Navi explained as she turned back to Halimah, "the king sends his guards to search all of the buildings for night angels."
      Halimah blinked. "Night angels?"
      "We're the ones who have been breaking night angels out of the king's mines for years," Nihira said as she brushed charcoal dust off of her wings and clothes. "They've been staying in our safe houses, hidden from the king's guards. But lately, it's been getting more and more risky. We know the king has a weapon and that he wants to use it against the night angels. We can't let that happen. But if we get everyone together and try to storm the castle, he'll likely use it against us instead."
      "About that," Halimah said slowly. Her chains clinked as she pulled out the vacuum of magic she had tucked under her belt.
      Navi and Nihira's jaws dropped in identical expressions of shock as the icy blue light of the orb inside it flooded the room.
      "Is that . . .?" Navi whispered as she clapped a hand to her mouth.
      "The king's weapon?" Nihira finished for her sister.
      Halimah tucked the magic vacuum away, and the blue light faded. "I took a little detour on my way to the throne room."
      Navi and Nihira looked at each other. "This could change everything," Nihira said softly.
      Navi nodded in agreement. "Goddess of Life, you are brilliant."
      Halimah laughed. "Please, call me Halimah."
      "Halimah," Navi amended. "You are brilliant."
      "You should be careful with that," Nihira warned as her smile faded. "We don't know if the king and his guards will be able to track it here."
      Navi suddenly looked panicked. "We can't just toss it! We don't know what that weapon is capable of."
      Nihira frowned. "We need to move it to a place the king will never go even if he can track the weapon's magic."
      The two sisters shared a look before nodding. "The realm of the night angels," Navi voiced softly. "The king can travel anywhere he pleases in this realm. If we move the weapon to a different realm, he won't take the risk of facing the queen."
      "Then it's decided," Nihira said. "We'll move the weapon at nightfall."
      Navi glanced over at her sister. "Just in case anything happens, we should tell the night angels to keep a low profile. They know the drill."
      "We're sheltering a number of night angels here," Nihira explained. "We have hidden rooms built into all of our safe houses. We'll give you a tour of headquarters."
      "Should I do anything about this?" Halimah gestured to the chains and shackle attached to her wrist.
      "Hmm," Navi hummed thoughtfully as she leaned over to examine the length of chain. "This kind of shackle cancels out magic. If you had two shackles, you wouldn't be able to use any of your power. But with only one, you can use your magic while its presence is masked."
      "The only place you can find this kind of shackle is in the king's dungeons," Nihira added with a slight smile. "You're using his own inventions against him. If he can't sense your magic, he won't be able to find you."
      Halimah looked down at the shackle. "I guess I'll be wearing this for a while."
      "We could cut the chain," Navi offered. "That way you'll only have the shackle."
      Halimah watched as Nihira drew a dagger-like blade from her leg holster. "Hold still," the day angel instructed as she carefully picked up the chain and got to work slicing it free from the shackle. There was a loud clunk as the chain Nihira was cutting fell to the ground. "There you go."
      "Thank you." Halimah smiled gratefully.
      Nihira sheathed her blade. "You're welcome."
      "Follow us." Navi beckoned Halimah brightly. "We'll show you around."
      The two sisters led Halimah out of the room and onto the landing beyond. Halimah's eyes widened as she looked around. Wooden stairs spiraled from the bottom floor of the tower-like building all the way to the top. Glass lamps hung from the ceiling far above, and golden flames danced playfully inside.
      "How many people are currently staying here?" Halimah decided to inquire.
      "There's twenty-five of us here right now," Navi told Halimah as they made their way down the stairs. "Sixteen day angels and nine night angels. Let's meet the night angels first, shall we?" Navi's eyes sparkled as she came to a stop in front of what appeared to be a section of solid wall. Reaching out with a hand, she pressed one of the stones on the wall. The stone retreated at her touch, and a moment later, a section of the wall rose upward to reveal a wooden door.
      "You like it?" Nihira asked Halimah. "We had to create it all mechanically just in case the king's guards ever decided to detect any magic entries."
      "It's brilliant."
      "It's me, Navi," the day angel called through the closed door. "I'd like to introduce you all to the Goddess of Life."
      "Come in," a quiet voice called from the other side of the wood.
      Navi gently pushed open the door and held it open for Nihira and Halimah. Halimah stepped over the threshold into what appeared to be a small living room. Three violet-winged night angels stood against the back wall of the room-one female and two males.
      Navi shut the door behind her and casually leaned against it. "Everyone, this is Halimah. She's the new goddess of life."
      "Hello." Halimah bowed her head to the night angels. "It's a pleasure to meet you."
      The female night angel inclined her head. "Likewise, Goddess of Life." She had long hair and ghostly pale skin. When Halimah looked closer, she noticed with a jolt that every inch of the night angel's visible skin was covered in scars.
      The night angel noticed Halimah's stare and she smiled sadly. "Don't worry about me. I've been here for nearly fifty years now. I managed to get off better than others."
      It took Halimah a moment to notice that one of the male night angels was staring at her white hair with wide eyes. He lifted a finger and pointed.
      The female night angel smiled faintly. "I think he's trying to say that he thinks the color of your hair is very interesting. He can't talk," the female night angel added softly. "Neither of them can."
      "Oh." Halimah fell silent.
      The female night angel gestured to the night angel who had pointed at Halimah's hair. "His tongue was removed during his time in the mines. And him"-she gestured to the other male night angel who hadn't spoken-"he hasn't said a word in years."
      There was a long silence until Navi finally spoke up. "Are the others still asleep?"
      The female night angel nodded.
      "We'll leave you be." Navi beckoned Halimah back toward the door. "Come, let's finish our tour."

    Chapter Twenty-Eight

	Crow leaned against the rail of the balcony as he watched the snow flutter down from the cloudy sky. His breath puffed out in front of him as he exhaled. Was there really nothing they could do? He hadn't been able to contact Cora at all in the past couple of days. And just last night . . . it had felt as if their connection had been severed completely.
	Absently, Crow pulled back his right sleeve to look at the small bruise-like mark. This had been with him for a while now. And as he continued to look at it, Crow suddenly had the urge to tell someone about it. Crow turned around and made his way back inside the temple.
      Saedyn was sitting on the couch in front of the fireplace, a book in his hands. When the white-haired boy saw Crow approaching, he set his book down and smiled faintly at Crow.
	Crow dropped his gaze. "I . . . there's something I want to get off my chest. Would you be willing to listen?"
      Saedyn nodded as he waited for Crow to go on.
      "You know how I told you-and everyone else-that I hadn't used my magic for years after my parents threw me out? There actually was a time I used it." Crow rolled up his right sleeve and showed his arm to Saedyn. "This was how Cora found me."
      The white-haired boy's eyes widened as he stared at the mark. "So it's true?"
      Crow looked at Saedyn in surprise. "You knew?"
      "I wasn't sure at first-I've only ever read about it in books before."
      "The king of the day angels . . ." Crow's voice dropped. "He has one on his arm too."
      "No," Saedyn said in shock.
      "It's true."
      Saedyn fell silent as he looked back down at Crow's arm.
      Crow smiled sadly. "For the longest time, I didn't tell anyone about my magic-I was afraid that they'd respond the same way my parents had. I hid it, but the magic was starting to mess with my head. It was during that period that I overheard a group of students researching different types of magic. I listened to them describe how one could use their magic to take their own life.
      "I still remember that day clearly." Crow suddenly realized he was talking faster and faster, and he stopped for a moment to take a deep breath. "I still remember clawing my fingers underneath my skin. I was ready to let my magic do the rest. But it was only when I was on the brink of death that I realized that it wasn't what I wanted. I was confused. I didn't know what I wanted anymore, but at that moment I knew it wasn't death."
      "Well," Saedyn said weakly, "I'm really, really, glad you didn't go through with it."
      
~

	Dinner had just ended, and Crow was standing on one of the overhanging balconies with Saedyn, Lyria, Maliq, and Fern. The snow had stopped for the time being, and the night was surprisingly clear.
	"We saw the map of the king's castle you presented at dinner, Crow," Lyria said brightly. "It's brilliant! I think the former gods will definitely be able to use it to their advantage."
	"I hope so." Crow sighed. The coldness of the air stung his face and lungs, but there was something refreshing about it. After telling Saedyn about his past, the two of them had worked on drawing up a map of the castle. Crow drew as much as he could from memory, and then Saedyn had added the labels according to Crow's instructions.
	"Look"-Maliq pointed upward-"we can see the constellations! There's the Tree of Life. Do you see all its branches?"
	"The Crystal District is the closest you can get to the stars from the ground of Hali," Fern said softly as she stared up at the thousands of twinkling lights. "You'd have to be one of the winged folk to get any closer."
      Crow leaned against the balcony's railings as he stared out at the snow-capped mountains in the distance. No one spoke for a while. There was silence, but it wasn't the awkward kind. It was just . . . peaceful.
      Suddenly Fern leaped up onto the balcony railing. Flames crackled at her fingertips, and her eyes narrowed as she scanned the open air. "I saw something." Fern didn't take her eyes off the night sky for an instant.
      "Saw what?" Maliq asked as he jumped up to perch on the railing as well.
      "It was a blur of wings. Silver wings."
      Lyria turned worriedly to Crow. "You should go back inside. If there are day angels around, I think that's probably for the best."
      "The three of us will survey the area." Fern's deep red hair whispered in the breeze as she gestured to Lyria, Maliq, and herself. "The two of you should alert the others." A moment later, Lyria, Maliq, and Fern were gone.

    Chapter Twenty-Nine

	Halimah sat on her bed, absentmindedly fiddling with the shackle around her wrist. She had given the Flames of Ice orb to Navi and Nihira to keep safe, and the two day angels promised that they'd do everything in their power to keep it out of the king's hands.
	The room she was staying in was simple-outfitted only with a bed, nightstand, and dresser. There was a single window in the corner of the room, but it was made entirely from stained glass. That way, no one from the outside could see into the room.
	She had changed into the clean outfit the twins had provided for her, and now Halimah got to her feet. After stopping at the door, Halimah gently turned the handle and walked out into the living room area. The same female night angel from earlier in the morning was sitting on the couch.
      "Hello," Halimah said, trying her best not to startle the night angel with her sudden presence.
      "Hello." The night angel smiled wistfully as she turned her attention to Halimah.
      "I hope I'm not interrupting anything."
      The night angel adjusted her violet wings neatly behind her. "I'm kind of glad I have someone to talk to now. I'm Eve, by the way. It really is a pleasure to meet you, Goddess of Life. We heard about how you single-handedly stopped the king's attack on the night angel realm. All of us are in your debt. We also heard how you saved the wielder of soul's life. He could have been the one to stop the king-but at the cost of his life."
      Halimah sighed. "I didn't want him to die. I don't want anyone to die. In all the fifty years you've been here, have you and the other night angels tried to return to the realm of the night angels?"
      "We haven't tried." Eve clasped her pale hands together in her lap. "We decided that if we were to return to our home realm, we would go together. Even now, half of us aren't in any state to make the journey."

~

	The following morning, Halimah sat in the dining room with the day angels when, suddenly, glass shattered as a dark-haired figure crashed through the window. Halimah was on her feet in an instant, and magic sparked at her fingers.
      Halimah's tension faded when she realized it was Nihira, but she was carrying another day angel in her arms. The day angel appeared to be unconscious. His silver wings were slashed, and blood dripped down the side of his face. When Halimah did a double-take, Nihira looked like a wreck as well; the day angel was covered in cuts and scratches.
	"They're coming," Nihira gasped out as she lay the male on the floor. "The king's guards."
	"What happened?" Navi asked in alarm as she waved a hand to repair the broken window. "Where are the others?"
	"We were attacked." Nihira clamped a hand over her arm to stop the large gash in it from bleeding. "I don't know how the king's guards found us, but they were violent. I told the others to split up and fly to different safe houses. The guards took the orb from us."
      Halimah felt the color drain from her face.
      "It was too dark for them to see our faces, but the guards must know by now that we landed around this general area." Nihira tried and failed to rise to her feet, and Navi was there within a second to help support her sister. "They're going to search the building any minute."
      Navi frowned. "You know the drill."
      Two day angels swiftly walked over to pick up their unconscious friend before turning to leave the room. Halimah followed them up the staircase and to the hidden room behind the wall.
      Eve was sitting on the couch, and the night angel jumped to her feet the moment she saw them walk in. She hurried over to help the other two day angels carry the unconscious one to the couch and lay him down in a way that wouldn't crush his wings. "I'll go alert the others," she said softly.
      "Remember to stay quiet and not use any magic," Navi said in an undertone as she set Nihira down next to the doorway. "I'll let you know when the guards leave." Navi exited the room and quickly closed the door. There was a soft noise as the stone wall fell back into place behind it.
      A moment later, the sound of muffled knocking sounded from the front door. "Open up," a gruff voice demanded. "We're here on orders from His Majesty."
      Nihira lay down on the floor and pressed her ear to the wood. She motioned for Halimah to do the same.
      "May I ask why you want to search my residence?" Navi's cool voice drifted up through the floorboards.
      "We tracked day angel rebels to this location," the voice replied shortly. "We're searching all the buildings around."
      Footsteps shuffled around downstairs followed by the sound of muffled voices. Then armored footfalls sounded on the stairs again as the guards made their way to the upper levels of the tower-like building.
      Out of the corner of her eye, Halimah saw Nihira resting a hand on the hilt of her blade. For a moment, the footsteps were right on the other side of the wall. And then they passed.
      About ten minutes later, the footsteps went back down the stairs. "Good day," one of the guards said curtly.
      The door clicked shut, and Navi opened the wall to the secret room shortly after. "They're gone," she announced. "But we should lay low for the rest of the day just in case."
      
~

	That night at dinner, the atmosphere was heavy. Four members were missing from the table, and two more were severely wounded and covered in bandages. Things only got worse when Navi entered the room with a grim expression on her face.
      "Cora has been locked up," she announced. "According to one of our spies inside the castle, the king's guards threw her in the dungeons last night."
	Halimah stared at her plate helplessly.
	"Since the king didn't kill her on the spot," Navi said as if reading Halimah's thoughts, "I think she'll be alright."
	"Could I suggest something?" Halimah spoke up.
	Navi turned to Halimah expectantly. "Of course."
	"I think we should talk to the queen of the night angels."
	"Getting the queen of the night angels involved definitely would be helpful-but we've never talked to her before," Navi admitted. "We don't know how she'll react if a number of us day angels just showed up at her doorstep."
      "She knows me," Halimah said softly. "I can talk to her and ask her to help."

    Chapter Thirty

	"As of now"-Thuc pinched the bridge of his nose as if trying to ward off a headache-"we can't be sure whether day angels are here or not. We've put up a shield around the temple, and starting today, we'll take turns keeping watch."
      As the former flame god talked, Crow found himself constantly glancing out the large windows of the dining hall as if a day angel would appear at any moment. But whenever he looked, there was always nothing except cloudy sky and frosted mountains.
      "We don't know what their motivation or intentions are," Thuc continued. "Until we do, it's better for us to stay on guard."
      Everyone nodded in agreement, and breakfast was eaten in silence.

    

    Chapter Thirty-One

	Halimah stood next to Navi and Nihira. They were all dressed in flying leathers, and they watched the last rays of sunlight fade into the ever-expanding sea of night.
	"Are you ready?" Nihira turned to Halimah. Like her sister, Nihira's long black hair had been braided back away from her face.
	Halimah let out a breath. "Yes."
	Navi grinned. "Good." The day angel effortlessly scooped Halimah into her arms as if she weighed nothing more than a feather. And with a nod to Nihira, Navi jumped from the window.
	Halimah's eyes were wide as they shot toward the stars. The cold wind whipped at Halimah's face and hair, and somewhere far below, a lantern blazed to life.
	"That's the signal for all clear," Navi said loudly over the rushing of the wind.
	Nihira was a dark blur against the night as the day angel swept in and out of Halimah's line of sight. Halimah was fine not having wings, but she had to admit that it was nice to borrow someone else's.
	"We're crossing the border," Navi yelled over the roaring wind after a while. "You might want to shield."
      Halimah nodded. There was a flash of pale pink light as she summoned an invisible shield of magic to counter the winds. Everything seemed to calm down within a matter of seconds. Even the howling had subsided.
      Navi's eyes sparkled. "Look down."
      Halimah dropped her gaze, and her breath caught in her throat. The entirety of Hali was glowing beneath them. Even though it was dark, Halimah could see everything. The snow-capped mountains of the Crystal District, the dusky sand of the Sand Dance District, the spiral of lights from Hali Central. The vast ocean.
	The night sky was slowly lightening, and Halimah blinked in awe as she looked ahead. The second moon of Hali-the realm of the night angels-was rising in front of them. The golden glow of city lights was faintly visible against the moon's surface.
      "There aren't any guards following us." Navi swooped up from somewhere below them to fly at Nihira's side. "Once we get closer to the realm of the night angels, we should slow and find their border patrol. Hopefully, they won't shoot us out of the sky."
	The sunrise was one of the most beautiful sights Halimah had ever witnessed. There was something spectacular about watching the light wash over the land below them. Even in the day, Halimah could still see the stars outlined faintly against the sky and the swirls of the vibrant galaxy beyond.
      After what seemed like another hour or two of flying, there was a rush of violet wings as a group of about seven night angels blocked their path. "Halt," the female night angel at the front command. Her smokey eyes surveyed Halimah and the day angels from behind her helmet.
      "I'm Halimah," Halimah called from Nihira's arms, "the goddess of life. We come in peace."
      "The goddess of life," the night angels murmured.
      "The queen of the night angels once told me and my friends that if we ever needed help, we could come to her."
      "We believe you." The first night angel angled her head to the side. "But just for an extra precaution, we'll have to escort you anyway."
      Halimah smiled. "Thank you."
      "I'm Navi, and this is my sister Nihira," Navi introduced herself as they followed the night angels toward the surface of the realm. "We're in charge of the day angel rebellion."
      "Day angel rebellion?" the female night angel questioned curiously.
      "We doing everything we can to stand up to the king." Nihira explained.
      The night angel smiled faintly. "That's wonderful. I'm Sey, by the way. I'm the head of this particular unit. Were the two of you always the leaders of the rebellion?"
      Navi shook her head. "We took over from the past leaders, who had taken over from the original founders. It's been a while."
      Nihira nodded in agreement. "The two of us have been the leaders for the past seventy years or so."
      Sey smiled. "Then I'm honored to welcome you to the realm of the night angels. Look down."
      Halimah's eyes widened as she looked down. Grassy fields and wooden buildings dotted the surface of the realm, and violet-winged figures flew back and forth in a carefree manner. While the realm of the day angels had been towering stone buildings, the realm of the night angels was bursting with warm color.
      "Here we are," Sey announced. "The castle is coming up straight ahead of us."
      Sey was right-stone turrets were suddenly visible along the horizon, and they were quickly followed by the majestic body of the castle.
      As they drew closer, Halimah noticed that unlike the king's castle, the queen's was sitting firmly on the ground. Flowering vine-like plants snaked up the castle's walls, and even more sprouted from between the stone bricks.
      Before Halimah knew it, they were touching down on the dirt path right in front of the castle's stained glass doors.
      Sey's eyes were bright as she turned to face the three of them. "So, are you ready to meet the queen?"

    Chapter Thirty-Two

      "Get down!" Ewen's voice yelled.
      No one needed to be told twice as they dropped to the polished floor. A gust of wind shot over their heads followed by wingbeats and a shriek.
      Ewen was helping them to their feet a moment later. "Day angels," he said darkly.
      Fire blossomed outside, red, golden, and white. Thuc and Lianna were visible through the large windows in the hall for a moment before they vanished behind a plume of smoke and steam. "Those two are insane." Ewen shook his head. "I've only been guarding the front doors, but they've been running around the entire temple. Rania too-she's on the roof right now."
      "I will go assist them." Gwenevieve hurried toward the doors, but before she made it to the exit, a dark-haired figure dropped down from somewhere above.
      "There's no need," Rania said in a way of greeting as she flipped her thick braid over a shoulder. "They just flew away."
      "They're after me," Crow said quietly, and everyone turned to look at him. "The king wants me back."
      "It looks as if the king is getting desperate," Saedyn added. "He sends them to the temple even though three of the four former gods are here."
      "Do you think it has something to do with Halimah?" Ewen asked quickly.
      
~

	The following day, Saedyn was quieter than usual during breakfast. His brow was slightly furrowed, as if he were deep in thought.
	"Is everything alright?" Crow asked softly.
	"What?" Saedyn said distractedly. "Yes. I was just thinking of ways we might be able to get Halimah out of the castle."
	Crow gave the white-haired boy a sideways look but returned to his food without asking any more questions.
	When everyone finished eating, Saedyn quietly reached across the table and tapped Professor Lethco on the paw. "Could I talk to you outside for a moment?"
	The cat nodded and hopped down from his chair.
	Saedyn turned back to Crow. "You too, Crow."
	When they crossed into the entrance hall, Saedyn made sure that the doors had closed behind him before he began talking. "Professor," he addressed the cat, "you've been teaching magic for many years . . ."
	"Indeed I have." Professor Lethco flicked his tail.
	"Can you perform transfiguration magic?"
	"Yes. Why?"
	Saedyn smiled faintly. "I came up with a plan to rescue Halimah that might just work."
	"Do tell," said Professor Lethco.
	"I want you to turn me into Crow. I will go to the castle in his place."

    Chapter Thirty-Three

	Halimah stared up at the castle. The most stunning part of it were front doors. They were large and made entirely from stained glass with reds, oranges, yellows, and greens popping out from the intricate design. It was a tree. A tree that told the story of life and love and loss.
      "This way." Sey smiled as she pushed open the large doors. Even Navi and Nihira were in awe as they stepped over the threshold. Sunlight streamed into the room from the windows, and the light cut through the faint swirls of dust in the air.
      Sey removed her helmet and shook back her sheet of flaming hair. "Could you please let the queen know that she has visitors?" she asked one of the other armored night angels.
      Nodding, the night angel quickly took off up the stairs.
      Fortunately, they didn't have to wait long. "Look!" Sey turned to gesture at the staircase. "There she is now."
      The queen of the night angels stood at the top of the steps, her head held high. She was dressed in flowing robes the color of sunshine, and her large violet wings were folded neatly at her back.
      "Your Majesty." The night angels simultaneously dropped to their knees in a bow.
      "Please rise." The queen smiled warmly. "There's no need to be so formal. Halimah! Welcome. Let's go to my study, shall we?"
      "It was a pleasure meeting you," Sey addressed Halimah, Navi, and Nihira. "I've got to return to my post. I hope we'll have the opportunity to meet again."
      Once she was gone, Halimah and the twins followed the queen through a long hall lined with windows. Soon they stopped in front of a wooden door at the back of the castle, and the queen held open the door for her guests to enter. After shutting the door behind them, the queen of the night angels walked over to the desk and took a seat behind it. And with a wave of her hand, three comfortable chairs appeared in front of it in a flash of golden light. "Please sit."
      As the sisters repeated the information they had given Halimah a few days ago to the queen, Halimah found herself looking around the room. On the wall next to the door, there was a painting of a female with long flaming hair and violet wings. It was the queen of the night angels.
      When Navi and Nihira finished talking, Halimah turned to the queen. "Your Majesty," she couldn't help but ask, "that painting. How long ago was that?"
      The queen smiled somewhat wistfully. "That's one of the few paintings of me from before the First War." The queen was still smiling, but her eyes were sad. "It feels like a lifetime ago that the day and night angels were united."
      "We're planning to take on the king of the day angels," Halimah told her.
      "Now is the time for action," Navi added. "If we strike now, he won't have the time to build anything even more powerful to counter you."
      "Please, Your Majesty." Halimah stood from her chair and bowed as low as she could. "Please lend us your assistance."
      The queen stood as well. "If there is anything I can do to end the suffering of those being crushed under the king's hands, I will gladly provide you with my support."
      
~

	That evening, Halimah and the twins went down to the dining hall for dinner. The three of them arrived to find the queen sitting at the head of a long table. A long-haired night angel stood at her side.
	"Halimah!" Sera's coal-colored eyes widened as Halimah hurried over to greet her. "I heard that you got your vision back." Sera flipped her long flaming hair over a shoulder. "It's been a little while, hasn't it?"
	"It has been," Halimah agreed. "Sera, do you think you could contact Saedyn and tell him what's going on? Everyone back at the temple still thinks that I'm locked up in the king's castle."
	"I tried already." Sera frowned as she ruffled her violet wings. "I don't know why, but I can't seem to connect to him. I think there's a shield around the temple. I can't get through it from this distance."
	"Would you be up for a trip to the temple?" the queen asked.
	Sera bowed. "I'll start making preparations."
	"It's becoming more and more dangerous for us night angels to leave our realm," the queen told Halimah, Navi, and Nihira after Sera vanished from sight. "The king has guards stationed everywhere. I think he's paranoid that we're going to attack his realm. Please, have a seat."
	"There's something I'm curious about," Halimah said as she pulled up a chair. "Were you the one who chose Sera to be the one to communicate with the wielders of soul, or did she volunteer herself?"
      The queen smiled. "At the time, I was looking for someone willing to take on the job. Not many night angels wanted to in case something went wrong, but Sera enthusiastically volunteered. She's confident and passionate about protecting her people. And I find that extremely valuable."

    Chapter Thirty-Four

	Crow shook his head in a daze, refusing to believe his ears.
	Saedyn sighed heavily. "We're out of ideas, and this is the only thing that might have a chance of working."
	"It's too dangerous." Crow continued to shake his head. "The king of the day angels-"
	Saedyn smiled sadly. "This is my responsibility as a wielder of soul. Besides, I still owe Halimah for saving my life. I wouldn't be here if it wasn't for her."
	
~

	The first hour after Saedyn's departure dragged by unbelievably slowly. Crow was sitting next to the window with Gloria on his lap. He absently stroked the chicken's soft feathers as he stared blankly at the snow falling outside.
	Suddenly something violet blurred past the window. Crow jumped to his feet and pressed his nose to the glass. Crow hastily scooped Gloria into his arms and ran toward the stairs. He recognized this particular night angel. It was Sera.
	Crow skidded to a stop at the top of the entrance hall's staircase. The former gods were already gathered by the door, and Crow's heart sank when he saw all of the god's shocked expressions. "What is it?" Crow asked, dreading the answer.
	"Halimah isn't at the king's castle," Rania said as if she couldn't believe it herself. "She hasn't been for some time. She broke out."
	Crow froze. Saedyn was going to the castle even though Halimah was no longer there.
	"I'll go alert the queen." Sera turned and disappeared into the open air with a flap of her violet wings.
	Just then, Crow froze. He could feel a disturbance in the air. A powerful magic was rumbling in the sky. From the way the former gods were looking at each other, they had felt it too.
	"The king is making his move," Gwenevieve said grimly. There was something like panic in her normally calm eyes.
	Thuc's face was pale. "But our son is still up there with him!"
      Gwenevieve began to glow with a turquoise light. "We'll leave for the castle now. Crow, you should stay-"
      Crow quickly shook his head. "I want to help. If the king is using his weapons, my magic can help stop them."
      After looking at him for a long moment, Gwenevieve finally nodded her head. Before Crow could blink, the temple was fading away in a flash of turquoise light. When the light cleared, Crow found himself standing in the throne room of the king's castle.
	"Where is everyone?" Rania asked as she looked around. She had a blade drawn in one hand and magic sparkled in the other.
	The throne room was eerily empty.
	Just then, the entire world seemed to explode in silver, and the disturbance Crow had felt in the air suddenly disappeared.
	"That was Saedyn's magic," Lyria said worriedly. "He must be near the king."
	Suddenly, Crow felt something soft brush against his ankle. "Gloria?"
	The chicken clucked once.
	"Gloria, what are you doing here?" Crow asked in a panic.
	Without warning, the doors to the throne room violently burst open as the king's guards charged into the room.
	Favian's hands flared with blue light as he threw up a shield of pulsing magic. "We can't afford to waste time here! Find Saedyn!"
	"This way." Fern hurriedly gestured for Lyria, Maliq, and Crow to follow her.
      Crow scooped Gloria into his arms and took off at a sprint after the red-haired girl. Lyria and Maliq ran on either side of him, and their magic flared as they blasted the armored day angels out of the way.
	Flames blazed as Fern cleared a path toward the doors. "Crow," the red-haired girl yelled as she slammed her flaming fist into one of the many armored day angels charging at them. "You know the castle! Which way should we go?"
	Crow gave himself only a moment's thought before pointing to the hall on their right. "That way."
	Fern nodded before plowing forward through the swarm of day angels. Crow used his void magic to throw out shields to counter the blades swinging toward Lyria and Maliq's unprotected backs. The four of them sprinted down the hall. They skidded around the corner and hurtled up the flight of stairs at the end.
	"Keep running!" Fern yelled as she whirled around to face the day angels who had tailed them. There were ten day angels.
	"I'll help you," Lyria leaped back down the stairs to stand at Fern's side. Her violet eyes blazed with determination as she summoned a tidal wave of water to crash into their pursuers.
	The stairs ended at a long hall, and Crow and Maliq sprinted down it at full speed. The further they went, the more the sounds of the fighting below faded. Within minutes, the only sound was their heavy footfalls echoing through the silence.
	Suddenly there was a loud boom, and Crow was thrown forward as he lost his footing. Instinctively, he curled around Gloria, using his body to shield the chicken. He painfully slid across the polished floor before finally coming to a stop underneath a window. His ears were ringing dully, and his head was spinning.
	Crow slowly sat up, and his eyes widened in disbelief as he took in the damage. Where the hall had once been was a gaping hole in the floor below. "Maliq!" Crow called, scanning for him in a panic.
	"I'm here," Maliq's voice called from the level below.
	Crow quickly crawled over to the broken floor to look down. Maliq waved up at him. He was covered in bruises, but seemed fine other than that.
	Armored footsteps sounded as guards rushed toward Maliq. "Keep going," Maliq yelled as his magic flared. "I'll hold them off!"
	Even though Maliq couldn't see him, Crow nodded as he scrambled to his feet. He needed to get to Saedyn.

    Chapter Thirty-Five

	Halimah spent the morning exploring the queen's castle alone since Navi and Nihira were still asleep in their designated rooms. The sun was slowly rising in the sky outside the large glass windows, and the long halls were bathed in rose-gold light.
      When it was time for breakfast, Halimah sat between Navi and Nihira at the table in the dining hall. The queen was at the head of the table again, chatting with the two sisters when suddenly the doors were thrown open as Sera sprinted in. "The wielder of soul was sent to the king's castle," she panted as she skidded to a stop next to the queen. "I couldn't get to them in time to explain that you were no longer there."
	"What?" Halimah stared at her. But then everyone in the room paused. "There's a disturbance in the air," Halimah whispered.
      "We need to get to the castle." The queen of the night angels stood as well, and her expression was grim. "The king is about to attack. Sera, please get our forces ready to teleport."
      "Yes, Your Majesty." Sera bowed before hurrying back out of the dining hall.
      "Ready?" the queen of the night angels asked as she lifted her hands into the air.
      "Ready," Navi, Blair, and Halimah replied in unison.
      There was a flash of light, and the world was ripped away from underneath Halimah's feet. When the light faded, she was falling through open air. A split second later, Navi picked her up, and the four of them circled above the castle.
      "The king doesn't have guards stationed above," the queen explained. "No one can get past the guards to even get this high."
      "I'm going to send the signal." Nihira took off in a blur of silver feathers.
      "I'll look for the king," the queen told them. "I'll leave it to the rest of you to keep the guards busy."
      Halimah's heart was pounding a mile a minute in her chest as she nodded. Navi set Halimah down on the castle's roof before swooping down to enter the structure through the large open arches of the throne room.
      There was a sudden roar followed by the sound of weapons being unsheathed. Then the clanking of armor faded as the king's guards chased Navi out of the throne room and into the castle beyond.
      After parting ways with the queen, Halimah broke into a sprint. She hurried down flight after flight of stairs. She only came across a few guards along the way, and Halimah made quick work of them. There was something she needed to do. Sprinting down the steps, Halimah hurried down to the castle dungeons. The guards barely had time to cry out as she knocked them unconscious with her magic.
      "Halimah?" a disbelieving voice called from one of the far cells.
      Halimah sprinted over to find Cora's shocked face looking at her from behind the bars. "I've come to get you out of here," Halimah told her. "Stand back."
      With a wave of her hand, the bars vanished. Halimah hurried forward and magically cut the day angel's chains from the wall. Cora opened her mouth, but closed it when no sound came out.
      "The day angels from the rebellion are on their way to the castle right now," Halimah explained quickly. "The queen's army is coming too."
      The two of them took off out of the dungeons at a run, careful to avoid trampling on the unconscious guards. After throwing open the door, Halimah blinked as the bright sunlight from the open windows temporarily blinded her.
      "Look!" Cora froze as she pointed to one of the windows. Hundreds upon hundreds of day angels were flying toward the castle. None of them were wearing the armor of the king's guards, and some held blades in their hands while others held pitchforks and shovels. These were the people banding together to rise up against the king.
      The king's guards had drawn their blades, but judging from their body language, they were clearly overwhelmed by the sheer numbers. A moment later, the rising day angels reached the king's guards, and a roaring filled the air. The sound of metal upon metal mingled with the screams and roars of those fighting on both sides.
      Tearing her eyes away from the window, Halimah pulled Cora along as she sprinted down the hall. "We have to find Saedyn-he's here somewhere in the castle!"
      Suddenly a tremendous boom sounded from behind them, and Halimah and Cora were thrown forward by the blast of the explosion. The wind was knocked from Halimah's lungs as she hit the hard floor. Cora hissed quietly from the floor next to her. The day angels were already laying siege to the castle.
      "This way." Halimah helped Cora to her feet before gesturing to a spiraling staircase. They took the steps two at a time as they hurried upward. Then Halimah let out a cry as she almost collided with someone.
      "Halimah?" a familiar voice asked.
      "Ewen!" Halimah finally found her voice. "What are you doing here?"
      Ewen just responded by wrapping his arms around her in a tight embrace.
      Halimah held Ewen tightly. "Not only is the king using his weapon now, but Saedyn came to the castle without knowing I was no longer here. He's in danger."
      "I know," Ewen said grimly. "Sera told us about how you escaped."
      Another explosion sounded from somewhere in the distance, and the whole castle shook.
      "Just what is happening?" Ewen threw out a shield of solid air to protect them from any falling debris.
      "The day angel rebellion," Halimah explained quickly. "The king wants to use his weapon, so they're rising up against him. The queen of the night angels is bringing her forces as well."
      Ewen was shaking, and Halimah suddenly realized that she was too. "You're safe," Ewen whispered.
      "I'm safe." Halimah smiled. "Are the others here?"
      "Yes. The former gods and their partners are here along with Lyria, Maliq, and Fern. Professor Lethco and Crow too."
      "Come on"-Halimah grabbed the green-haired boy by the hand-"let's go look for Saedyn. Cora, do you . . ." They had lost the day angel along the way. Halimah just hoped she was alright as the two of them hurried up the staircase and down a long hallway. As they turned the corner, a familiar figure came into view.
      "Crow!" Halimah called out.
      Crow whirled around. Even from a distance, Halimah could see that his eyes were wide, and his face was pale and terrified. "Halimah!" he exclaimed as he hurried over to greet them. Crow's hair hosted pieces of stone and dust, and his clothes were powdered with the same sediment. "I was with Lyria, Maliq, and Fern, but then we got separated. And I don't know where the other gods are either."
      Suddenly, golden light flared outside as the sky was momentarily engulfed in the blinding radiance. Then a moment later, a loud roar sounded. Halimah cracked open an eye. It was the night angels. The army of violet blurs slammed into the king's guards with a cry. Blades clashed and magic crackled. For a second, Halimah spotted Navi, Nihira, and Sey among them.
      "I found him," Crow's said suddenly. "He just used his magic!  I-I can sense it!" Crow quickly crouched down and set Gloria on the polished floor. "Gloria, stay here. I've got to run."
      "Wait!" Ewen called as Crow took off at a sprint down the hall.
      Halimah and Ewen shared a glance, and then the two of them hurried to close the gap. Just then, a silver-winged figure crashed through a window in front of them. Halimah instinctively flung her hands up to create a shield as glass shards flew in every direction. When the dust cleared, Crow had vanished.
      Before Halimah had time to wrap her head around what was going on, another crashing noise sounded as the window behind them shattered. Then Ewen was yelling as an armored day angel grabbed him and leaped out the window.
      "Ewen!" Halimah cried as she ran over to the window.
      The day angel was gone, and Ewen was tumbling through the sky.
      Halimah took a running jump and threw herself out of the window. The wind hit her full in the face as she plummeted down after the green-haired boy. In a flash of pale pink light, Halimah was suddenly tumbling through the open sky directly above Ewen.
      "Take my hand!" Halimah yelled. The wind whisked her voice away.
      Ewen's eyes were wide as he looked up at her, and the green-haired boy extended his fingers toward Halimah. His mouth was moving, but Halimah couldn't hear over the roar of the wind.
      They were falling faster and faster with each passing second, and the floating castle was growing smaller and smaller. Day angels and night angels alike filled the air, and metal clashed against metal. Halimah ignored all of them. Her eyes were glued to Ewen as she stretched her fingers toward him.
      Then her fingers brushed Ewen's, and the world faded in a flash of pale-pink light.
      The two of them crashed through the roof of the castle in a heap as the world rematerialized around them. "Halimah," Ewen said breathlessly. His eyes were still large.
      The two of them were in the middle of a deserted hallway. Windows were broken, and sections of the castle wall missing completely. "Ewen," Halimah said, still shaken.
      Ewen gave Halimah's hand a squeeze. "Let's go find the others."

    Chapter Thirty-Six

      Crow's heart was pounding in his ears as he sprinted through the halls of the castle. Where was Saedyn? He could feel the white-haired boy's magic.
      Crow flew up another staircase and skidded around the corner of the landing. He flailed his arms out as his momentum sent him careening into the wall. After hastily tugging off his shoes and socks, Crow continued to run barefoot over the smooth floors.
      The presence of Saedyn's magic was getting stronger. After turning the corner, Crow came to a stop.
      "Crow?" It was Saedyn. The white-haired boy was standing in the middle of the hall, wide eyed.
	"What happened?" Crow asked quickly as he hurried over. "You're you again!"
      "The king actually believed that I was you at first." Saedyn's face was deathly pale. "I was worried when he mentioned that Halimah was no longer here, but then he started using that weapon of his, and my cover was blown when I tried to stop him. We fought, and now the king is really, really, angry. I've been running away from him ever since. He used his magic to create creatures to attack me-wherever I run, they can track me down. I think I just got the last of them, but the king won't give up that easily."
      "Let's find the others."
      "I've tried to use my magic against him," Saedyn panted as they ran. "But he's just too fast-he dodges whatever I throw at him." Magic flared as the two of them blasted one of the king's magical creatures out of the way.
      "So you can't escape," a deep voice purred from behind them.
      Crow's blood turned to ice.
      "Run!" Saedyn screamed as he threw a blast of silver soul magic in the direction of the king's voice. Metallic feathers blurred behind them as the white-haired boy pulled Crow along. The two of them sped down the stairs, refusing to look back.
      A blast of navy light hit the wall right where Crow's head had been just a split-second before.
      "Weidler of Void, Wielder of Soul," the king called, "I'll admit that you had me fooled. And do you know what I do to people who dare to take me as a fool?"
      Crow ran faster. No, no, no. He didn't want to hear the answer.
      "Don't listen to him!" Saedyn pulled Crow through a doorway leading to a spiraling staircase.
      As they sprinted through the door frame, Crow waved a hand. Void filled the air as the doorway collapsed on itself. Crow was confident that neither of them knew where they were going at this point. All that mattered right now was getting away from the king.
      Without warning, the large window in front of them exploded with a bang, and both Crow and Saedyn were knocked off their feet. Crow barely had time to throw out a shield as glass shards rained down around them.
      The king of the day angels was perched lazily on the window frame, and his navy eyes glinted. Crow slowly got to his feet. He knew the king was fast enough to block them if they tried to run.
      Silver light flared as Saedyn created a protective shield against the king. "Don't worry," he told Crow quietly. "He can't get through the shield."
      The king's lips tugged upward in a smile. "I might not be able to break your shield myself, but what happens when your magic dies out?"
      Saedyn silently glared at the king through the pulsing shield.
      The king's eyes flickered. "You'll find that I'm very patient. I'll just wait here until you use up the last of your magic."
      Crow stepped in front of Saedyn, and his eyes caught on something attached to the king's belt. A cloth pouch glowing faintly with an icy blue light. The Flames of Ice. So the king had it on him after all.
      The king stepped forward from the window, and a whip of icy magic materialized in his hands. "I've changed my mind. I'm losing my patience." The king smiled awfully as he brought the whip crashing down through the air with a deafening crack.
      A small fracture formed in Saedyn's shield from where the whip had struck it. The shield flared silver as Saedyn hastily repaired the gap as the king's whip came down again and again and again.
      Crow turned back to Saedyn in a panic to find beads of sweat dripping down the white-haired boy's face. "Do you think he's close enough to blast him with your magic?" Crow asked worriedly.
      "I thought so when I used my magic against him earlier." Saedyn's brows were knitted together. "If he dodged it then, he's more than capable of doing it now."
      The castle shook again, and both Crow and Saedyn staggered back toward the wall.
      Magic crackled as the whip ruthlessly bit into Saedyn's shield. If this kept up, Saedyn would use up all of his magic. That would lead to a burnout. And a burnout could be fatal. But Saedyn's eyes blazed with determination as he continued to hold the shield in place.
      There wasn't much Crow could do, but he had to go with the best of all the bad ideas. Raising a shaking hand, Crow shot a blast of void magic at the pulsing silver shield. The moment his magic touched the surface, both magics vanished as they canceled each other out.
      "What are you doing?" Saedyn asked as all the remaining color drained from his face. Then Saedyn screamed in warning as the whip flashed through the air.
      Crow made to whirl around, but it was too late. His back was on fire as the king's whip lashed him. Crow's vision swam, and red spots blossomed as he collapsed to his knees.
      "Move out of the way, Wielder of Void," the king said lazily. "I still have use for you."
      Crow shook his head as he fought through the pain. He lifted a shaking hand and sent a blast of void magic at the king.
      The king brushed the magic away as if it were nothing more than a gust of wind. "It seems like we're going to have to do this the hard way-" the king suddenly trailed off as a clucking noise sounded through the staircase.
      Gloria. Crow's head was spinning too much to think straight. He watched in shock as the chicken flapped up the stairs, clucking angrily at the king.
      Disbelief fell across the king's face as he stared at Gloria.
      Silver light and darkness exploded as Saedyn and Crow blasted the king with their magic at the same time. Gloria's unforeseen distraction had worked in their favor.
      When the light cleared, the king staggered and collapsed to his knees. His metallic feathered wings were ruined, and his skin was covered in angry welts. And then with a rush of wings as he leaped out the window and disappeared into the sky beyond.
      "Do you think he'll be back?" Crow whispered after a long moment.
      Saedyn frowned faintly. "His strength has decreased significantly. I don't know."
      Brown-speckled feathers came in and out of focus as Gloria brushed her soft head against Crow's hand. "Gloria," Crow said softly, "I thought I told you to stay in the hallway."
      Gloria clucked as if to say, And if I did, where would you be now?
      Crow smiled weakly. Silver light flared faintly as Saedyn made to heal Crow's wound.
      "Wait." Crow turned painfully to look up at Saedyn. "You shouldn't-you're already low on strength."
      "But you're hurt. I can't just leave you like this! Oh, Gloria, where are you going?"
      "Gloria?" Crow's vision swam again.
      Hurried footsteps sounded on the stairs from somewhere far away. Lyria and Gwenevieve appeared around the corner a moment later, with Gloria leading the way in front of them.
      "What happened here?" Gwenevieve asked weakly.
      "The king of the day angels-" Saedyn explained quickly. But whatever he said next was lost as Crow blacked out.
      
~

	When Crow came to, the pain had vanished. His back was sore, but that was about it.
	Crow blinked to find Saedyn, Lyria, and Gwenevieve staring down at him. "How long was I out?" Crow asked in a rising panic.
	"Only about five minutes," Saedyn reassured him.
	"The king has the weapon," Crow blurted out as he suddenly remembered.
	Gwenevieve's eyes widened. "The weapon?"
	Crow nodded.
	"Can you stand? We need to find the king."
	Saedyn helped Crow to his feet, and the four of them took off down the stairs. "As I said earlier, the king was injured badly," the white-haired boy informed Gwenevieve and Lyria. "It's very likely that he's still somewhere in the castle."
      Lyria was carrying Gloria in her arms, and the chicken clucked softly as they ran. "It looks like all the fighting moved outside," the curly-haired girl observed. It was true; the hallways were empty and covered in piles of rubble.
      Just then, a rumbling began to shake the air. The disturbance was back. Crow quickened his pace. "It's coming from the throne room!"
      Turning the corner, they nearly crashed headfirst into a group of people running in the same direction. After skidding to a stop, Crow looked up to find Halimah, Ewen, Thuc, Lianna, Favian, Rania, Fern, Maliq, and Professor Lethco.
      "Saedyn!" Halimah exclaimed. "You're okay!"
      Thuc and Lianna rushed over to embrace their son tightly.
      "The king has the weapon," Lyria told the others worriedly. "We think he's in the throne room right now."
      Rania nodded grimly. "We came to that conclusion as well."
      "We need to hurry," Fern said as she took off at a run, and the others followed close behind.
      "Where's the queen of the night angels?" Halimah asked suddenly. "She has the power to stop the weapon!"
      "She led a group to the mines," Favian said. "She suspected the king might be there, but she's not the only one with the power to stop his weapon. The power of the four gods can too. After all, it was how we stopped the king the first time."
      They reached the throne room in no time and burst through the doors. Crow nearly stumbled as powerful winds hit him square in the face. The once elegant room was a wreck. Pillars had collapsed, and piles of rock lay scattered over the cracked floor.
      The king of the day angels stood in the middle of the room, his tattered wings dragging on the ground behind him. His hands were raised above his head, and the Flames of Ice orb pulsed in his fingers. Icy light and wind were spilling from the orb, and the king's long silver-blue hair was blowing in every direction as he stood in the center of the storm.
      There were cries from the sky outside as day angels and night angels alike fled from the growing tempest.
      "Stop!" Lyria cried desperately. "You'll kill your day angels as well!"
      "Silence, girl!" the king whirled in a crazed sort of way.
      "You'll kill yourself as well!" Maliq yelled.
      The rage vanished from the king's face as it was replaced by a deadly calm. "As long as I take everyone down with me, so what if I fall?"
      Fern sent a blast of fire at the king, but the howling winds whisked it away.
      "Goodbye," the king said with a smile. His navy eyes glinted. "It's truly a shame things had to go this way."
      An explosion of icy light engulfed the room, and everything faded to white.

    Chapter Thirty-Seven

	"Take my hand!" Thuc extended his hands.
	Halimah quickly took the former flame god's in one hand and Gwenevieve's in the other. The moment the four gods were connected in a circle, a surge of magic thrummed through Halimah.
	"Follow my lead," Gwenevieve instructed as a glowing golden light began to form between them.
	"What are you doing?" the king demanded. His figure was barely visible through the light, and yet his tone turned panicked when he seemed to realize what was happening. "Stop, stop! I command you to stop!"
	"Get ready." Gwenevieve's voice rang.
	Suddenly the wind was roaring so loudly that Halimah's eardrums began to rattle. Then there was an explosion of ice-blue light as the king hurled the full force of the weapon at them.
	Golden light shot into the air like a pillar before spreading out to fully engulf the ice. Halimah felt Thuc and Gwenevieve's hands tighten around hers as they braced for the impact. The force of the blast seemed to shake Halimah's very bones as the ice crashed into their shield of light. And for a long moment after, all she could see was gold.
	Halimah clung tightly to the hands of her fellow gods as they stood their ground. She squinted against the brightness, and all the while the roaring was growing louder and louder and louder.
	Then everything went silent, and the light cleared to reveal the king of the day angels gaping at the four of them in shock. The Flames of Ice orb lay in pieces on the ground at his feet, and its blue glow faded as it died out.
	Halimah staggered back as Thuc and Gwenevieve let go of her hands. Ewen was there in an instant to help her balance. Halimah looked around at the others.
