	Lyria, Maliq, and Fern had identical expressions of shock on their faces. Rania's mouth had fallen open in awe, and Lianna was standing in front of Crow and Saedyn, still shielding the two boys with her body.
	"What have you done?" The king's eyes narrowed in rage, and the muscles in his jaw worked furiously.
	"We stopped your weapon." Gwenevieve's voice rang through the deafening silence. "It's over."
	The king of the day angels dropped to his knees.
	"We should block the exits so he can't escape," Thuc suggested.
	Seeing that the gods were exhausted, Rania, Lyria, Saedyn, and Fern hurried over to stand in front of the large arches leading to the open sky beyond. Eyeing his every move, the four of them formed a loose circle around the king. Maliq walked over to block the throne room's doors and folded his arms over his chest.
	"What are you going to do with me?" the king hissed, trying and failing to rise to his feet.
	"I don't think that should be for us to decide," Lianna spoke up as she glided over to stand beside Halimah and the other gods. "The day angels and night angels should be the ones to decide your fate."
	"The queen should be back soon," Thuc added. "I'm sure she'll be more than happy to put you in your place."
	"Life isn't fair," the king spat bitterly. "It isn't kind. No, it's a cruel journey of pain and misery and anger. Happiness is just an illusion. There's only power. That's what's real."
	"You're wrong." Halimah's voice was braver than she felt as the king turned his attention to her. "Happiness isn't just an illusion. You've just never found it, Your Majesty."
	"You know nothing, girl," the king said softly.
	Halimah refused to back down from his gaze. "I may not have been alive nearly as long as you have, but I've found happiness. I've found friends who have walked with me through the dark until I could finally see the light again."
	The king's navy eyes glinted. "I was going to exterminate the night angels once and for all. They robbed me of my happiness. And in turn, I would be the most powerful ruler of them all. Everyone would bow before me."
	"Power doesn't equal happiness, Your Majesty."
	The king glared at her before suddenly collapsing on the ground.
      "Leave him," Gwenevieve told the others with a frown. "It is up to him if he wants to get back up or not."
      Ewen looked skeptical. "I wouldn't trust him not to try anything."
      But the moment the words left his mouth, there was a blur of metallic silver too fast for the human eye to keep up with. The king of the day angels materialized directly behind Saedyn on the other side of the throne room, and his navy eyes glinted. Before Halimah could even let out a scream, the king had clawed his bare hands into Saedyn's chest.
      The king's smile was a horrible one. "It seems like you aren't the only ones who can act."

    Chapter Thirty-Eight

	Crow's mouth was open in a scream, but no sound was coming out.
      Saedyn's amber eyes met Crow's as he hit the floor at the king's feet. His blood stained the white tiles crimson as it steadily pooled beneath him.
      I, the white-haired boy mouthed as he choked on his own blood. But before he could finish, his eyes turned glassy and unseeing.
      The king of the day angels was laughing hysterically, but all Crow could hear was a dull ringing in his ears. Then he was screaming. All the light faded from the room as Crow's void magic roared to life.
      "Crow," someone's voice reached him. He couldn't tell who was calling him. Everything was muffled.
      "Stay back!" Crow panted as his magic swirled around him.
      "Wielder of Void." The king of the day angels just sneered at him. His hands dripped with blood, and his robes were splattered with red. "That's right, Crow. Kill me. The two of us are more alike than you think. My death will be your awakening. You'll complete what I couldn't."
      No, a soft voice at the back of Crow's mind said. No, it said a little louder this time. "No," Crow whispered. Slowly, the light returned in a flood.
      "No?" Shock flickered over the king's face for a split second before it was replaced with an amused smile.
      "No," Crow said firmly even as tears slid down the sides of his face. "I won't kill you. I've figured out your secret, Your Majesty. You enjoy torturing and breaking others because it makes you feel better about yourself. You wanted to become king because you wanted people to respect you. And maybe you could have been if you had a little kindness."
      "Nonsense." The king shook his head. But there was something flickering behind his eyes.
      "I've learned what it's like to not be alone," Crow said quietly. "What you've done is unforgivable. Even so, I'm sorry no one ever showed you the way back to the light. I refuse to become you. And that is why I can't kill you."
      The king of the day angels just stared at Crow. But Crow's vision was still blurred too much for him to notice the dagger in the king's hand before it was too late. Someone was screaming behind him as the king hurled the blade through the air.
      Crow watched the dagger spiral through the air in slow motion. The surface of the blade glinted in the dying light.
      Before Crow could fully register what was happening, there was a rush of silver wings as a dark-haired figure plucked the dagger out of the air before landing behind the king. Even from where Crow was standing, he could hear the words Cora whispered. "Crow might not kill you, but I can."
      Cora shoved the dagger into the king's chest. The king's expression was frozen in shock as Cora twisted the blade deeper. "This is for my brother." Cora yanked out the blade, and the king of the day angels collapsed to the floor, coughing as blood trickled from his mouth. Cora grimly took a step backward.
      The life faded from the king's eyes, and his stare became blank and unseeing.
      Without a second glance at the king, Crow ran over to Saedyn's lifeless body. He dropped to his knees. Crow's vision swam as fresh tears threatened, and he placed a trembling finger on Saedyn's wrist. There was no pulse.
      Unable to look into Saedyn's unseeing eyes any longer, Crow closed them with a shaking hand.
      "He's not dead," a voice said softly.
      Crow turned slowly to find Professor Lethco solemnly walking toward him. "Not dead?" Crow repeated. His voice was a broken sound.
      "Well, he's not completely dead yet," the cat amended softly. "I used my magic to freeze him in time. You can still save him."
      "How?" Crow croaked.
      "Your void magic. Only you can heal him."
      Crow gently placed both hands on the white-haired boy's chest-directly over his heart. The blood warmed Crow's hands as he summoned his void magic to him. The lazy tendrils spiral into the air as he closed his eyes and slipped into the dark.
      After what felt like an eternity, Crow opened his eyes. Saedyn's unbound white hair was splattered with red, but even though the blood remained, the wound on his chest had healed.
      "Crow." Saedyn smiled weakly.
      Crow smiled back as he blinked away the stinging in his eyes.
      Suddenly Thuc and Lianna were there as they swept both Crow and Saedyn into a tight embrace. Then Halimah and Ewen joined as well, followed closely by Lyria, Maliq, Fern, Gwenevieve, Rania, Favian, and Professor Lethco.
      The booming of wings sounded as the queen of the night angels swept into the wrecked throne room. Her eyes instantly fell on the king's lifeless body.
      Everyone turned to watch as Cora stepped forward and dropped into a deep bow at the queen's feet. "Your Majesty."
      The queen looked down at Cora. "You killed him."
      "I had to."
      "I was prepared to battle him to the death." The queen smiled faintly as she motioned for Cora to stand. "But it looks like you got there first."
      As Cora rose to her feet, she seemed to remember that she was still gripping the blade she had used to kill the king. The blade clattered to the floor a moment later with a sound that echoed through the silent throne room. "He murdered my brother," Cora spoke at last. "I wanted to kill him ever since that fateful day. So why? Why am I shaking?" She stared hopelessly at the queen for an answer.
      Sey landed next to the queen in a rush of violet feathers. "Taking a life isn't easy. In fact, it shouldn't be easy." The night angel offered Cora a small smile before turning to address the queen. "On a different note, every last night angel has been freed from the mines. The rest of our night angels are chasing down the remaining guards as you commanded."
      "I'll go talk with those day angels later," the queen said with a sigh. "Please, let me help teleport you all back to the ground."
      Halimah took a step forward. "Ewen and I have somewhere to go first. We'll meet up with the rest of you later."
      The queen of the night angels nodded as she raised her hands. "Then I wish you the best of luck."
      Crow took one last look at the ruined throne room before everything vanished in a flash of golden light.

    Chapter Thirty-Nine

	"I can't believe it." Navi was still in shock as she slumped down against the doorframe to their headquarters. "The king is dead!"
	"We've succeeded." Nihira patted her sister on the shoulder. The twins were covered head to toe in cuts and bruises, but their spirits couldn't have been brighter.
	Ewen looked up at the tower-like building with wide eyes. "This is the headquarters to the rebellion?"
	Halimah nodded. She had been filling Ewen in about everything that had happened during the past week as they followed the sisters down the empty streets. The night angel army had just departed, and the day angels were still keeping a close eye on the king's guards.
	The two of them followed Navi and Nihira through the door and into the building. They walked in silence up the spiraling staircase until they reached the hidden door built into the stone wall.
	Eve was sitting on the couch with the two other male night angels from before. The moment she saw them enter, the night angel rose to her feet. "We heard noises outside." Eve's voice was no more than a whisper. "Explosions and the clashing of blades."
	Navi hurried over to take Eve's hands in her own. "We won," she said breathlessly. "The king of the day angels is dead."
	"Dead?" Eve's eyes widened as she stared at Navi.
      Halimah smiled at the night angel. "His reign is over."
      Eve's eyes filled with tears as Navi squeezed her scarred hands comfortingly.
      Both of the males on the couch had identical looks of shock on their faces. They shared a look before turning back to the others. "Thank you," the male on the right whispered. His voice was hoarse from years of unuse.
      Navi and Nihira just smiled radiantly.
      
~

	Halimah and Ewen returned to the Temple of Fire an hour later to meet up with the others. Halimah turned to look around the entrance hall. Crow and Saedyn were sitting on the floor next to the staircase with Thuc and Lianna, and the four of them were talking in quiet voices. Gloria was fast asleep in Crow's lap-the chicken was just as exhausted as everyone else.
	On the other side of the stairs, Gwenevieve, Rania, and Favian were helping each other heal their many cuts and scratches. Lyria, Maliq, and Fern stood nearby. All of them looked as if they had seen better days, but they were smiling among themselves.
      There was a patter of light steps, and then something furry leaped up to perch on her shoulder. "Halimah, Ewen," Professor Lethco said with a flick of his tail, "welcome back."
	Halimah and Ewen stayed the night at the Temple of Fire. When morning arrived, they ate in the dining hall as usual. All of the former gods were going to depart today to their designated temples. They decided the previous night that the best thing to do would be to inform the citizens of Hali about the fall of the king and the fighting that had taken place at the castle.
      After they finished saying their farewells to everyone at the temple, Ewen offered his hand to Halimah. "Are you ready to go home?"
      Halimah looked up at the green-haired boy to find his eyes sparkling. She smiled as she laced her fingers through his. Ewen smiled back. Then the world faded in a flash of green light as the two of them were transported back to the Firefly District. The moment the light faded, a strong blast of salt-tinged wind hit Halimah in the face. Laughing, Halimah brushed her hair out of her eyes as she squinted against the bright sunlight. The Temple of Life was just up ahead.

    Chapter Forty
One Month Later

      Crow walked down the familiar streets of Hali Central with Saedyn. A lot had happened during the past month. For one thing, the night angels and day angels had agreed to overcome their differences and start over as one united people.
      Crow couldn't help but smile as he led Saedyn up the stairs to his apartment. True to his word, Crow was determined to attend school, and Professor Lethco had helped him register at the academy he taught at in the Firefly District. To Crow's surprise, Saedyn decided to join the academy as well. The white-haired boy had never been to a proper school before and claimed that it would be a good learning opportunity.
	Right now the two of them were in Hali Central to collect Crow's belongings from his apartment. The new school semester was scheduled to start in a week, and they would be moving into on-campus dormitories for the next few years.
	Crow's apartment was exactly the way he had left it all of those months ago. Crow walked over to the large window at the back of the living room and drew open the curtains. Sunlight spilled in through the glass and washed away the shadows as it cut through the dusty air.
	"If you had the choice to redo your life as a normal magic wielder," Saedyn asked softly, "would you take it?"
	"No." Crow didn't need to think about his answer. "My void magic . . . It's been a long struggle, but I'm thankful. The void magic was never a curse like I initially thought."
	Saedyn's amber eyes sparkled with understanding as he nodded. "I'm glad."
	
~

	Crow was sitting on the floor of his dormitory room as he excitedly pulled on his shoes. Today was going to be his first day of school.
	He was sharing a room with Saedyn, and the white-haired boy was standing in front of the mirror on the door of the dresser, looking at his reflection in the glass. Both of them were dressed in the uniform of Firefly District's magic academy.
	Saedyn's eyes caught Crow's in the glass and the two of them shared a smile.
	Gloria clucked softly as she hopped over to brush up against Crow's ankles. She clucked once in a way that said, If you don't go now, you'll be late for class.
	"Ready?" Saedyn asked as the two of them made their way over to the door.
      Crow grinned. "Ready."
      And together, the two of them stepped through the doorway and out into the sunlit hallway beyond.
    

    Epilogue

	Professor Lethco walked along the sandy beach next to the Temple of Life. The night was silent, and the inky sky was full of twinkling lights. He tilted his head upward to watch the colors swirling among the stars. The two moons of Hali hung in the air like pearly orbs.
	The cat stopped and turned to look over his shoulder at the trail of pawprints he had left behind in the powdery sand. It was time to head back, so the professor turned and made his way toward the golden fields of grass. The sky was slowly lighten. Then stopping in the middle of the swaying field, Professor Lethco raised his head to watch the sun rise over Hali.
